فصل في الأحكام بيان أقسام حقوق الله وحقوق دائرة بينهما، أي بين العبادة والعقوبة كالكفارات فإن فيها معنى العبادة من حيث إنها تؤدى بالصوم والإعتاق والإطعام والكسوة، ومعنى العقوبة من حيث إنها لم تجب ابتداء، بل وجبت أجزية على أفعال محرّمة صدرت عن العباد. وعبادة فيها معنى المؤنة أي المحنة والثقل كصدقة الفطر، فإنها في أصلها عبادة ملحقة بالزكاة، ولهذا شرط لها الإغناء، ولكن فيها معنى المؤنة، ولهذا تجب عمّن يمونه وينفق أي للحوقها بالزكاة عليه كنفسه وأولاده الصغار وعبيده المملوكين، فإنه لما مَأَنهم بالنفقة والولاية وجب أن يمونهم بالصدقة أيضًا لدفع البلاء. ومؤنة فيها معنى العبادة كالعشر، فإنه في نفسه مؤنة للأرض التي يزرعها، ولو لم يعط العشر للسلطان لاسترد الأرض منه، وأحالها بيد آخر، ولكن فيها معنى العبادة، وهو أنه يصرف مصارف الزكاة، ولا يجب إلا على المسلم، فحمل فعلهم المزارعة على كسب الحلال الطيب. = مورثه عمدا أو خطأ لا يحرم عن الميراث عندنا خلافًا للشافعي له، وقال في 'الهداية': إن حرمان الميراث عقوبة، والصبي ليس من أهل العقوبة. (القمر) كالكفارات: إنما سميت كفارات لأنها تستر الذنوب والكفر الستر. (القمر) لم تجب ابتداء: كما تحب العبادات ابتداءً. (القمر) بل وجبت أجزية إلخ كما أن العقوبات تحب أجزية على أفعاله.(القمر) معنى المؤنة قيل: إن المؤنة ما يجب على رجل بسبب الغير وهو رأس الغير، أو بما يحتاج إليه ذلك الغير للبقاء كالنفقة، فإنها ثقيلة على المؤدّي. (القمر) عبادة ولذا سميت عبادة فيها مؤنة لا مؤنة فيها معنى عبادة (القمر) معنى المؤنة: فإنه يجب على الإنسان بسبب رأس الغير. (القمر) مؤنة: أي على المعطي بسبب الأرض النامية . (القمر) مصارف الزكاة فإنه زكاة الخارج. (القمر) ولا يجب إلخ : أي ابتداءً وأجاز محمد لله بقاءه على الكافر بأنه إذا ملك الذمي أرضًا عشرية لمسلم تبقى عشرية كما كانت عنده، ولا يوضع على أرض الكافر العشر في ابتداء وضع الوظيفة؛ لأن فيه معنى القربة، والكافر ليس بأهل كذا للقربة بوجه في 'التحقيق'. (القمر) فحمل إلخ جواب سؤال مقدر تقديره أنكم قلتم: إن العشر فيها معنى العبادة، والواقع خلاف ذلك، فإن العشر يحصل من الزراعة والزراعة تكون سببًا لترك الصلاة وغيرها من المأمورات الشرعية كما نرى الزارعين عموما على ذلك، فأجاب بهذا القول بأن المراد ههنا من المزارعة التي يحصل العشر بها: التي لا تكون سببًا للمعصية بل خالية عنها، ولا شك في كونها كسباً حلالاً طيبا. (السنبلي) مي فصل في الأحكام ١١١ بيان أقسام حقوق الله ومؤنة فيها معنى العقوبة كالخراج، فإنه في نفسه مؤنة للأرض التي يزرعها، وإلا استردّها وأحالها بيد آخر، ولكن فيه معنى العقوبة من حيث إنه يجب على الكفار السلطان منه الذين اشتغلوا بزراعة الدنيا ونبذوا الآخرة وراء ظهورهم. ابتداء وحق قائم بنفسه، أي ثابت بذاته من غير أن يتعلّق بذمة العبد شيء منه حتى يجب عليه أداؤه، بل استبقاه الله تعالى لأجل نفسه وتولّى أخذه وقسمته من كان خليفته في الأرض، أي جعله وليا وهو السلطان كخمس الغنائم والمعادن، فإن الجهاد حق الله، فينبغي أن يكون المصاب به وهو الغنيمة كلها الله تعالى، لكن أوجب أربعة أخماسه للغانمين منّةً منه عليهم، وأبقى الخمس وكذا المعادن، فإنها اسم لما خلقه الله في الأرض من الذهب والفضة، فينبغي أن يكون لنفسه، كله لله تعالى، ولكن الله تعالى أحلّ للواجد أو للمالك أربعة أخماسه منّةً منه وفضلاً. وحقوق العباد كبدل المتلفات والمغصوبات وغيرهما من الدية وملك المبيع والثمن وملك النكاح ونحوه. كالطلاق أي من مال الغير أي الواجبة على القاتل مؤنة للأرض إلخ أي على المعطى بسبب الاشتغال بالزراعة مع الإعراض عن الإسلام حين فتح الإمام تلك البلدة وعرض عليه الإسلام. (القمر) يجب أي ابتداء، وأجاز محمد الله بقاء الخراج على المسلم إذا اشترى المسلم من كافر أرض خراج (القمر) على الكفار لا على المسلم فإن العزة للمسلمين، فلا لياقة لهم للعقوبة، فلو فتح الإمام بلدة وأسلم أهلها طوعًا أو قسمت الأرض بين المسلمين لا يُوضع الخراج على أراضيهم، كذا في 'التحقيق'. (القمر) نبذوا في القاموس النبذ طرحك الشيء أمامك أو ورائك. (القمر) قائم بنفسه: أي ليس فيه جهة العبادة ولا جهة العقوبة، ولا جهة المؤنة. (القمر) أي ثابت إلخ إيماء إلى أن الحق ههنا بمعنى الثابت. (القمر) منه أي من ذلك الحق القائم بنفسه.(القمر) أداؤه : أي بطريق الطاعة، فأداء الحق القائم بنفسه ليس طاعة منا بل تقسيمه بين الفقراء نيابة من الله تعالى. (القمر) الغنائم والمعادن الغنيمة ما نيل عن أهل الشرك عنوةً والحرب قائم كذا قال العلوي في حاشية 'شرق الوقاية'، والمعدن ما كان مخلوقا في الأرض كالذهب والفضة والحديد والصفر. (القمر) حق الله: لأنه لإعزاز دينه وإعلاء كلمته . (القمر) وأبقى الخمس إلخ وجعل له مصارف (القمر) للواجد : أي الذي وجد المعادن في غير ملكه. (القمر)
Chapter on rulings: Explanation of the categories of the rights of Allah and rights that are between them, i.e., between worship and punishment, like expiations (kaffarat), for they contain the meaning of worship in that they are performed by fasting, freeing slaves, feeding, and clothing, and the meaning of punishment in that they were not obligatory initially, but became obligatory as recompense for forbidden actions committed by servants. And worship that contains the meaning of burden (mu'na), i.e., hardship and weight, like charity of breaking the fast (sadaqat al-fitr), for in its origin it is worship attached to zakat, and for this reason the condition of sufficiency is stipulated for it, but it contains the meaning of burden, and for this reason it is obligatory upon one who supports and spends on others, i.e., due to its attachment to zakat upon him, like himself, his minor children, and his owned slaves, for since he supports them with maintenance and guardianship, it became necessary that he support them with charity as well to repel affliction. And a burden that contains the meaning of worship, like the tithe ('ushr), for it is in itself a burden upon the land that he cultivates, and if he does not give the tithe to the ruler, he would take the land from him and give it to another, but it contains the meaning of worship, namely that it is spent on the categories of zakat, and it is obligatory only upon a Muslim, so they interpreted their cultivation as earning pure lawful sustenance. = One who kills his bequeather intentionally or unintentionally is not deprived of inheritance according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, and he said in al-Hidayah: 'Deprivation of inheritance is a punishment, and a child is not liable to punishment.' (al-Qamar) 'kaffarat': they are called kaffarat because they conceal sins, and kufr means concealment. (al-Qamar) 'did not become obligatory initially': as acts of worship become obligatory initially. (al-Qamar) 'but became obligatory as recompense etc.': just as punishments become obligatory as recompense for his actions. (al-Qamar) 'meaning of mu'na': it is said that mu'na is that which is obligatory upon a man due to another, and it is the head of the other, or what that other needs for survival, like maintenance, for it is heavy upon the payer. (al-Qamar) 'worship': therefore it is called worship that contains mu'na, not mu'na that contains the meaning of worship. (al-Qamar) 'meaning of mu'na': that it becomes obligatory upon a person due to the head of the other. (al-Qamar) 'mu'na': i.e., upon the giver due to the productive land. (al-Qamar) 'categories of zakat': for it is the zakat of produce. (al-Qamar) 'and it is not obligatory etc.': i.e., initially, and Muhammad permitted its remaining upon the disbeliever, that if a dhimmi owns a 'ushri land from a Muslim, it remains 'ushri as it was with him, and the tithe is not placed upon the land of the disbeliever initially in the imposition of the function, because it contains the meaning of devotion, and the disbeliever is not qualified for devotion in any way, as in al-Tahqiq. (al-Qamar) 'so they interpreted' etc.: a response to an implied question, which is: you said that the tithe contains the meaning of worship, but the reality is otherwise, for the tithe comes from agriculture, and agriculture causes neglect of prayer and other legal obligations, as we see farmers generally doing that. So he answered with this statement that what is meant here by agriculture from which the tithe is obtained is that which is not a cause of sin, but is free of it, and there is no doubt that it is pure lawful earning. (al-Sanbali) Mi. Chapter on rulings 111: Explanation of the categories of the rights of Allah and a burden that contains the meaning of punishment, like the land tax (kharaj), for it is in itself a burden upon the land that he cultivates, otherwise he would take it back and give it to another, but it contains the meaning of punishment in that it is obligatory upon the disbelievers, the ruler from among them who engaged in cultivation of the world and cast the Hereafter behind their backs. Initially. And a right that stands by itself (haqq qa'im bi nafsihi), i.e., established in its essence without any part of it being attached to the liability of the servant such that its fulfillment becomes obligatory upon him, rather Allah preserved it for His own sake and undertook its collection and distribution by whoever is His vicegerent on earth, i.e., He made him a guardian, and he is the ruler, like the khums of spoils and minerals, for jihad is a right of Allah, so it should be that what is obtained, i.e., the spoils, is entirely for Allah, but He made four-fifths obligatory for the fighters as a favor from Him, and retained the fifth, and similarly minerals, for they are a name for what Allah created in the earth of gold and silver, so it should be for Himself, all of it is for Allah, but Allah permitted for the finder or the owner four-fifths of it as a favor and bounty. And the rights of servants like compensation for destroyed and usurped property and others, such as blood money, ownership of the sold item and the price, ownership of marriage, and the like, like divorce, i.e., from the property of another, i.e., obligatory upon the killer. 'Burden upon the land' etc.: i.e., upon the giver due to engagement in agriculture while turning away from Islam when the Imam opened that town and presented Islam to them. (al-Qamar) 'it is obligatory': i.e., initially, and Muhammad permitted the remaining of kharaj upon a Muslim if a Muslim buys kharaj land from a disbeliever. (al-Qamar) 'upon the disbelievers, not upon the Muslim': for honor belongs to Muslims, and they are not fit for punishment, so if the Imam opens a town and its inhabitants embrace Islam willingly, or the land is divided among Muslims, kharaj is not placed on their lands, as stated in al-Tahqiq. (al-Qamar) 'they cast': in al-Qamus, 'al-nabd' is throwing something in front of you or behind you. (al-Qamar) 'qa'im bi nafsihi': i.e., it has no aspect of worship, nor aspect of punishment, nor aspect of burden. (al-Qamar) 'i.e., established' etc.: indicating that 'haqq' here means established. (al-Qamar) 'minhu': i.e., from that right that stands by itself. (al-Qamar) 'its fulfillment': i.e., by way of obedience, so fulfilling the right that stands by itself is not an act of obedience from us, but rather its distribution among the poor as deputyship from Allah. (al-Qamar) 'spoils and minerals': spoils are what is taken from the people of shirk by force while the war is ongoing, as said by al-Alawi in the gloss of Sharh al-Wiqaya, and minerals are what is created in the earth like gold, silver, iron, and brass. (al-Qamar) 'right of Allah': because it is for the exaltation of His religion and the elevation of His word. (al-Qamar) 'and retained the fifth' etc.: and He made for it recipients. (al-Qamar) 'for the finder': i.e., he who finds minerals in other than his own property. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is from a Hanafi usul work (Noor al-Anwar) with commentary by al-Qamar and others. It opens with a classification of rights (huquq). The author divides the rights of Allah into categories based on the presence of elements of worship (ibada), punishment (uquba), and burden/expense (mu'na). Some rights are purely worship (e.g., obligatory prayers), purely punishment (e.g., hadd penalties), or mixed (e.g., expiations - kafarat - which combine worship through fasting/feeding and punishment as recompense for sins). The text then introduces subcategories: an act of worship that also carries a burden (like sadaqat al-fitr, which is an act of worship but is also heavy on the giver as it is required for dependents), and a burden that also has an element of worship (like the tithe 'ushr, which is a burden on land but its proceeds are spent like zakat and only required from Muslims, giving it a devotional aspect). This classification helps understand the legal nature of these obligations. The passage then digresses to a specific fiqh ruling: a child who kills his parent (intentionally or accidentally) is not deprived of inheritance according to the Hanafi school, contrary to al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi proof, cited from al-Hidayah, is that deprivation is a punishment, and a child is not subject to punishment. The remainder of the commentary explains key terms such as 'mu'na' (defined as an obligation due to another person or property) and addresses potential objections, e.g., that agriculture leading to 'ushr might be sinful, but the response clarifies that the 'ushr here is from lawful cultivation. On page 112, the classification continues with a burden containing the meaning of punishment (like kharaj, the land tax on non-Muslims, which is a burden but also penal). Finally, a third category is introduced: a right that stands by itself (haqq qa'im bi nafsihi), which has no aspect of worship, punishment, or burden. Examples are khums (one-fifth of spoils) and minerals (gold, silver, etc.), which are inherently Allah's property, but He allows four-fifths to the fighters or finders as a favor. These rights are collected and distributed by the ruler as Allah's deputy. The passage concludes by contrasting with rights of servants (e.g., compensation for damage, blood money, sale contracts, marriage) which are based on private claims.

Key Terms
مؤنة (mu'na): An obligatory payment or burden due to another person or property; hardship or expense.
حق قائم بنفسه (haqq qa'im bi nafsihi): A right that stands by itself, without attachment to a servant's liability, and is collected and distributed by the ruler as Allah's deputy.
عبادة (ibada): Act of worship or devotion, implying spiritual benefit and nearness to Allah.
عقوبة (uquba): Punishment or penalty, usually for disobedience.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in this passage, what is the category of 'ushr (tithe)?
A) A right of Allah that is pure worship
B) A right of Allah that is pure punishment
C) A burden (mu'na) that contains an element of worship
D) A right that stands by itself (haqq qa'im bi nafsihi)

Key Takeaway
The classification of rights of Allah into categories based on ibada, uquba, and mu'na is essential for understanding the legal nature and conditions of various obligations in Hanafi fiqh.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
6 min
Original and Substitute Rights in Hanafi Usul
Definition of original and substitute rights with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to APPLY the Hanafi concept of asl and khalaf to classify legal rights and identify substitute relations in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Every right has an original; when impossible, a substitute steps in – but never a substitute for a substitute.

This passage from Noorul Anwar introduces a foundational usul concept: legal rights are divided into an original (asl) and a substitute (khalaf) that replaces the original when it cannot be fulfilled. This principle appears across many fiqh chapters, from purification to inheritance. Understanding asl and khalaf helps you see how Hanafi scholars maintain legal consistency while accommodating practical limitations.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish Haqq Allah from Haqq al-‘Abd
Identify the two main categories of rights: those belonging to Allah (e.g., kharaj, khums) and those belonging to servants (e.g., compensation, ownership). Note that some rights of Allah carry a punitive element.
Rights of Allah are often managed by the ruler as vicegerent.
2
Identify the Original (Asl) of a Right
For each right, determine its complete or original form. Example: Faith's original is inner attestation (tasdiq) together with oral confession (iqrar).
The original is the fullest expression of the obligation.
3
Identify the Substitute (Khalaf)
Find the substitute that stands in when the original is impossible. Example: Oral confession alone becomes a substitute for the full faith regarding worldly rulings.
The substitute must serve the same purpose and be of the same genus.
4
Avoid the Error of Chained Substitutes
The text warns against making one substitute a substitute of another. Each substitute is directly for the original, not for another substitute. Example: Parent's faith and adherence to dar al-Islam are both direct substitutes for a minor's own faith, not a chain.
This preserves the logical structure of substitution.
5
Recognize Dependency, Not Substitution Chain
Some substitutes may be dependent on another condition (e.g., adherence to dar al-Islam depends on loss of parental adherence), but this is not a chain of substitutes. Learn to apply the concept without creating a cascade.
Analogy: In inheritance, the son is a substitute for the father; the grandson is a substitute for the son, not directly for the father.

فصل في الأحكام
بيان أقسام حقوق الله ومؤنة فيها معنى العقوبة كالخراج، فإنه في نفسه مؤنة للأرض التي يزرعها، وإلا استردّها وأحالها بيد آخر، ولكن فيه معنى العقوبة من حيث إنه يجب على الكفار الذين اشتغلوا بزراعة الدنيا ونبذوا الآخرة وراء ظهورهم.
ابتداء
وحق قائم بنفسه، أي ثابت بذاته من غير أن يتعلّق بذمة العبد شيء منه حتى يجب عليه أداؤه، بل استبقاه الله تعالى لأجل نفسه وتولّى أخذه وقسمته من كان خليفته في الأرض، وهو السلطان كخمس الغنائم والمعادن، فإن الجهاد حق الله، فينبغي أن يكون المصاب به وهو الغنيمة كلها الله تعالى، لكن أوجب أربعة أخماسه للغانمين منّةً منه عليهم، وأبقى الخمس وكذا المعادن، فإنها اسم لما خلقه الله في الأرض من الذهب والفضة، فينبغي أن يكون كله لله تعالى، ولكن الله تعالى أحلّ للواجد أو للمالك أربعة أخماسه منّةً منه وفضلاً. وحقوق العباد كبدل المتلفات والمغصوبات وغيرهما من الدية وملك المبيع والثمن وملك النكاح ونحوه.
وهذه الحقوق، أي جنسها سواء كان حقا الله أو للعبد تنقسم إلى أصل وخلف يقوم مقام الأصل عند التعذر، فالإيمان أصله التصديق والإقرار جميعا عند الله تعالى، ثم صار الإقرار وحده أصلاً مستبدًا خلفًا عن التصديق في حق أحكام الدنيا بأن يقوم الإقرار مقامه في حق ترتب أحكامه كما في المكره على الإسلام أجري الإقرار مقام مجموع التصديق والإقرار وإن عدم التصديق منه، ثم صار أداء أحد الأبوين في حق الصغير خلفا عن أداء الصغير الإيمان حتى يُجعل مسلما بإسلام أحد الأبوين، ويجري عليه أحكامه بالميراث وصلاة الجنازة ونحوها، ثم صارت تبعية أهل الدار خلفا عن تبعية الأبوين في إثبات الإسلام في الصبي الذي سباه أهل الإسلام، وأخرجوه إلى دارهم يُحكم عليه بالإسلام في الصلاة عليه بحكم التبعية، وليس هذا أن تبعية أهل الدار خلف عن أداء أحد الأبوين وأداء أحد الأبوين خلف عن الصغير، فإنه يؤدّي حينئذ إلى أن يكون للخلف خلف، وهذا فاسد لصيرورة شيء واحد أصلاً وخلفا، بل المراد أن كل واحد من تبعية أهل الدار وأداء أحد الأبوين خلف عن أداء الصغير بنفسه، إلا أن البعض أي تبعية الدار مرتب على البعض، أي تبعية الأبوين، ونظيره أن ابن الميت خلف عنه في الميراث، وإذا عدم كان ابن الابن خلفا عنه لا عنه، لئلا يلزم للخلف خلف.
Chapter on Rulings. Explanation of the divisions of Allah's rights: and there is a burden meaning punishment in it, like kharaj, for it is itself a burden for the land that one cultivates, otherwise he would return it and transfer it to another hand, but there is the meaning of punishment in it in that it is obligatory upon the disbelievers who occupied themselves with cultivating the world and cast the Hereafter behind their backs. Initially. And a right that is self-subsisting, i.e., established by its essence without anything from it being attached to the servant's liability such that its performance becomes obligatory upon him, but Allah has preserved it for His own sake and undertook its collection and distribution by whoever is His vicegerent on earth, i.e., the ruler, like the khums of spoils and mines. For jihad is a right of Allah, so it is fitting that what is acquired thereby, i.e., the spoils, all belongs to Allah, but He made four-fifths obligatory for the warriors as a favor from Him, and kept the fifth; likewise mines, for they are a name for what Allah created in the earth of gold and silver, so it is fitting that it all be for Allah, but Allah made permissible for the finder or owner four-fifths of it as a favor and bounty. And the rights of servants, like compensation for destroyed property and usurped goods and others, such as blood money, ownership of the sold item and the price, ownership of marriage, and the like. And these rights, i.e., their genus, whether a right of Allah or of a servant, are divided into an original and a substitute that stands in place of the original when it is impossible. So faith: its original is attestation and confession together before Allah Almighty, then confession alone became an independent original substituting for attestation regarding the rulings of this world, such that confession takes its place regarding the derivation of its rulings, as in the case of one coerced into Islam: confession is made to take the place of the sum of attestation and confession even if attestation is absent from him. Then the performance of one of the parents for a minor became a substitute for the minor's own performance of faith, so that the minor is made a Muslim by the Islam of one of his parents, and its rulings apply to him regarding inheritance, funeral prayer, and the like. Then the adherence to the people of the abode became a substitute for adherence to the parents in establishing Islam for a child captured by the people of Islam and brought out to their abode: he is judged to be Muslim and prayer is performed over him by virtue of adherence. And this is not that adherence to the people of the abode is a substitute for the performance of one of the parents and the performance of one of the parents is a substitute for the minor, for that would lead to a substitute having a substitute, which is invalid because one thing becomes both original and substitute. Rather, the meaning is that each of adherence to the people of the abode and the performance of one of the parents is a substitute for the minor's own performance, except that some, i.e., adherence to the abode, is dependent on some, i.e., adherence to the parents. An analogy is that the son of the deceased is a substitute for him in inheritance, and if he is absent, the son's son is a substitute for him, not for him, to avoid a substitute having a substitute.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage from Noorul Anwar is an explanation of the categories of legal rights (huquq) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author first distinguishes between rights of Allah and rights of servants. Rights of Allah include those with a punitive element like kharaj (land tax) and self-subsisting rights like khums (one-fifth of spoils and mines) which are collected by the ruler. Rights of servants include compensation for damages, blood money, and contractual ownership. The main focus is the division of rights into an original (asl) and a substitute (khalaf) that steps in when the original is impossible to fulfill. The example of faith (iman) illustrates this: the original is attestation (tasdiq) and confession (iqrar) together, but confession alone substitutes for attestation in worldly rulings because inner attestation is hidden. Further substitutions occur: a parent's faith substitutes for a minor's, and adherence to an Islamic abode substitutes for parental adherence. The author clarifies that substitution is not hierarchical in the sense that one substitute replaces another in a chain; rather, each is a direct substitute for the original, though one may be dependent on another condition. This concept prevents the logical error of a substitute having its own substitute.

Key Terms
حق الله (haqq Allah): A right that pertains to Allah Almighty, whether for His own sake or for public interest, with or without punishment.
حق العبد (haqq al-ʿabd): A right belonging to a human being, such as compensation, ownership, or personal status.
أصل (aṣl): The original form of a right, which is the primary and complete mode of obligation.
خلف (khalaf): A substitute that stands in place of the original right when the original cannot be realized.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi usul, which is considered a substitute (khalaf) for the original attestation (tasdiq) in faith?
A) Fear of punishment
B) Oral confession (iqrar)
C) Performance of rituals
D) Membership in an Islamic state

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, every right has an original and a substitute that directly replaces the original when it is impossible, but substitutes are never themselves substituted in a chain.

The Four Categories of Things Rulings Are Attached To: Sabab, 'Illah, Shart, and 'Alamah
Definition and division of sabab among four categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sabab in Hanafi usul, distinguish it from 'illa, shart, and 'alama, and apply the rule that a valid substitute requires the possibility of the original.

Core Idea
Sabab is a non-effective cause set by the Lawgiver; a substitute is valid only if the original could have existed.

In this passage, the author clarifies that rulings are attached to four types of things: sabab, 'illa, shart, and 'alama. The focus is on sabab, which is a cause but not directly effective. A key principle is that a substitute (like tayammum for wudu) is valid only if the original act could have been performed. This distinguishes sabab from other categories and has practical implications for oaths and purity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
The text lists four: sabab (cause), 'illa (effective cause), shart (condition), and 'alama (sign). Understand each briefly from the description.
2
Define sabab as non-effective
Sabab is a cause that does not necessitate the ruling by itself; it is set by the Lawgiver. Contrast with 'illa, which is directly effective. For example, intention to pray is sabab for wudu, but wudu is not automatically obligatory without the intention.
3
Apply the substitute condition
The text explains that a substitute (khalaf) is valid only if the original is possible. Work through the examples: in a false oath about the past (ghamus), truthfulness is impossible, so no expiation as substitute; in an oath about touching the sky, truthfulness is theoretically possible, so expiation is obligatory.
This illustrates that a substitute requires the possibility of the original.
4
Locate the method of induction
The four categories are derived by induction (istiqra'). The text mentions that some scholars have explained a logical division, but induction is the most appropriate method. Reflect on why induction is used here: to categorize all possible attachments.
5
Recognize the scope
These four categories cover everything that rulings are attached to. Understand that knowing this classification helps in analyzing how a ruling relates to its causes and conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(القمر) إذا لم يحتمل الأصل إلخ فلا يثبت الأصل من السبب، فلا يصح الخلف عنه كالخارج من البدن الذي لا يكون موجبًا للوضوء كالدمع ليس موجبًا للأصل، أي الوضوء، فليس موجبًا للخلف أي التيمم، فلا يصح الخلف. (القمر) في يمين الغموس هي الحلف على ماض كاذبًا عمدًا، كذا في "الكنز". (القمر) في يمين الغموس إلخ حاصل هذه المسألة: أن الكفارة في اليمين خلف للبر؛ لأنه يجب في الخلف لكون وضع الحلف لأجله، ولما لم يحصل البر فيجب الكفارة خلفًا عن البر لتكون مكفرة للذنب الذي حصل من عدم البر، ولا يمكن البر في الغموس لكون عود الماضي ممتنعا ، ولما لم يمكن البر فلم يلزم خلفه أيضا أي الكفارة. (القمر) فأربعة إلخ ودليل الحصر وإن بينوا فيه لكن الأوجه أن يقال بالاستقراء، وما بينوه هو أن ما يتعلق به الأحكام إما أن كان مؤثرًاً في إيجاب الحكم ووجوده الظاهر أو لا يكون، والأول: هو العلة، والثاني: إما أن يوجد الحكم عنده أم لا، الأول هو الشرط، والثاني: إما أن يكون علمًا على وجود الحكم أو لا، الأول: العلامة، والثاني: هو السبب، كذا قيل. Chapter on rulings: Explanation of the cause and its divisions. It is connected to the original first, so the substitute is valid. But if the original does not admit of existence, then the substitute is not valid from it. Likewise, if the original itself exists, the substitute is also not valid. And this—i.e., the fruit (outcome) of the possibility of the original's existence—appears in the oath of ghamus (false past oath) and the oath regarding touching the sky. For in the oath of ghamus, expiation is not obligatory, because truthfulness (al-birr), which is the original, is not conceivable: the past time has passed for the swearer and he has no power over it. In the oath regarding touching the sky, truthfulness is conceivable and possible because prophets and angels touch it, and for saints it is also possible by miraculous breach of custom, but the inability is apparent at the time, so expiation is obligatory for him. Meaning: by custom and habit, i.e., as a substitute for truthfulness. [Explanation of the cause and its divisions] As for the second division of the aforementioned division at the beginning of the chapter—that which rulings are attached to—there are four: the first: the cause (sabab), and it has four divisions: the first: meaning the second division. First: then the original is established, then by its loss the substitute is valid, just as the cause of the obligation of wudu, which is the intention to pray, established wudu as obligatory, then by inability to find water, one transfers to its substitute, i.e., tayammum. (al-Qamar) If the original does not admit of existence etc., then the original is not established from the cause, so the substitute from it is not valid, like something exiting the body that does not necessitate wudu, such as tears: it is not a cause for the original (wudu), so it is not a cause for the substitute (tayammum), so the substitute is not valid. (al-Qamar) The oath of ghamus is the oath about the past intentionally false, as in al-Kanz. (al-Qamar) The sum of this issue: expiation in oaths is a substitute for truthfulness; because it is obligatory as a substitute since the oath is placed for its sake. When truthfulness does not occur, expiation becomes obligatory as a substitute for truthfulness to atone for the sin of lacking truthfulness. Truthfulness is impossible in ghamus because the return of the past is prevented, and when truthfulness is impossible, its substitute (expiation) is also not required. (al-Sunbuli) Expiation is not obligatory: i.e., that which is a substitute for truthfulness. (al-Qamar) It (truthfulness) is the original: i.e., in oaths, for the oath is placed for truthfulness. (al-Qamar) From the aforementioned division: i.e., the division of all that is established by evidences (al-Qamar) So four, i.e., by induction: cause ('illa), condition (shart), and sign (alama). (al-Qamar) So four etc. The proof of the enumeration—though they have explained it—the most appropriate is to say by induction. What they explained is that that to which rulings are attached either is effective in necessitating the ruling and its apparent existence, or not. The first is the 'illa (effective cause). The second: either the ruling exists with it or not. The first is the condition (shart). The second: either it is a sign of the existence of the ruling or not. The first is the sign (alama), and the second is the cause (sabab). This is what is said. (al-Sunbuli) And it (the cause): i.e., that to which the term 'sabab' is applied, either literally or metaphorically. (al-Qamar) It is.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage introduces the second major category of the text's overall division—the things to which rulings are attached. It lists four: cause (sabab), effective cause ('illa), condition (shart), and sign (alama). Here, the focus is on 'sabab' (cause). The definition is approached by induction: sabab is that which rulings are attached to but is not directly effective; it is a marker established by the Lawgiver. The text first explains a condition for the validity of a substitute (khalaf): the original must be potentially existent. Examples are given: in a false oath about the past (ghamus), truthfulness (the original) is impossible, so no expiation is due; but in an oath about touching the sky, truthfulness is theoretically possible (for prophets, etc.), so expiation is obligatory. This illustrates that a substitute requires the possibility of the original. The passage then clarifies the four categories: (1) 'illa is effective in causing the ruling; (2) condition is where the ruling exists with it but not necessarily caused by it; (3) sign indicates the ruling's existence; (4) sabab is what remains after the others. The text ends with a note that 'sabab' is used both literally and metaphorically.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): A cause: one of the four categories that rulings are attached to; it is not directly effective but is established by the Lawgiver.
علة (ʿillah): The effective cause that directly necessitates the ruling and its apparent existence.
شرط (sharṭ): A condition: the ruling exists when it is present, but it does not cause the ruling.
علامة (ʿalāmah): A sign: it indicates the existence of the ruling without being a cause or condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The original must exist at the same time.
B) The original must be possible to exist.
C) The substitute must be identical to the original.
D) The substitute must be easier than the original.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, rulings are attached to four categories: sabab (non-effective cause), 'illa (effective cause), shart (condition), and 'alama (sign); a substitute is valid only if the original could have been performed.

The Real Cause (Sabab Haqiqi) in Hanafi Usul
Defines sabab haqiqi and contrasts with other categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sabab haqiqi and distinguish it from 'illa, shart, and 'alama by applying the Hanafi usul criteria.

Core Idea
Sabab is a path to the ruling with no causal influence—unlike 'illa which necessitates.

In Hanafi usul, understanding the precise categories of things that relate to rulings is essential for correct istinbat. This passage from Noor al-Anwar defines the real cause (sabab haqiqi) and distinguishes it from the effective cause ('illa), condition (shart), and sign ('alama). The definition hinges on whether the thing has any causal efficacy or influence over the ruling. By mastering this distinction, you will be able to correctly classify legal indicators and avoid conflating them in istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
The passage lists four things that rulings are attached to: sabab, 'illa, shart, 'alama. Note each one and their general role.
This list is derived from istiqra' (induction) of the Sharia.
2
Extract the definition of sabab haqiqi
Locate the sentence: 'سبب حقيقي، وهو ما يكون طريقًا إلى الحكم أي مفضيًا إليه في الجملة'. Parse that sabab is a path (tariq) that leads to the ruling, not necessarily causing it.
The phrase 'في الجملة' indicates generality.
3
Analyze the exclusions
Each part of the definition excludes other categories: 'من غير أن يضاف إليه وجوب' excludes 'illa (which imposes obligation); 'ولا وجود' excludes shart (which causes existence); 'ولا يعقل فيه معاني العلل' excludes any sabab with a hint of causality.
A cause with shubhat al-'illa is not a real cause.
4
Apply to the example
The example of a person pointing out someone's property for theft: the pointing is a path to the theft, but does not cause it. The thief's free will is the cause. This illustrates a real cause.
The 'illa (theft) is attributed to the thief, not the pointer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الأحكام
بيان السبب وأقسامه
منعقدًا للأصل أوّلاً، فيصح الخلف، أمّا إذا لم يحتمل الأصل الوجود، فلا يصح الخلف عنه، وكذا إذا كان الأصل موجودًا بنفسه فلا يصح الخلف أيضًا وتظهر هذه أي ثمرة احتمال الأصل للوجود في يمين الغموس والحلف على مس السماء، فإن في يمين الغموس لا تجب الكفارة؛ إذ لا يتصور البرّ الذي هو الأصل فإن زمان الماضي قد فات عن الحالف، ولا قدرة له عليه وفي الحلف على مس السماء يتصوّر البرّ ويمكن؛ لأن الأنبياء والملائكة يمسونه، وللأولياء أيضًا ممكن بخرق العادة، ولكنّ العجز ظاهر في الحال، فتجب الكفارة له. أي عرفا وعادةً أي خلفا عن البر
بيان السبب وأقسامه]

(السنبلي) وهو: أي ما يطلق عليه السبب حقيقة أو مجازا. (القمر)
هو
سبب حقيقي، وهو ما يكون طريقًا إلى الحكم أي مفضيًا إليه في الجملة، بخلاف العلامة، فإنها دالة عليه لا مفضية إليه من غير أن يضاف إليه وجوب الحكم كما يضاف ذلك إلى العلة ولا وجود كما يضاف ذلك إلى الشرط، ولا يعقل فيه معاني أي وجوب الحكم العلل بوجه من الوجوه بحيث لا يكون له تأثير في وجود الحكم أصلاً، لا بواسطة ولا بغير واسطة؛ إذ لو كان كذلك لم يكن سببًا حقيقيًا، بل سببًا له شبهة العلة، أو سببًا فيه معنى العلة، لكن يتخلّل بينه أي بين السبب وبين الحكم علة لا تضاف إلى السبب؛ إذ كانت مضافة إلى السبب والحكم مضاف إليها لكان السبب علة العلة، لا سببًا حقيقيًا على ما سيأتي كدلالة إنسان على مال إنسان أو نفسه ليسرقه أو ليقتله، أي تلك العلة سبب حقيقي أي ليس فيه شائبة العلية أصلاً. (القمر) سبب حقيقي إلخ واعلم أولاً أن السبب في اللغة اسم لما يتوصل به إلى المقصود، ومنه سمي الطريق سببًا؛ لأنه وسيلة يتوصل به إلى المقصود، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَآتَيْنَاهُ مِنْ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ سَبَبًا﴾ (الكهف: ٨٤) أي طريقًا موصلاً إليه، وسُمي سببًا؛ لأنه يوصل إلى البيت، ويسمى الحبل سببًا؛ لأنه يوصل إلى الماء، وما بينه الماتن له هو ما في الشريعة وفوائد القيود هكذا، فبقوله: "طريقا" احترز عن العلامة؛ لأنها ليست بطريق إلى الحكم، بل هي دلالة على الطريق، وبقوله: "من غير أن يضاف إليه وجوب" احترز عن العلة، وبقوله : "ولا وجود" احترز عن الشرط، وبقوله : "ولا يعقل فيه معاني العلل" احترز عن السبب الذي له شبهة العلة وعن السبب الذي فيه العلة هذا هو السبب الحقيقي على اختيار المصنف له، وهو اختيار فخر الإسلام لله وغيره. (السنبلي) وجوب الحكم المراد بوجوب الحكم: صحة قولنا: "وجد فوجد" أي لزوم المعلول العلة لزوماً عقليًا مصحّحا لترتبه بالفاء. (القمر)
معنى
ولا وجود أي وجود الحكم، والمراد بالوجود: صحة قولنا وجد عنده ولا يكون له تأثير". (القمر)
فيه معنى
العلة،
إذ لو كان كذلك: أي كان فيه معاني العلل (القمر) العلة: فإن كلاً منهما طريق إلى الحكم من غير أن يُضاف إليه وجوب ولا وجود ولكن لا يخلو عن معنى العلة. (القمر) معنى العلة: اعلم أن علة علة الشيء تسمى بسبب وهو يكون مؤثرًا في وجود الحكم بواسطة، وما في مسير" "الدائر" من أن له تأثيرًا في وجود الحكم "مسير بغير واسطة بدون إضافة الوجوب والوجود فعجيب تأمل (القمر) علة أي علة مؤثرة في الحكم يكون الحكم مضافًا إليها، ولا تضاف إلى السبب بأن يكون العلة من الأفعال الاختيارية. (القمر) ليسرقه: أي ليسرق المال، وما في "مسير "الدائر" في إظهار مرجع الضمير في هذا القول أي المال أو النفس فعجيب. (القمر)
Chapter on Rulings. Explanation of the Cause and Its Divisions... As for the second division from the mentioned division at the beginning of the chapter, which is that to which rulings are attached, they are four: first: the cause (sabab), and it has four divisions... The real cause is that which is a path to the ruling, i.e., leading to it in general, unlike the sign...
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage from Noor al-Anwar defines the real cause (sabab haqiqi) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It begins by discussing the concept of substitute (khalf) in legal causes: if the original (asl) can potentially exist, then the substitute is valid; otherwise not. Examples include false oaths about the past (yamin ghamus) where expiation is not required because the original (righteousness/truthfulness) is impossible, versus oaths about touching the sky where the original is possible (prophets and angels can touch it), so expiation is required. The text then turns to the four categories of things that relate to rulings: cause (sabab), effective cause ('illa), condition (shart), and sign ('alama). It defines the real cause as something that is a path to the ruling without the ruling's obligation or existence being attributed to it, and without it containing any meaning of 'illa. The commentary explains that the cause is a path (tariq) to the ruling, unlike the sign which merely indicates; it does not have the effect of 'illa (which necessitates the ruling's obligation) nor does it have the existential effect of a condition. The real cause has no causal influence whatsoever, directly or indirectly. If it had any element of 'illa, it would be a cause with a semblance of 'illa or a cause containing 'illa, which would make it a cause of the 'illa rather than a real cause. An example is a person pointing out someone's property or self for theft or murder — the pointing is a real cause for the act, not a causal influence. The gloss (al-Qamar) clarifies the linguistic meaning of sabab as a means to an end, citing Quran 18:84. The author emphasizes that the real cause as defined by the matn (al-Matin, likely al-Nasafi) is the preferred view of Fakhr al-Islam and others.

Key Terms
سبب حقيقي (sabab haqiqi): A real cause: a path to the ruling with no causal influence.
علة ('illa): Effective cause that necessitates the ruling; obligation is attributed to it.
شرط (shart): Condition; the ruling's existence depends on it but is not caused by it.
علامة ('alama): Sign that indicates the ruling without leading to it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT excluded from the definition of sabab haqiqi?
A) The obligation of the ruling being attributed to it.
B) The existence of the ruling being attributed to it.
C) The ruling being indicated by it as a sign.
D) Any meaning of 'illa being understood in it.

Key Takeaway
A real cause (sabab haqiqi) is a path to the ruling with absolutely no causal influence, obligation, or existence attributed to it.

The Substitute (Khalf) Principle and Its Conditions
Explains the condition for validity of a substitute using oath examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that a substitute is valid only when the original can potentially exist, using the examples of false oaths about the past and oaths about touching the sky.

Core Idea
A substitute is only valid if the original can be realized; otherwise, no substitute.

The passage opens with an important principle concerning legal substitutes (khalf): a substitute is only enacted when the original (asl) can potentially exist. Using the examples of false oaths (yamin ghamus) versus oaths about touching the sky, the text illustrates how the possibility of the original determines whether a substitute (expiation) is required. This lesson unpacks that principle and its application.

Guided Path
1
Understand the substitute principle
The passage states: 'if the original can potentially exist, then the substitute is valid; otherwise not.' This is the core rule. The substitute (e.g., expiation) stands in for the original (e.g., truthfulness) when the original is possible but not performed.
The original must be capable of existence in the first place.
2
Apply to false oath about the past (yamin ghamus)
In a false oath about a past event, the original (al-birr, being truthful) is impossible because the past cannot be changed. Therefore, no substitute (kaffara) is required. The passage says: 'لا تجب الكفارة'.
The impossibility is due to the past being unchangeable.
3
Apply to oath about touching the sky
In an oath about touching the sky, the original (touching the sky) is possible in principle: prophets, angels, and saints by miracle can touch it. Therefore, the substitute (kaffara) is required when the oath is broken.
Even though it is impossible for ordinary humans, the possibility in the Sharia (through miracles) suffices.

(القمر) في يمين الغموس إلخ حاصل هذه المسألة: أن الكفارة في اليمين خلف للبر؛ لأنه يجب في الخلف لكون وضع الحلف لأجله، ولما لم يحصل البر فيجب الكفارة خلفًا عن البر لتكون مكفرة للذنب الذي حصل من عدم البر، ولا يمكن البر في الغموس لكون عود الماضي ممتنعا ، ولما لم يمكن البر فلم يلزم خلفه أيضا أي الكفارة. هو
سبب حقيقي، وهو ما يكون طريقًا إلى الحكم أي مفضيًا إليه في الجملة، بخلاف العلامة، فإنها دالة عليه لا مفضية إليه من غير أن يضاف إليه وجوب الحكم كما يضاف ذلك إلى العلة ولا وجود كما يضاف ذلك إلى الشرط، ولا يعقل فيه معاني أي وجوب الحكم العلل بوجه من الوجوه بحيث لا يكون له تأثير في وجود الحكم أصلاً، لا بواسطة ولا بغير واسطة؛ إذ لو كان كذلك لم يكن سببًا حقيقيًا، بل سببًا له شبهة العلة، أو سببًا فيه معنى العلة، لكن يتخلّل بينه أي بين السبب وبين الحكم علة لا تضاف إلى السبب؛ إذ كانت مضافة إلى السبب والحكم مضاف إليها لكان السبب علة العلة، لا سببًا حقيقيًا على ما سيأتي كدلالة إنسان على مال إنسان أو نفسه ليسرقه أو ليقتله، أي تلك العلة سبب حقيقي أي ليس فيه شائبة العلية أصلاً. (القمر) سبب حقيقي إلخ واعلم أولاً أن السبب في اللغة اسم لما يتوصل به إلى المقصود، ومنه سمي الطريق سببًا؛ لأنه وسيلة يتوصل به إلى المقصود، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَآتَيْنَاهُ مِنْ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ سَبَبًا﴾ (الكهف: ٨٤) أي طريقًا موصلاً إليه، وسُمي سببًا؛ لأنه يوصل إلى البيت، ويسمى الحبل سببًا؛ لأنه يوصل إلى الماء، وما بينه الماتن له هو ما في الشريعة وفوائد القيود هكذا، فبقوله: "طريقا" احترز عن العلامة؛ لأنها ليست بطريق إلى الحكم، بل هي دلالة على الطريق، وبقوله: "من غير أن يضاف إليه وجوب" احترز عن العلة، وبقوله : "ولا وجود" احترز عن الشرط، وبقوله : "ولا يعقل فيه معاني العلل" احترز عن السبب الذي له شبهة العلة وعن السبب الذي فيه العلة هذا هو السبب الحقيقي على اختيار المصنف له، وهو اختيار فخر الإسلام لله وغيره. (السنبلي) وجوب الحكم المراد بوجوب الحكم: صحة قولنا: "وجد فوجد" أي لزوم المعلول العلة لزوماً عقليًا مصحّحا لترتبه بالفاء. (القمر)
معنى
ولا وجود أي وجود الحكم، والمراد بالوجود: صحة قولنا وجد عنده ولا يكون له تأثير". (القمر)

خلف (khalf): Substitute; a ruling that stands in for the original when the original cannot be performed.
يمين غموس (yamin ghamus): A false oath about the past, sworn deliberately and knowingly.
برّ (birr): Righteousness, truthfulness, fulfilling the oath.

The Three Divisions of Cause (Sabab) in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the three types of sabab with examples and rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of cause (sabab) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, apply the distinction between pure cause and cause of the cause, and explain the legal consequences of each type with examples.

Core Idea
A pure cause does not create liability; when the intervening act is attributed to the causer, it becomes a cause of the cause and incurs compensation.

In Hanafi legal theory, the concept of cause (sabab) is central to attributing effects to actions. But not all causes are equal: some are pure, some are indirect, and some are metaphorical. This lesson unpacks the three divisions of sabab as explained in the commentary of Nur al-Anwar, showing how liability, guarantee, and penalties are determined by the type of cause involved. You will learn to discriminate between these types and apply them to real cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of sabab
Read the passage and list the three categories: pure cause (sabab mahd), cause of the cause ('illat al-'illa), and metaphorical cause (sabab majazi). Note the Arabic terms.
Pure cause = no liability; cause of cause = indirect liability; metaphorical cause = liability only after violation.
2
For each type, locate the example and ruling
Find the example given: indication to thief (pure cause), driving/leading an animal (cause of cause), oath (metaphorical cause). Note the specific legal consequence (guarantee, no guarantee, expiation, etc.).
The muhrim pointing to game is an exception due to prior obligation.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil) behind each ruling
Analyze why each type yields a different ruling. For pure cause, the free will of the direct agent breaks the causal chain. For cause of cause, the intervening agent has no choice (animal), so causation is attributed upward. For oath, the primary purpose (birr) prevents it from being a direct cause of consequences.
Key concept: attribution (idafah) of the intervening cause to the original cause.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on the conspirator (sa'i)
The passage mentions that early scholars ruled no liability (pure cause), but later jurists (mutakkhirin) ruled liability due to corruption of times (taqdir al-zaman). Understand the shift and why later jurists prioritized public interest.
This is an example of how rulings can change with changing circumstances.

Source Text

فصل في الأحكام
بيان السبب وأقسامه
فإنها سبب حقيقي للسرقة والقتل؛ لأنها تفضي إليه من غير أن تكون موجبة أو موجدة الدلالة السرقة أو القتل له، ولا تأثير لها في فعل السرقة أصلا لكن تخلّل بين الدلالة وبين السرقة علة غير مضافة للسرقة والقتل للدلالة إلى الدلالة، وهو فعل السارق المختار وقصده؛ إذ لا يلزم أنّ من دلّه أحد على فعل سُوء يفعله المدلول البتة، بل لعلّ الله يوفقه على تركه مع دلالته، فإن وقع منه السرقة أو القتل أي فعل السوء لا يضمن الدال شيئًا؛ لأنه صاحب سبب محض لا صاحب علّة، وعلى هذا فينبغي أن لا يضمن من سعى إلى سلطان ظالم في حق أحد بغير حق حتى غرمه مالاً؛ لأنه صاحب أي السلطان سبب محض، لكن أفتى المتأخرون بضمانه لفساد الزمان بالسعي الباطل وكثرة السعاة فيه، وأما المحرم الدال على صيد فإنما ضمن قيمته؛ لأنه ترك الأمان الملتزم بإحرامه بفعل الدلالة كالمودع إذا دلّ السارق على الوديعة يضمن لكونه تاركًا للحفظ الملتزم. فإن أضيفت العلة المتخلّلة بين السبب والحكم إليه أي إلى السبب صار للسبب حكم العلل في وجوب الضمان عليه؛ لأن الحكم حينئذٍ مضاف إلى العلة، والعلة مضافة إلى السبب، على السبب وهو فعل السارق إلخ وهذا الفعل لا يُضاف إلى الدلالة إذ إلخ. (القمر) يوفقه أي المدلول على ترك الفعل السوء. (القمر) لا يضمن إلخ فليس على الدال حد السرقة ولا يُقاد هو ولا يؤخذ منه الدية فإنه ليس سارقا ولا قاتلاً، بل السارق والقاتل من صدر منه السرقة والقتل بالاختيار. (القمر) لأنه إلخ: هذا متعلق بقوله: فينبغي أن لا يضمن أي لأن الساعي صاحب سبب محض، فالساعي سعى لأخذ المال، وأما الآخذ بالاختيار فهو الظالم لا الساعي. (القمر) بضمانه: أي بضمان الساعي؛ لأن المظلوم لا يقدر على أخذ الضمان من الظالم، فحكموا بالضمان على الساعي لئلا يضيع الحقوق وينزجر السعاة عن السعي. (القمر) وأما المحرم إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره أن المحرم الدال على صيد سبب محض قد تحلّل بينه وبين المقصود علة لا تضاف إلى هذا السبب، وهو فعل الفاعل المختار ، أي المدلول المباشر، فينبغي أن لا يضمن الدال مع أنه حكم بأنه يضمن الدال قيمة الصيد (القمر) الأمان: أي أمان الصيد عن الاصطياد. (القمر) بفعل الدلالة فكان الدال جانيًا بترك الأمن، فيجب عليه الضمان بهذا الوجه لا لكونه سببا محضا لقتل الصيد وهذا متعلق بقوله: ترك. (القمر) للحفظ الملتزم أي للحفظ الذي التزمه المودع بعقد الوديعة.(القمر)
فصل في الأحكام
بيان السبب وأقسامه
فكان السبب علّة العلة، وهذا هو القسم الثاني من السبب، وفيه فائدة الاحتراز عن قوله : علة لا تضاف إلى السبب كسوق الدابة وقودها فإن كل واحد منهما سبب لتلف أي سوق والقود ما يتلف بوطئها في حالة السوق والقود، وقد تخلّل بينه وبين التلف ما هو علة له، وهو أي مال والنفس فعل الدابة، لكنه مضاف إلى السوق والقود؛ لأن الدابة لا اختيار لها في فعلها سيما إذا كان أحد سائقاً أو قائدا لها، والعلة ليست صالحة للحكم، فيضاف التلف إلى علّة العلة فيما يرجع إلى بدل المحل، وهو ضمان الدية والقيمة، وأما فيما يرجع إلى جزاء المباشرة أي قيمة المتلف أي جزاء الفعل فلا يكون مضافًا إليها، فلا يحرم عن الميراث، ولا يجب عليه الكفارة والقصاص. واليمين بالله تعالى بأن يقول: والله لأفعلن كذا، أو لا أفعل كذا. أو بالطلاق والعتاق بأن يقول: "إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق، أو أنت حر " يسمّى سببًا مجازا أي قبل الحنث للكفارة والجزاء، وهذا هو القسم الثالث من السبب، وإنما كان سببًا مجازا؛ لأن اليمين شرعت للبرّ، والبرّ لا يكون قط طريقا إلى الكفارة في اليمين بالله وإلى الجزاء في اليمين بغير الله؛ لأنه أي ما هو كذا علة العلة أي للحكم، وهذا السبب سبب فيه معنى العلة. (القمر) وفيه: أي في قول المصنف له: فإن أضيف .إلخ . (القمر) وقد تخلّل بينه: أي بين كل واحد من السوق والقود وبين التلف ما هو علة له، أي للتلف، وهو علة للتلف فعل الدابة لكنه إلخ . (القمر) فيضاف إلخ فيجب الضمان على السائق والقائد.(القمر) وهو : الضمير عائد إلى ما في قوله فيما يرجع والدية مائة من الإبل أو ألف دينار أو عشرة آلاف درهم في "الكنز". (القمر) فلا يكون أي التلف مضافا إليها أي علة العلة فلا يحرم أي السائق والقائد عن الميراث عند تلف نفس المورث، ولا يجب عليه الكفارة والقصاص عند تلف النفس، فإن هذه الأمور جزاء المباشرة، والسائق والقائد ليسا بمباشرين حقيقة (القمر) إن دخلت إلخ إيماء إلى أن اليمين بالطلاق والعتاق تعليق الطلاق والعتاق (القمر) للكفارة وهذا في اليمين بالله. (القمر) والجزاء: أي وقوع الطلاق والعتاق وهذا في اليمين بالطلاق والعتاق . (القمر) شرعت للبر: فإن المقصود من شرعية اليمين سواء كانت بالله أو لغيره تحقق المحلوف عليه من الفعل أو الترك. (القمر) طريقا إلخ : أي طريقا مفضيًا إلى إلخ. (القمر) لأنه : أي لأن البر مانع من الحنث؛ لأنه ضده.(القمر)
Section on Legal Rulings: Explanation of the cause and its divisions. For it (the indication) is a real cause for theft and murder because it leads to it without being necessitating or creating the theft or murder for him, and it has no effect on the act of theft at all, but between the indication and the theft intervenes a cause ('illa) not attributed to the theft and murder for the indication, which is the act of the thief with his free choice and intention; for it is not necessary that one who is indicated to do an evil act will do it at all, but perhaps Allah grants him success in leaving it despite the indication. If the theft or murder occurs (i.e., the evil act), the indicator does not guarantee anything because he is a possessor of a pure cause, not a possessor of a cause ('illa). And on this basis, one who conspires (sa'a) to a tyrant ruler against someone unjustly until he (the tyrant) takes his property should not guarantee, because he (the conspirator) is a possessor of a pure cause as well. But the later jurists gave a fatwa that he does guarantee due to the corruption of the times through false conspiracy and the abundance of conspirators. As for the muhrim (one in ihram) who points out game, he only guarantees its value because he abandoned the security (of the game) that he was obligated to maintain by his ihram through the act of indication, like the depositary who points out the deposit to the thief guarantees because he abandoned the safeguarding he was obligated to maintain. If the intervening cause ('illa) between the cause and the ruling is attributed to the cause, then the cause acquires the ruling of the 'illa in the obligation of guarantee upon him, because then the ruling is attributed to the 'illa, and the 'illa is attributed to the cause. So the cause is 'illat al-'illa, and this is the second division of cause. And in it is the benefit of avoiding his saying: a 'illa not attributed to the cause, like driving an animal and leading it, for each one of them is a cause for the destruction of what is destroyed by its hooves in the state of driving and leading. There intervenes between it and the destruction what is a 'illa for it, namely the action of the animal, but it is attributed to the driving and leading because the animal has no choice in its action, especially when there is a driver or leader. The 'illa is not suitable for the ruling, so the destruction is attributed to the 'illat al-'illa with regard to the compensation for the thing itself, which is the guarantee of blood money and value. As for with regard to the punishment of direct action (i.e., the penalty for the act), it is not attributed to it, so he (the driver or leader) is not disinherited, and he is not obligated for expiation and retaliation. The oath by Allah the Exalted, by saying 'By Allah, I will do such-and-such' or 'I will not do such-and-such', or by divorce and manumission by saying 'If you enter the house, you are divorced' or 'you are free', is called a cause metaphorically before the violation (of the oath) for the expiation and the consequence (of divorce/freeing). This is the third division of cause. It is only a metaphorical cause because the oath is legislated for the fulfillment of the oath (al-birr), and the fulfillment is never a path to expiation in the oath by Allah, nor to the consequence in the oath by other than Allah, because it is 'illat al-'illa for the ruling. And this cause is a cause that has the meaning of 'illa.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding the principle of cause (sabab) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It opens with defining pure cause (sabab mahd): something that leads to an effect but does not necessitate it, because a free agent intervenes. Example: indicating a location to a thief does not make the indicator liable because the thief's own choice is the direct cause. The same applies to one who conspires with a tyrant: early scholars said no liability, but later jurists (mutakkhirin) held the conspirator liable due to prevailing corruption. The muhrim pointing to game is an exception: he guarantees because his ihram obligated him to protect game, so his act is a breach of duty, not a pure cause. The second type is when the intervening cause (like the animal's step) is attributed to the original cause (driving) because the animal has no choice; then the driver becomes indirectly liable for compensation (diyah, value) but not for criminal penalties (expiation, retaliation, disinheritance). The third type is oaths: they are causes metaphorically before violation because they are meant for fulfillment (birr), not for the expiation or divorce that follows violation. Thus, the oath is an 'illat al-'illa, and the ruling (expiation) is attributed to the violation, not the oath itself. The commentary by al-Qamar clarifies that the oath by Allah is for expiation, and by divorce/emancipation is for the occurrence of those consequences.

Key Terms
سبب محض (sabab mahd): A pure cause that leads to an effect without any willful act of the causer, e.g., indicating a thief to a location.
علة العلة (illat al-'illa): A cause that becomes the indirect cause because the intervening act (by an involuntary agent) is attributed to it, e.g., driving an animal that tramples.
يمين (yamin): An oath, which is considered a metaphorical cause (sabab majazan) for expiation or divorce/manumission after violation, because its primary purpose is fulfillment, not consequences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on a person who conspires (sa'i) with a tyrant ruler to take someone's property unjustly?
A) The conspirator is absolutely not liable because his act is a pure cause.
B) The conspirator is liable for compensation according to later Hanafi jurists due to corruption of the times.
C) The conspirator is liable for retaliation (qisas).
D) The conspirator is liable only if he directly took the property.

Key Takeaway
The three types of cause—pure, cause of the cause, and metaphorical—determine the extent of liability, with pure causes generally incurring no liability unless a prior obligation exists, while cause of the cause incurs compensation but not criminal penalties.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Second and Third Types of Cause (Sabab) in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the second and third divisions of cause in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the second and third types of sabab in Hanafi usul, apply them to examples, and evaluate the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute regarding metaphorical causes.

Core Idea
A sabab may be either the cause of the effective cause (second type) or a metaphorical cause (third type) like oaths.

This passage from 'Noor al-Anwar' builds on the earlier definition of sabab (cause) by introducing two further categories. The second type is the cause of the effective cause (illat al-illa), where the direct cause is an act of a non-rational agent. The third type is the metaphorical cause (sabab majazi), exemplified by oaths that are legislated for birr but may lead to a ruling when the preventer is removed. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly attributing liability and penalties in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two new types of sabab
The passage presents the second type (cause of the effective cause) and the third type (metaphorical cause). Locate the Arabic terms and note their definitions.
Second type: علة العلة (illat al-illa). Third type: سبب مجازي (sabab majazi).
2
Analyze the second type with the animal example
Examine the driving and leading example. Note that the animal's action is the effective cause of destruction, but because the animal has no choice, the destruction is attributed to the driver/leader. The effective cause is not the direct sabab; the sabab is the driving.
Legal effect: liability for monetary compensation (daman, diyah) but not for penalties (hadd, kaffarah, qisas).
3
Understand the third type: metaphorical cause
Study the oath examples: oaths by Allah and conditional divorces/emancipations. The passage explains they are called causes only metaphorically because they are legislated for birr (fulfillment), which prevents the ruling. The ruling only occurs when the condition is met or the oath is broken.
Key: the oath itself does not cause the ruling; it may lead to it when the preventer (birr) is removed.
4
Explore the madhhab dispute with al-Shafi'i
The text notes that al-Shafi'i considers such oaths real causes immediately, though the ruling is delayed. The Hanafi response is that they are metaphorical because the primary purpose is birr, not causing the ruling. Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).
Al-Shafi'i's view: real cause with delayed effect. Hanafi: metaphorical cause.
5
Consider Zufar's position and the 'semblance of reality'
Zufar denies any ruling follows from conditional oaths. Additionally, the text mentions that the conditional oaths have a 'semblance of reality' (shubhat al-haqiqah) because they lead to rulings, but they are not real causes.
This nuance helps distinguish degrees of metaphor.

فصل في الأحكام بيان السبب وأقسامه فكان السبب علّة العلة، وهذا هو القسم الثاني من السبب، وفيه فائدة الاحتراز عن قوله : علة لا تضاف إلى السبب كسوق الدابة وقودها فإن كل واحد منهما سبب لتلف ما يتلف بوطئها في حالة السوق والقود، وقد تخلّل بينه وبين التلف ما هو علة له، وهو فعل الدابة، لكنه مضاف إلى السوق والقود؛ لأن الدابة لا اختيار لها في فعلها سيما إذا كان أحد سائقاً أو قائدا لها، والعلة ليست صالحة للحكم، فيضاف التلف إلى علّة العلة فيما يرجع إلى بدل المحل، وهو ضمان الدية والقيمة، وأما فيما يرجع إلى جزاء المباشرة فلا يكون مضافًا إليها، فلا يحرم عن الميراث، ولا يجب عليه الكفارة والقصاص. واليمين بالله تعالى بأن يقول: والله لأفعلن كذا، أو لا أفعل كذا. أو بالطلاق والعتاق بأن يقول: "إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق، أو أنت حر " يسمّى سببًا مجازا أي قبل الحنث للكفارة والجزاء، وهذا هو القسم الثالث من السبب، وإنما كان سببًا مجازا؛ لأن اليمين شرعت للبرّ، والبرّ لا يكون قط طريقا إلى الكفارة في اليمين بالله وإلى الجزاء في اليمين بغير الله؛ لأنه مانع من الحنث وبدون الحنث لا تجب الكفارة ولا ينزل الجزاء، ولكن لما كان يحتمل أن يفضي إلى الحكم عند زوال المانع سمي سببًا مجازا باعتبار ما يؤول إليه، وعند الشافعي له اليمين بالله والمعلق بالشرط سبب حقيقى للكفارة والجزاء في الحال، ولكن الحكم تأخر إلى زمان الحنث ووجود الشرط كما مرّ في الوجوه الفاسدة. ولكن له شبهة الحقيقة أي ليس هو بمجاز خالص، بل مجاز يشبه الحقيقة، وعند زفر لا تجب الكفارة ولا ينزل الجزاء. (القمر) ولكن لما كان إلخ جواب سؤال مقدر، تقديره: أن اليمين لما لم يكن طريقا إلى الكفارة فكيف يصح قول المصنف له سابقا : اليمين بالله وبالطلاق والعتاق يسمّى سببًا مجازا؛ لأن العلاقة ضروري بين الحقيقة والمجاز، فأجاب بما قال ولكن إلخ فافهم (السنبلي سمي سببًا مجازا كإطلاق الخمر على عصير العنب باعتبار ما يؤول إليه وما في "مسير [؟] الدائر" من أن هذا الإطلاق إطلاق لاسم السبب على المسبب فمما لا أفهمه، تأمل، ثم اعلم أن فيما قال الشارح نظراً؛ لأن المعلّق بالشرط لا يؤول إلى السببية الحقيقية بعد وقوع المعلق عليه، أي الشرط بأن يصير طريقًا مفضيًا إلى الحكم، بل يؤول إلى العلية، فإنه بعد وقوع الشرط علة للحكم، إلا أن يقال: إنه أراد السبب بحسب اللغة. (القمر) وعند الشافعي له إلخ قلت: وثمرة الخلاف بين الشافعي وبيننا مر في الوجوه الفاسدة فتنبه له. (السنبلي) اليمين بالله إلخ أي اليمين بالله هي التي توجب الكفارة عند الحنث، والمعلق بالشرط وهو قوله: "أنت طالق" مثلاً هو الذي يوجب الجزاء، وهو الطلاق عند وجود الشرط ولكن الحكم إلخ. (القمر) ولكن له أي للمعلّق بالشرط الذي يسمى سببًا مجازا وهو قوله : أنت حر، وأنت طالق" مثلاً، وأما اليمين بالله فهو سبب مجازي فقط، ليس له شبهة الحقيقة، كذا قيل. (القمر) شبهة الحقيقة إلخ أي من حيث أنه مفض إلى الحكم كما أن السبب الحقيقي مفض إلى الحكم، لكن لما يكن موضوعًا للإفضاء إلى الحكم لم يكن سببا حقيقيًا بل شبيها بالحقيقة من حيث الإفضاء فقط، والسبب الحقيقي ههنا هو قوله: أنت طالق"؛ لأنه موضوع لوقوع الطلاق واليمين بالله وبالطلاق سبب مجازي يشتبه الحقيقة؛ لأنه ليس موضوعًا لوجوب الكفارة وللزوم الجزاء، بل اليمين بالله موضوع للبر، واليمين بالطلاق موضوع للمنع لكنهما مفضيان إليهما. (السنبلي) يشبه الحقيقة باعتبار أن اليمين شرعت للبر، فلو فات البر يلزم الجزاء في اليمين بالطلاق والعتاق، فصار البر مضمونًا بالجزاء، فصار لِمَا ضمن به البر من الطلاق والعتاق شبهة الثبوت في الحال، أي قبل فوات البر، فكان اليمين بالطلاق والعتاق سببًا حقيقيًا له. (القمر)
Chapter on Legal Rulings. Exposition of the cause and its divisions. The second type of cause is the cause of the effective cause. Its benefit is to avoid cases where an effective cause is not attributed to the cause, such as driving and leading an animal: each of them is a cause of the destruction of what is destroyed by its hooves while being driven or led. Between the driving/leading and the destruction intervenes what is the effective cause of destruction, namely the animal's action, but it is attributed to the driving/leading because the animal has no choice in its action, especially when someone is driving or leading it. The effective cause is not valid for the ruling, so destruction is attributed to the cause of the effective cause regarding compensation for the property (diyah and value). As for the penalty for direct action (hadd, kaffarah, qisas), it is not attributed to it, so the driver/leader is not deprived of inheritance, nor is kaffarah or qisas obligatory upon him. The oath by Allah (by saying 'by Allah, I will do such' or 'I will not do such') or by divorce and emancipation (by saying 'if you enter the house, you are divorced' or 'you are free') is called a metaphorical cause before breaking the oath regarding kaffarah and penalty. This is the third type of cause. It is called metaphorical because the oath is legislated for the fulfillment (birr), and fulfillment can never be a path to kaffarah in oaths by Allah or to penalty in oaths by other than Allah; because fulfillment prevents breaking the oath, and without breaking there is no kaffarah or penalty. But since it may lead to the ruling when the preventer is removed, it is called a metaphorical cause considering what it leads to. According to al-Shafi'i, the oath by Allah and the conditional [oath] are real causes for kaffarah and penalty immediately, but the ruling is delayed to the time of breaking and occurrence of the condition, as mentioned in the invalid aspects. However, it has a semblance of reality: it is not purely metaphorical but a metaphor resembling reality. According to Zufar, kaffarah and penalty do not occur. [Glosses from (al-Qamar) and (al-Sunbulī) elaborate on definitions, quotations, and responses to al-Shafi'i's view.]
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage from 'Noor al-Anwar' is an expansion on the types of cause (sabab) in Hanafi usul. It begins by defining the second type: the cause that is itself the cause of the effective cause (illa). The example given is driving or leading an animal that causes destruction. Although the direct cause of destruction is the animal's action, that action is attributed to the driving/leading because the animal lacks choice. Consequently, the driver/leader is held liable for monetary compensation (daman, diyah, value) since these relate to replacement of the property, but not for punishments like kaffarah or qisas, which are penalties for direct action. The third type is the metaphorical cause, exemplified by oaths: an oath by Allah (e.g., 'Wallahi I will not do X') or conditional divorce/emancipation (e.g., 'If you enter the house, you are divorced'). These are called causes only metaphorically because the oath is legislated for birr (fulfillment of the oath), and birr is the opposite of breaking the oath. Kaffarah or talaq only occur upon breaking the oath or fulfillment of the condition, not from the oath itself. However, because the oath may lead to those rulings when the preventer (birr) is removed, it is termed a metaphorical cause in anticipation of its consequence. The passage then notes a dispute: al-Shafi'i considers such oaths real causes immediately, though the effect is delayed. The Hanafi response, attributed to the commentator, argues that the conditional clause is not a real cause because it is not intended for causing the ruling; it is a metaphor with a semblance of reality. Zufar's position is also mentioned: no kaffarah or penalty at all. The glosses from al-Qamar and al-Sunbulī clarify terms, resolve apparent contradictions, and distinguish between linguistic and technical cause.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): That which leads to a ruling, either as a cause of the effective cause (second type) or as a metaphorical cause (third type).
علة العلة (illat al-illa): The cause of the effective cause; something that is indirectly responsible for a ruling because the direct cause is attributed to it.
سبب مجازي (sabab majazi): A cause that is not real but considered a cause in a metaphorical sense because it may lead to a ruling when a preventer is removed.
يمين (yamin): An oath, either by Allah or by divorce/emancipation, which serves as a metaphorical cause for kaffarah or talaq upon breaking or condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, what is the third type of cause (sabab)?
A) The cause of the effective cause (علة العلة)
B) A metaphorical cause (سبب مجازي) like oaths
C) A real cause (سبب حقيقي) like direct action
D) A cause that brings about immediate punishment

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul recognizes two additional types of sabab: cause of the effective cause (second) and metaphorical cause (third), each with distinct legal effects and subject to a madhhab dispute with al-Shafi'i.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Condition Subsequent to the Cause: Shart Mahd vs. Hukm al-Sabab
Usul rule explaining the nature of a condition subsequent to the cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul distinction between a condition (shart) and a cause (sabab) to determine liability when a condition follows the cause, using the examples of releasing a slave's shackle and ordering a slave to run away.

Core Idea
A condition that follows the cause is pure, but if it precedes the effect it takes the ruling of a cause—yet remains a condition.

In Hanafi usul, a condition (shart) is external to the ruling, while a cause (sabab) brings it about. But what happens when the condition appears after the cause? This lesson explores that nuance through the classic example of releasing a slave's shackle, and clarifies when liability attaches.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic distinction
Understand that a shart is something on which the existence of a ruling depends but does not produce it, while a sabab directly produces the effect. The passage contrasts a pure condition (shart mahd) with a cause.
Example: 'You are divorced if you enter the house' – the condition (entry) follows the cause (pronouncement) but is a pure condition.
2
Analyze the slave example
Examine the scenario: releasing a slave's shackle is a condition for running away. However, the slave's free act intervenes, so the release is not a cause of the loss. The releaser is not liable.
The intervention of a free agent (the slave) severs the attribution of the running away to the release.
3
Compare with ordering the slave
If the master orders the slave to run away, the orderer is liable because the order is a use of the slave; the slave's act is attributed to the orderer as if he usurped him.
The order is considered a cause (sabab) in the sense of utilization, not a mere condition.
4
Understand 'ruling of a cause'
The release precedes the running away, so it takes the ruling of a cause (hukm al-sabab) temporally, but it is not a true cause (ma'na al-sabab) because the slave's choice is the actual cause.
This is like releasing an animal on the road that later causes damage; the releaser is not liable because the animal's movement is its own.
5
Apply the principle to other cases
Contrast with driving an animal: the driver is liable because the animal's movement is attributed to the driver's action. The key is whether the intervening act is attributed to the original actor.
This distinction is used to determine liability in many fiqh cases involving indirect causation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعمّا إذا لم يكن الشرط سابقا على العلة كدخول الدار في قوله: "أنت طالق إن دخلت الدار"؛ إذ هو مؤخّر عن تكلّم قوله : أنت طالق" فإنه شرط محض داخل في القسم الأول.
كما إذا حلّ قيد عبد فَأَبق، فإنه شرط للإباق؛ إذ القيد كان مانعا، فإزالته شرط، ولكن

العلة : أي فعل الفاعل المختار . (القمر) فإنه شرط محض لخلوه عن معنى العلية والسببية. (القمر) ولكن تخلّل إلخ : فإن العبد فرّ باختياره. (القمر) إذ لا يلزم إلخ فإن حق المولى مانع من الخروج والإباق. (القمر) على الإباق إلخ: فلم يترتب الإباق على الحلّ، فلا يكون مضافًا إليه، فلم يكن ضامنًا، والإباق في الحقيقة علة التلف، والحاصل أن الحل وإن كان في الحقيقة شرطًا لكن له حكم السبب؛ إذ السبب الحقيقي يتقدم على وجود العلة كما أن الشرط يتأخر عنها، وهذا الوصف حاصل للحل؛ لأنه سابق على الإباق الذي هو علة التلف، فثبت أن له حكم السبب . (السنبلي) حكم الأسباب أي التي ليس فيها معنى العلة. (القمر) لا يضمن الحال إلخ أي لمالك العبد، وهذا إذا كان العبد عاقلا، وأما إذا كان مجنونا فالحال ضامن قيمته للمالك عند محمد الله (القمر) فإنه يضمن إلخ لأن هذا السبب في معنى العلة. (القمر) كسوق الدابة إلخ فإن السوق والقود سبب له حكم العلة؛ لأن العلة تحدث به، وههنا ليس كذلك؛ لأنه قد اعترض على الحلّ ما هو علة قائمة بنفسها غير حادثة بالشرط وهو الإباق، فالحلّ سبب محض ليس فيه معنى العلة أصلاً، فثبت أنه شرط في حكم السبب لا في حكم العلة، فليس الحلّ كحفر البئر، بل هو كمن أرسل الدابة في الطريق، فجالت يُمنةً ويُسرةً، ثم أصابت شيئًا لم يضمنه المرسل؛ لأن فعله قد انقطع بالجولان أو الوقوف، ثم أنها أنشأت سيرًا آخر باختيارهما. (السنبلي)
مضاف إلخ لأن السوق والقود حمل على الذهاب كرها فينتقل فعل الدابة إلى السائق والقائد.(القمر)
And regarding when the condition is not prior to the cause, like entering the house in his saying: 'You are divorced if you enter the house'; it is subsequent to his utterance of the word 'you are divorced', so it is a pure condition falling under the first category. Similarly, if one unties a slave's shackle and he runs away, it is a condition for the running away; because the shackle was a preventer, so removing it is a condition. But between the release and the running away intervenes the act of a free agent, namely the slave, and this act is not attributed to the condition; because not everyone whose shackle is released necessarily runs away. This release precedes the running away, so it is in the category of causes; therefore, the releaser is not liable for the value of the slave. Unlike if he ordered the slave to run away, then the orderer is liable even though the act of a free agent intervenes; because ordering him to run away is using him, so when he runs away by his order, it is as if he usurped him by use. Unlike if the intervening means is attributed to the cause, then the owner of the cause is liable, like driving an animal and leading it; because the act of the animal, which is the destruction, is attributed to the driver and the leader; so they are liable for what it destroys. (Al-Qamar) says: it is a pure condition because it is devoid of the meaning of causality and causation. (Al-Qamar): But the intervention etc.: because the slave fled by his choice. (Al-Qamar): Because it is not necessary etc.: because the right of the master is a preventer of exit and running away. (Al-Qamar): Precedes the running away etc.: so the running away did not result from the release, so it is not attributed to it, so he is not liable. Running away is in reality the cause of destruction. The conclusion: the release, although in reality a condition, has the ruling of a cause; because the real cause precedes the existence of the effect, while the condition follows it, and this description applies to the release because it precedes the running away which is the cause of destruction, so it is established that it has the ruling of a cause. (Al-Sunbuliy): The ruling of causes, i.e., those which do not contain the meaning of cause. (Al-Qamar): 'He is not liable' etc., i.e., to the owner of the slave. This is when the slave is sane. But if he is insane, the releaser is liable for his value to the owner according to Muhammad (Allah have mercy on him). (Al-Qamar): 'He is liable' etc., because this cause is in the meaning of a cause. (Al-Qamar): 'Like driving an animal' etc.: because driving and leading are a cause having the ruling of a cause; because the effect occurs by them. Here it is not so; because the release was intervened by something that is an independent cause not arising from the condition, namely the running away. So the release is a pure cause without any meaning of cause at all. So it is established that it is a condition in the ruling of a cause, not in the ruling of a cause. So the release is not like digging a well, but like one who releases an animal on the road, and it wanders right and left, then hits something; the releaser is not liable because his act was cut off by the wandering or stopping, then it initiated another movement by its own choice. (Al-Sunbuliy): 'Attributed' etc.: because driving and leading force it to go against its will, so the act of the animal transfers to the driver and leader. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the distinction between a condition (shart) and a cause (sabab) in Hanafi usul. The author clarifies that a condition may be subsequent to the effect, yet still be a pure condition (shart mahd) rather than a cause. The example of divorce: 'You are divorced if you enter the house' – the condition of entering occurs after the pronouncement of divorce, but it is still a condition. The main example: releasing a slave's shackle leads to the slave running away. The release is a condition, but because the slave's free choice intervenes, the releaser is not liable. However, if he ordered the slave to run away, he is liable because the order is a cause in the sense of use. The commentary explains that the release has the ruling of a cause (hukm al-sabab) because it precedes the running away, but it is not a true cause; it's like releasing an animal that later causes damage on its own accord. The ruling differs if the slave is insane. This passage is a typical Hanafi usul analysis distinguishing between different categories of conditions.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition is something on which the existence of another thing depends, but it is not the cause (sabab) of that thing.
سبب (sabab): A cause is something that produces the effect directly, often through a medium.
علة (illa): The actual effective cause that brings about the effect; in this passage, the running away of the slave is the 'illa of loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a person who releases a slave's shackle not liable if the slave runs away?
A) Because the release is a cause of the running away
B) Because the slave's free act intervenes between the release and the running away
C) Because the release is a condition, not a cause
D) Because the release is subsequent to the running away

Key Takeaway
A condition that follows the cause but precedes the effect takes the ruling of a cause only in its temporal precedence, not in its causal efficacy; thus liability depends on whether a free agent's act intervenes.
