The Pure Sign (Alama Khalisa) as a Condition
Defines the condition that is a pure sign, like ihsaān in zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a condition that is a pure sign and distinguish it from a condition for existence or a cause.

Core Idea
A pure sign indicates the ruling without causing or conditioning it.

In Hanafi usul, conditions are categorized into types. One type is the 'pure sign' (alama khalisa) — a marker that shows a ruling applies but does not affect the act's existence or obligation. The example given is ihsan (being married) in zina, which triggers stoning but is not a condition for zina itself. This lesson unpacks that definition.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition
Find the phrase 'الخامس: شرط هو كالعلامة الخالصة'. This is the fifth type: a condition that is like a pure sign.
2
Understand the negation
The commentary says it is 'لا يتعلق بها وجود' (not attached to existence) and 'لا وجوب' (not attached to obligation). This distinguishes it from a condition (shart) and a cause (illa).
3
Identify its function
It is 'تعرف وجود الحكم' — it makes known the existence of the ruling. It is a sign, not a constituent.
4
Apply to the example
Ihsan in zina: it does not make zina exist (zina can occur without marriage), nor does it make zina obligatory. Rather, it indicates that the ruling of stoning applies.
Note: For the unmarried, the ruling is flogging, not stoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخامس: شرط هو كالعلامة الخالصة كالإحصان في الزنا (القمر) كالعلامة الخالصة: أي التي لا يتعلق بها وجود حتى يكون شرطًا ولا وجوب حتى يكون علة، بل هي تعرف وجود الحكم. (القمر)
And the fifth: a condition that is like a pure sign, like ihsaān (being married) in zina (adultery). (Al-Qamar): 'Like a pure sign': i.e., that which is not attached to existence so as to be a condition, nor to obligation so as to be a cause, but rather it indicates the existence of the ruling.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This is a definition of the fifth type of condition: the condition that is a pure sign (al-'alama al-khalisa). It is neither a condition upon which existence depends, nor a cause that creates obligation. Rather, it is a sign that indicates the presence of a ruling. The example given is ihsaān (being in a valid marriage) in the context of zina. In Hanafi law, ihsaān is not a condition for the act of zina itself, but it is a condition for the hadd punishment of stoning (rajm). Thus, ihsān indicates that the ruling of stoning applies. It is a pure sign, not a cause or condition for the act.

Key Terms
علامة خالصة (alama khalisa): A pure sign that indicates the ruling without being a condition or cause.
إحصان (ihsan): The state of being in a valid marriage; in the context of zina, it is a condition for stoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes a pure sign (alama khalisa) from other types of conditions?
A) It is a cause (sabab) for the ruling
B) It is necessary for the existence (wujud) of the act
C) It indicates (yu'arraf) the existence of the ruling without affecting existence or obligation
D) It is a condition for the obligation (wujub) of the act

Key Takeaway
The fifth type of condition is a pure sign that signals the applicability of a ruling without being a condition for the act or a cause for the obligation.

Explicit and Implicit Conditions in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the division of shart into explicit and implicit types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between explicit (sighah) and implicit (dalalah) conditions in Hanafi usul and apply the rule that implicit conditions only apply to indefinite nouns.

Core Idea
A condition may be explicit via 'if' or implicit via a description; the implicit form requires an indefinite noun.

In Hanafi usul, a condition (shart) is not always stated with conditional particles like 'if' or 'when'. Sometimes, a description in speech can imply conditionality, but this only works when the description modifies an indefinite noun. This lesson explains the two types and their rules, as elaborated by the classical commentators.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two ways to express a condition
Read the passage and note that conditions are known either by their explicit wording (sighah) — using conditional particles like 'in' (if) — or by indicative meaning (dalalah) through a description that implies conditionality.
Example of explicit: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced.' Example of implicit: 'The woman whom I marry is divorced.'
2
Distinguish between the two in terms of definiteness
The explicit condition works with both definite and indefinite subjects (e.g., 'this woman' or 'a woman'). The implicit condition only functions when the description occurs in an indefinite noun (not specified by pointing). If the subject is definite via pointing, the implicit condition is void.
The passage explains why: 'the description in the present is superfluous; pointing is more effective in definition.'
3
Understand the grammatical basis for the implicit condition
The implicit condition relies on the relative pronoun and the indefinite noun. In Arabic, when an indefinite noun is described by a verbal sentence (as in 'woman whom I marry'), it carries a conditional meaning. This is a recognized principle in nahw (grammar).
The commentary (al-Sanbali) cites grammarians: the indefinite described by a relative clause implies conditionality.
4
Apply the rule to a test case
Consider: 'This woman whom I marry is divorced.' Is the condition valid? According to the rule, it is not, because 'this woman' is definite by pointing. The statement becomes a direct divorce (if she is his wife) or void (if she is a stranger).
The text says: 'So it is void concerning an unrelated woman.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الأحكام
بيان شرط الحكم شرط للرجم في معنى العلامة، وقد عدّوا هذا تارةً في الشرط وتارةً في العلامة على ما سيجيء، ولذا لم يعده صاحب "التوضيح" من هذه الأقسام، ثم أنهم بينوا ضابطةً يعرف بها الفرق بين الشرط وما في معناه على ما قال:
أي من أقسام الشرط
إنما يعرف الشرط بصيغته كحروف الشرط مثل قوله: "إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق"، وفيه تنبيه على أن صيغة الشرط لا ينفك عن معنى الشرط قط.
إيراد كلمة الحصر أو دلالته، وهي الوصف الذي يكون في معنى الشرط كقوله : "المرأة التي أتزوجها طالق ثلاثا"، فإنه بمعنى الشرط دلالة لوقوع الوصف في النكرة، أي الامرأة الغير المعينة بالإشارة، لا النكرة النحوية؛ إذ هي معرفة باللام، فلما دخل وصف التزوّج في المنكرة وهو معتبر في الغائب يصلح دلالة على الشرط، فصار كأنه قال: "إن تزوجت امرأة فهي طالق" ولو وقع في المعين بأن يقول: "هذه المرأة التي أتزوّج فهي طالق". أي الوصف بالإشارة لما صلح دلالة على الشرط؛ لأن الوصف في الحاضر لغو؛ إذ الإشارة أبلغ في التعريف من الوصف، فكأنه قال: "هذه المرأة طالق"؛ فيلغو في الأجنبية.
في معنى العلامة : فإنه معرف ومظهر لحكم الزنا، وهو أنه حين وجد كان موجبًا للرجم والمعرّف علامة. (القمر) ولذا لم يعده أي الشرط الذي هو كالعلامة (القمر) عن معنى الشرط وهو وجود الحكم عند وجود الشرط. (القمر) أو دلالته أي يدل الكلام على التعليق دلالة كلمة الشرط عليه. (القمر)
أي الامرأة إلخ: دفع دخل، تقريره: أن لفظ المرأة في المتن معرفة، فكيف تفوّه المصنف الله بكونه نكرة؟(القمر) لا النكرة النحوية: جواب سؤال مقدّر تقريره أنا لا نسلّم وقوع الوصف في النكرة؛ لأن المرأة في قوله: المرأة التي إلخ، معرفة لا نكرة؟ فأجاب بأن المراد بالنكرة غير المعينة بالإشارة لا النحوية. (السنبلي) وهو معتبر إلخ لتعرف الغائب بالصفة. (القمر) يصلح إلخ : وهذه الدلالة حصلت من الموصول، فإن النحاة يقولون: النكرة الموصوفة بالجملة الفعلية والظرفية، أو الاسم الموصول الذي صلته جملة فعلية أو ظرفية أو الاسم الموصوف باسم الموصول المذكور إذا وقع مبتدأ يكون متضمنا لمعنى الشرط، ولذلك يجوز الفاء على خبره (السنبلي) فصار كأنه إلخ لأن ترتب الحكم على الوصف تعليق به كالشرط. (القمر) فيلغو في الأجنبية: أي فيلغو هذا القول إذا أشار به إلى الأجنبية؛ لأنها لا تصلح لمحلية الطلاق، فصادف الإيقاع بغير محله، فيلغو. (القمر)

فصل في الأحكام
بيان شرط الحكم
ونص الشرط يجمع الوجهين أي المعين وغير المعين حتى لو قال: "إن تزوجت امرأة فهي طالق" أو "إن تزوّجت هذه المرأة فهي طالق" يقع الطلاق بالتزوج في الصورتين. والرابع: العلامة، وهي ما يعرف الوجود من غير أن يتعلق به وجوب ولا وجود، أي وجود الحكم فقوله: "ما يعرف الوجود احتراز عن السبب؛ إذ هو مُفضِ لا معرف، وقوله: "من غير أن يتعلّق به وجوب احتراز عن العلة ولا وجود احتراز عن الشرط كالإحصان في باب الزنا، فإنه علامة للرجم، وهو عبارة عن كون الزاني حرًّا مسلما مكلفا وطئ بنكاح صحيح مرّةً، فالتكليف شرط في سائر الأحكام والحرية لتكميل العقوبة، وإنما العمدة ههنا هي الإسلام، والوطء بالنكاح الصحيح، وإنما جعلناه علامةً لا شرطًا؛ لأن الزنا إذا تحقق لا يتوقف انعقاده علة للرجم على إحصان يحدث بعده؛ إذ لو وجد الإحصان بعد الزنا لا يثبت بوجوده الرجم، بل يجب الجلد أي بعد الزنا
ونص الشرط أي صريح الشرط، وهو ما يكون بصيغته يجمع الوجهين بخلاف دلالة الشرط فإنها لا تجمع الوجهين، بل تختص بالنكرة لقصور هذه الدلالة، فإنها شرط معنى لا صيغةً. (القمر) والرابع: أي مما يتعلّق به الأحكام. (القمر) يعرف الوجود إلخ مثل التكبيرات في الصلاة إعلام على الانتقال من ركن إلى ركن، والأذان علم الصلاة، والتلبية علم شعار الحج ومثل رمضان في قول الرجل لامرأته أنت طالق قبل رمضان بشهر، فإنه معرف محض للزمان الذي يقع فيه الطلاق، وقد يُسمّى العلامة شرطًا، يعني بطريق المجاز، وذلك مثل الإحصان في باب الزنا، "تحقيق". (السنبلي) احتراز عن العلة لتوقف وجوب المعلول على العلة. (القمر) احتراز عن الشرط: فإنه يتوقف عليه وجود المشروط. (القمر) لتكميل العقوبة أي ليصير الكاملة. (القمر) وإنما العمدة ههنا إلخ : قال في "التحقيق": قيل: إحصان الزنا عبارة عن اجتماع سبعة أشياء: العقل، والبلوغ والحرية والنكاح الصحيح، والدخول بالنكاح ، وكون كل واحد من الزوجين مثل الآخر في صفة الإحصان والإسلام قال وقال شمس الأئمة بالله شرط الإحصان على الخصوص شيئان: الإسلام والدخول بالنكاح الصحيح بامرأة هي مثله، فأما العقل والبلوغ فهما شرطا الأهلية للعقوبة لا شرطا الإحصان على الخصوص، والحرية شرط تحصيل العقوبة. (السنبلي ههنا أي في خصوص شرط الإحصان. (القمر)
لا يتوقف إلخ أي كما يكون التوقف على حدوث الشرط.(القمر)
أهلاً للعقوبة
Chapter on Rulings. Explanation of the condition of a ruling: a condition for stoning is in the sense of a sign. They have counted this sometimes as condition and sometimes as sign as will come. Therefore the author of al-Tawdih did not count it among these divisions. Then they explained a rule by which the difference between a condition and what is in its meaning is known as he said: i.e., from the divisions of condition. A condition is known by its wording, like conditional particles, such as his statement: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced.' And in it is a warning that the conditional wording never separates from the meaning of condition. Or its indicative meaning, which is the description that is in the meaning of condition, like his statement: 'The woman whom I marry is divorced three times.' For it is in the meaning of condition by indication because the description occurs in the indefinite, i.e., the woman not specified by pointing, not the grammatical indefinite; for it is definite with the lam. So when the description of marriage entered into the indefinite – and it is considered in the absent – it is suitable as an indication of condition. So it becomes as if he said: 'If I marry a woman, she is divorced.' And if it occurs in the definite by saying: 'This woman whom I marry, she is divorced' – i.e., the description with pointing – it is not suitable as an indication of condition because the description in the present is superfluous; for pointing is more effective in definition than description. So it is as if he said: 'This woman is divorced'; so it is void concerning an unrelated woman. In the meaning of sign: for it is a definer and revealer of the ruling of adultery, namely that when it occurs it necessitates stoning, and the definer is a sign. (al-Qamar) And therefore he did not count it – i.e., the condition that is like a sign (al-Qamar) – from the meaning of condition, which is the existence of the ruling upon the existence of the condition. (al-Qamar) Or its indication: i.e., the speech indicates suspension with the indication of the conditional word upon it. (al-Qamar) i.e., the woman etc.: rebuttal of an objection. Its explanation: that the word 'woman' in the text is definite, so how did the author [؟] speak of it as indefinite? (al-Qamar) Not the grammatical indefinite: answer to an implied objection. Its explanation: we do not concede the occurrence of the description in the indefinite because the woman in his statement 'the woman who...' is definite not indefinite. So he answered that what is meant by indefinite is that which is not specified by pointing, not the grammatical indefinite. (al-Sanbali) And it is considered etc.: to define the absent by the attribute. (al-Qamar) It is suitable etc.: And this indication is obtained from the relative pronoun, for grammarians say: the indefinite described by a verbal or circumstantial sentence, or the relative pronoun whose connecting sentence is verbal or circumstantial, or the noun described by the mentioned relative pronoun, when it occurs as a subject, it implies a conditional meaning. Therefore the fa' is permissible in its predicate. (al-Sanbali) So it becomes as if he said etc.: because the attachment of the ruling to the description is a suspension by it like the condition. (al-Qamar) So it is void concerning an unrelated woman: i.e., this statement is void if he points to an unrelated woman because she is not fit for the locus of divorce, so it meets effectuation without its place, so it is void. (al-Qamar) Chapter on Rulings. Explanation of the condition of a ruling: And the explicit condition combines the two aspects – i.e., the definite and indefinite – such that if he says: 'If I marry a woman, she is divorced' or 'If I marry this woman, she is divorced', the divorce falls due to marriage in both cases. And the fourth: the sign, which is that which indicates existence without there being attached to it obligation nor existence – i.e., existence of the ruling. So his statement: 'which indicates existence' excludes the cause; for it is a means, not a definer. And his statement: 'without there being attached to it obligation' excludes the effective cause, and 'nor existence' excludes the condition. Like ihsan in the chapter of adultery, for it is a sign for stoning, and it is the fact that the adulterer is free, Muslim, legally responsible, having had intercourse in a valid marriage once. So legal responsibility is a condition in all rulings and freedom is for perfecting the punishment. But the main point here is Islam and intercourse in a valid marriage. And we made it a sign not a condition because when adultery is realized, its being an effective cause for stoning is not contingent upon ihsan that occurs afterwards; for if ihsan occurs after adultery, stoning is not established by its existence, but rather lashes are wajib after adultery. And the explicit condition – i.e., the explicit condition, which is that which is in its wording – combines the two aspects, unlike the indication of condition, for it does not combine the two aspects but is specific to the indefinite due to the weakness of this indication; for it is a condition in meaning not wording. (al-Qamar) And the fourth: i.e., of those things related to rulings. (al-Qamar) It indicates existence etc., like the takbirat in prayer as signs of moving from one pillar to another, and the adhan as a sign of prayer, and talbiyah as a sign of the ritual of Hajj, and like Ramadan in a man's statement to his wife: 'You are divorced a month before Ramadan' for it is a pure definer of the time in which divorce occurs. And sometimes the sign is called a condition, metaphorically, such as ihsan in the chapter of adultery, 'tahqiq'. (al-Sanbali) It excludes the effective cause because the wajib of the effect depends on the effective cause. (al-Qamar) It excludes the condition because the existence of the conditioned depends on it. (al-Qamar) To perfect the punishment: i.e., to make it complete. (al-Qamar) And the main point here etc.: He said in al-Tahqiq: It is said: ihsan in adultery consists of the gathering of seven things: intellect, puberty, freedom, valid marriage, consummation, and that each of the spouses is like the other in the quality of ihsan and Islam. He said: And Shams al-A'imma said: the condition of ihsan specifically are two things: Islam and consummation in a valid marriage with a woman who is like him. As for intellect and puberty, they are conditions of legal capacity for punishment, not conditions of ihsan specifically. And freedom is a condition for achieving the punishment. (al-Sanbali) Here: i.e., specifically concerning the condition of ihsan. (al-Qamar) It is not contingent etc.: i.e., as contingency is upon the occurrence of the condition. (al-Qamar) Eligible for punishment.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the classification of conditions and signs in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by explaining that a 'shart' (condition) in legal rulings can be known by its explicit wording (sighah) like 'if' or 'when' in conditional sentences, or by its indicative meaning (dalalah) through a description that implies conditionality, e.g., 'the woman whom I marry...' which functions like 'if I marry a woman...'. The commentary distinguishes between shart bi as-sighah (explicit condition) which covers both definite and indefinite subjects, and shart bi ad-dalalah (implicit condition) which only applies to indefinite nouns because indefinite descriptions carry a conditional sense. The author then discusses the fourth category: al-`alamah (the sign), which indicates the existence of a ruling without causing it. An example is ihsan (being a free married Muslim) in the law of stoning for adultery – it is a sign that stoning is due, but not a condition because the ruling of stoning does not depend on it occurring after the act. The text also explains that the explicit condition (nass as-shart) combines both definite and indefinite cases, unlike the implicit condition. The commentary by Qamar and al-Sanbali clarifies points of grammar and fiqh, ensuring that the student understands the precise legal reasoning behind the classification. This passage is fundamental for understanding how Hanafi jurists categorize the elements that attach to rulings and how they differ from causes and signs.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): Something upon which the existence of a ruling depends, known by its wording (e.g., 'if') or by indication through a description.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi usul, when does a description (e.g., 'whom I marry') function as an implicit condition?
A) When it modifies any noun, definite or indefinite
B) When it modifies an indefinite noun that is not specified by pointing
C) When it is used with a conditional particle
D) When it modifies a definite noun with the definite article

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a condition may be expressed explicitly via conditional particles or implicitly via a description on an indefinite noun; the implicit type is limited to non-pointed nouns.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
The Sign (`Alamah) and Its Distinction from Condition
Defining `alamah and explaining the example of ihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define `alamah (sign) in Hanafi usul and explain why ihsan is a sign for stoning and not a condition.

Core Idea
A sign indicates the existence of a ruling without causing it or being required for its existence.

In addition to conditions, Hanafi jurists identify a category called `alamah (sign) — a marker that the ruling exists but does not cause or condition it. The classic example is ihsan (being a free married Muslim) in the law of stoning for adultery. This lesson covers the definition, examples, and the distinction from condition and cause, as explained in the passage.

Guided Path
1
Define `alamah according to the text
The passage defines `alamah as 'that which indicates existence without there being attached to it obligation nor existence' meaning it does not necessitate the ruling and the ruling does not depend on it. It is a definer (mu'arraf) of the existence of the ruling.
The definition excludes sabab (cause), `illah (effective cause), and shart (condition).
2
Examine the example: ihsan for stoning
Ihsan (being a free, Muslim, married adult who has consummated marriage) is considered a sign that stoning is the punishment for adultery. It does not cause stoning (the act of adultery causes it), nor is stoning contingent on ihsan occurring after the act.
The text says: 'when adultery is realized, its being an effective cause for stoning is not contingent upon ihsan that occurs afterwards.'
3
Understand why ihsan is not a condition
A condition must exist simultaneously with the ruling or precede it. In the case of ihsan, if a person commits adultery and later becomes muhsan (e.g., marries), stoning is not applied for that earlier adultery; only lashes are due. Thus, ihsan is not a condition for stoning. It is a sign that when adultery occurs by a muhsan, stoning is the appropriate punishment.
The text uses the phrase 'لا يتوقف انعقاده علة للرجم على إحصان يحدث بعده' (its being an effective cause for stoning is not contingent upon ihsan that occurs afterwards).
4
Distinguish `alamah from other categories
Using the definitions: sabab (cause) leads to the ruling (e.g., adultery is cause of stoning), `illah (effective cause) necessitates the ruling (e.g., the `illah for stoning is the act of adultery with specific attributes), shart (condition) is required for the ruling to exist (e.g., legal capacity is a condition for punishment). `Alamah merely indicates which ruling applies once the cause is present.
Other examples mentioned: takbirat in prayer as signs of transition, adhan as sign of prayer time, talbiyah as sign of ihram.

فصل في الأحكام
بيان شرط الحكم شرط للرجم في معنى العلامة، وقد عدّوا هذا تارةً في الشرط وتارةً في العلامة على ما سيجيء، ولذا لم يعده صاحب "التوضيح" من هذه الأقسام، ثم أنهم بينوا ضابطةً يعرف بها الفرق بين الشرط وما في معناه على ما قال:
أي من أقسام الشرط
إنما يعرف الشرط بصيغته كحروف الشرط مثل قوله: "إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق"، وفيه تنبيه على أن صيغة الشرط لا ينفك عن معنى الشرط قط.
إيراد كلمة الحصر أو دلالته، وهي الوصف الذي يكون في معنى الشرط كقوله : "المرأة التي أتزوجها طالق ثلاثا"، فإنه بمعنى الشرط دلالة لوقوع الوصف في النكرة، أي الامرأة الغير المعينة بالإشارة، لا النكرة النحوية؛ إذ هي معرفة باللام، فلما دخل وصف التزوّج في المنكرة وهو معتبر في الغائب يصلح دلالة على الشرط، فصار كأنه قال: "إن تزوجت امرأة فهي طالق" ولو وقع في المعين بأن يقول: "هذه المرأة التي أتزوّج فهي طالق". أي الوصف بالإشارة لما صلح دلالة على الشرط؛ لأن الوصف في الحاضر لغو؛ إذ الإشارة أبلغ في التعريف من الوصف، فكأنه قال: "هذه المرأة طالق"؛ فيلغو في الأجنبية.
في معنى العلامة : فإنه معرف ومظهر لحكم الزنا، وهو أنه حين وجد كان موجبًا للرجم والمعرّف علامة. (القمر) ولذا لم يعده أي الشرط الذي هو كالعلامة (القمر) عن معنى الشرط وهو وجود الحكم عند وجود الشرط. (القمر) أو دلالته أي يدل الكلام على التعليق دلالة كلمة الشرط عليه. (القمر)
أي الامرأة إلخ: دفع دخل، تقريره: أن لفظ المرأة في المتن معرفة، فكيف تفوّه المصنف الله بكونه نكرة؟(القمر) لا النكرة النحوية: جواب سؤال مقدّر تقريره أنا لا نسلّم وقوع الوصف في النكرة؛ لأن المرأة في قوله: المرأة التي إلخ، معرفة لا نكرة؟ فأجاب بأن المراد بالنكرة غير المعينة بالإشارة لا النحوية. (السنبلي) وهو معتبر إلخ لتعرف الغائب بالصفة. (القمر) يصلح إلخ : وهذه الدلالة حصلت من الموصول، فإن النحاة يقولون: النكرة الموصوفة بالجملة الفعلية والظرفية، أو الاسم الموصول الذي صلته جملة فعلية أو ظرفية أو الاسم الموصوف باسم الموصول المذكور إذا وقع مبتدأ يكون متضمنا لمعنى الشرط، ولذلك يجوز الفاء على خبره (السنبلي) فصار كأنه إلخ لأن ترتب الحكم على الوصف تعليق به كالشرط. (القمر) فيلغو في الأجنبية: أي فيلغو هذا القول إذا أشار به إلى الأجنبية؛ لأنها لا تصلح لمحلية الطلاق، فصادف الإيقاع بغير محله، فيلغو. (القمر)

فصل في الأحكام
بيان شرط الحكم
ونص الشرط يجمع الوجهين أي المعين وغير المعين حتى لو قال: "إن تزوجت امرأة فهي طالق" أو "إن تزوّجت هذه المرأة فهي طالق" يقع الطلاق بالتزوج في الصورتين. والرابع: العلامة، وهي ما يعرف الوجود من غير أن يتعلق به وجوب ولا وجود، أي وجود الحكم فقوله: "ما يعرف الوجود احتراز عن السبب؛ إذ هو مُفضِ لا معرف، وقوله: "من غير أن يتعلّق به وجوب احتراز عن العلة ولا وجود احتراز عن الشرط كالإحصان في باب الزنا، فإنه علامة للرجم، وهو عبارة عن كون الزاني حرًّا مسلما مكلفا وطئ بنكاح صحيح مرّةً، فالتكليف شرط في سائر الأحكام والحرية لتكميل العقوبة، وإنما العمدة ههنا هي الإسلام، والوطء بالنكاح الصحيح، وإنما جعلناه علامةً لا شرطًا؛ لأن الزنا إذا تحقق لا يتوقف انعقاده علة للرجم على إحصان يحدث بعده؛ إذ لو وجد الإحصان بعد الزنا لا يثبت بوجوده الرجم، بل يجب الجلد أي بعد الزنا
ونص الشرط أي صريح الشرط، وهو ما يكون بصيغته يجمع الوجهين بخلاف دلالة الشرط فإنها لا تجمع الوجهين، بل تختص بالنكرة لقصور هذه الدلالة، فإنها شرط معنى لا صيغةً. (القمر) والرابع: أي مما يتعلّق به الأحكام. (القمر) يعرف الوجود إلخ مثل التكبيرات في الصلاة إعلام على الانتقال من ركن إلى ركن، والأذان علم الصلاة، والتلبية علم شعار الحج ومثل رمضان في قول الرجل لامرأته أنت طالق قبل رمضان بشهر، فإنه معرف محض للزمان الذي يقع فيه الطلاق، وقد يُسمّى العلامة شرطًا، يعني بطريق المجاز، وذلك مثل الإحصان في باب الزنا، "تحقيق". (السنبلي) احتراز عن العلة لتوقف وجوب المعلول على العلة. (القمر) احتراز عن الشرط: فإنه يتوقف عليه وجود المشروط. (القمر) لتكميل العقوبة أي ليصير الكاملة. (القمر) وإنما العمدة ههنا إلخ : قال في "التحقيق": قيل: إحصان الزنا عبارة عن اجتماع سبعة أشياء: العقل، والبلوغ والحرية والنكاح الصحيح، والدخول بالنكاح ، وكون كل واحد من الزوجين مثل الآخر في صفة الإحصان والإسلام قال وقال شمس الأئمة بالله شرط الإحصان على الخصوص شيئان: الإسلام والدخول بالنكاح الصحيح بامرأة هي مثله، فأما العقل والبلوغ فهما شرطا الأهلية للعقوبة لا شرطا الإحصان على الخصوص، والحرية شرط تحصيل العقوبة. (السنبلي ههنا أي في خصوص شرط الإحصان. (القمر)
لا يتوقف إلخ أي كما يكون التوقف على حدوث الشرط.(القمر)

(al-Qamar) And the main point here etc.: He said in al-Tahqiq: It is said: ihsan in adultery consists of the gathering of seven things: intellect, puberty, freedom, valid marriage, consummation, and that each of the spouses is like the other in the quality of ihsan and Islam. He said: And Shams al-A'imma said: the condition of ihsan specifically are two things: Islam and consummation in a valid marriage with a woman who is like him. As for intellect and puberty, they are conditions of legal capacity for punishment, not conditions of ihsan specifically. And freedom is a condition for achieving the punishment. (al-Sanbali) Here: i.e., specifically concerning the condition of ihsan. (al-Qamar) It is not contingent etc.: i.e., as contingency is upon the occurrence of the condition. (al-Qamar) Eligible for punishment.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the classification of conditions and signs in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by explaining that a 'shart' (condition) in legal rulings can be known by its explicit wording (sighah) like 'if' or 'when' in conditional sentences, or by its indicative meaning (dalalah) through a description that implies conditionality, e.g., 'the woman whom I marry...' which functions like 'if I marry a woman...'. The commentary distinguishes between shart bi as-sighah (explicit condition) which covers both definite and indefinite subjects, and shart bi ad-dalalah (implicit condition) which only applies to indefinite nouns because indefinite descriptions carry a conditional sense. The author then discusses the fourth category: al-`alamah (the sign), which indicates the existence of a ruling without causing it. An example is ihsan (being a free married Muslim) in the law of stoning for adultery – it is a sign that stoning is due, but not a condition because the ruling of stoning does not depend on it occurring after the act. The text also explains that the explicit condition (nass as-shart) combines both definite and indefinite cases, unlike the implicit condition. The commentary by Qamar and al-Sanbali clarifies points of grammar and fiqh, ensuring that the student understands the precise legal reasoning behind the classification. This passage is fundamental for understanding how Hanafi jurists categorize the elements that attach to rulings and how they differ from causes and signs.

Key Terms
علامة (`alamah): A sign that indicates the existence of a ruling without being a condition or cause; e.g., ihsan in stoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is ihsan considered a sign (`alamah) and not a condition for stoning in Hanafi usul?
A) Because stoning is not contingent upon ihsan occurring after the act
B) Because ihsan is required for the validity of stoning
C) Because ihsan causes the stoning
D) Because ihsan is defined by the judge

Key Takeaway
A sign (`alamah) indicates a ruling but does not cause it nor condition it; ihsan is a sign for stoning because stoning is not contingent on ihsan occurring after adultery.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Definition of Al-ʿAlāmah (The Sign) in Hanafi Usul
Defining ʿalāmah and distinguishing it from other indicators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ʿalāmah and distinguish it from sabab, ʿillah, and sharṭ.

Core Idea
A sign indicates existence without causing or conditioning it.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the fourth category among the things related to a ruling (aḥkām) is the sign (ʿalāmah). Unlike a cause (sabab) that produces the ruling, an effective cause (ʿillah) that necessitates it, or a condition (sharṭ) on which its existence depends, a sign merely makes known that the ruling exists when the sign is present. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly analyzing how rulings are attached to their indicators.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of ʿalāmah
Locate the Arabic definition: 'ما يعرف الوجود من غير أن يتعلق به وجوب ولا وجود'. Parse each part.
The definition has three exclusions: (1) from sabab, (2) from ʿillah, (3) from sharṭ.
2
Apply the exclusions
Explain why 'by which existence is known' excludes sabab (cause), 'without obligation' excludes ʿillah, 'without existence' excludes sharṭ.
This is the core analytical move.
3
Examine the examples
Study the examples: takbīr as sign of transition, adhān as sign of prayer time, talbiyah as sign of Hajj rites, and the phrase 'divorced one month before Ramadan' as a pure time indicator.
These reinforce that a sign does not affect the ruling.
4
Contrast with iḥṣān dispute
Though iḥṣān is used as the primary example, the full dispute is in the next lesson. Here, note that some hold iḥṣān as a sign.

بيان شرط الحكم
ونص الشرط يجمع الوجهين أي المعين وغير المعين حتى لو قال: "إن تزوجت امرأة فهي طالق" أو "إن تزوّجت هذه المرأة فهي طالق" يقع الطلاق بالتزوج في الصورتين. والرابع: العلامة، وهي ما يعرف الوجود من غير أن يتعلق به وجوب ولا وجود، أي وجود الحكم. فقوله: "ما يعرف الوجود احتراز عن السبب؛ إذ هو مُفضِ لا معرف، وقوله: "من غير أن يتعلّق به وجوب احتراز عن العلة ولا وجود احتراز عن الشرط كالإحصان في باب الزنا، فإنه علامة للرجم، وهو عبارة عن كون الزاني حرًّا مسلما مكلفا وطئ بنكاح صحيح مرّةً، فالتكليف شرط في سائر الأحكام والحرية لتكميل العقوبة، وإنما العمدة ههنا هي الإسلام، والوطء بالنكاح الصحيح، وإنما جعلناه علامةً لا شرطًا؛ لأن الزنا إذا تحقق لا يتوقف انعقاده علة للرجم على إحصان يحدث بعده؛ إذ لو وجد الإحصان بعد الزنا لا يثبت بوجوده الرجم، بل يجب الجلد. ونص الشرط أي صريح الشرط، وهو ما يكون بصيغته يجمع الوجهين بخلاف دلالة الشرط فإنها لا تجمع الوجهين، بل تختص بالنكرة لقصور هذه الدلالة، فإنها شرط معنى لا صيغةً. (القمر) والرابع: أي مما يتعلّق به الأحكام. (القمر) يعرف الوجود إلخ مثل التكبيرات في الصلاة إعلام على الانتقال من ركن إلى ركن، والأذان علم الصلاة، والتلبية علم شعار الحج ومثل رمضان في قول الرجل لامرأته أنت طالق قبل رمضان بشهر، فإنه معرف محض للزمان الذي يقع فيه الطلاق، وقد يُسمّى العلامة شرطًا، يعني بطريق المجاز، وذلك مثل الإحصان في باب الزنا، "تحقيق". (السنبلي) احتراز عن العلة لتوقف وجوب المعلول على العلة. (القمر) احتراز عن الشرط: فإنه يتوقف عليه وجود المشروط. (القمر) لتكميل العقوبة أي ليصير الكاملة. (القمر) وإنما العمدة ههنا إلخ : قال في "التحقيق": قيل: إحصان الزنا عبارة عن اجتماع سبعة أشياء: العقل، والبلوغ والحرية والنكاح الصحيح، والدخول بالنكاح ، وكون كل واحد من الزوجين مثل الآخر في صفة الإحصان والإسلام قال وقال شمس الأئمة بالله شرط الإحصان على الخصوص شيئان: الإسلام والدخول بالنكاح الصحيح بامرأة هي مثله، فأما العقل والبلوغ فهما شرطا الأهلية للعقوبة لا شرطا الإحصان على الخصوص، والحرية شرط تحصيل العقوبة. (السنبلي ههنا أي في خصوص شرط الإحصان. (القمر) لا يتوقف إلخ أي كما يكون التوقف على حدوث الشرط.(القمر) أهلاً للعقوبة
وعدم كونه علة وسببًا ،ظاهر فعلم أنه عبارة عن حال في الزاني يصير به الزنا في تلك الحالة موجبًا للرجم، وهو معنى كونه علامة، وهذا عند بعض المتأخرين، ومختار الأكثر أنه الإحصان شرط لوجوب الرجم؛ لأن الشرط ما يتوقف عليه وجود الحكم والإحصان بهذه المثابة؛ إذ الزنا لا يوجب الرجم بدونه كالسرقة لا توجب القطع بدون النصاب حتى لا يضمن شهوده إذا رجعوا بحال، تفريع على كون الإحصان علامةً لا شرطًا، يعني إذا رجع شهود الإحصان بعد الرجم لا يضمنون دية المرجوم بحال أي سواء رجعوا وحدهم أو مع شهود الزنا أيضًا؛ لأنه علامة لا يتعلق بها وجوب ولا وجود ولا يجوز إضافة الحكم إليه، الإحصان بخلاف ما إذا اجتمع شهود الشرط والعلة بأن شهد اثنان بقوله: "إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق" وشهد اثنان بدخول الدار ، ثم رجع شهود الشرط وحدهم، فإنهم يضمنون عند بعض المشايخ؛ لأن الشرط صالح لخلافة العلة عند تعذر إضافة الحكم إليها لتعلق الوجود به وثبوت التعدّي منهم، وهو مختار فخر الإسلام ، وعند شمس الأئمة: لا ضمان. وعدم كونه أي الإحصان علة وسببًا ظاهر؛ لأنه ليس مؤثر في الرجم ولا هو طريق مفض إليه.(القمر) ظاهر إلخ وهو أنه ليس بطريق مفض إليه، فعرفنا أن الرجم غير مضاف إليه وجوبًا ولا جودًا، ولكنه عبارة عن حال في الزاني يصير الزنا في تلك الحالة موجبًا للرجم، فكان معرفًا أن الزنا حين وجد كان موجبا للرجم، فكان علامة لا شرطا . (السنبلي عن حال إلخ وهو كون الزاني حرا مسلما كما مر . (القمر) أنه شرط إلخ فشهود الإحصان إذا رجعوا يضمنون لإضافة التلف بالرجم إلى هذه الشهود.(القمر) والإحصان بهذه المثابة : فإن وجوب الرجم يتوقف عليه. (القمر) أو مع شهود الزنا إلخ: قبل القضاء أو بعده؛ لأنهم كانوا شهود العلامة والعلامة لا يتعلّق بها وجود ولا وجوب فلا يجوز إضافة الحكم إليها بوجه، فإذا لم يضف الرجم إلى العلامة وهو الإحصان فشهود الإحصان بريئون عنه، فلا ضمان عليهم (السنبلي) وجوب ولا وجود أي وجوب الحكم وهو الرجم ولا وجوده. (القمر) إن دخلت إلخ: أي بأن الزوج علق طلاقها على دخول الدار وهي غير موطوءة. (القمر) فإنهم يضمنون: أي الزوج ما أدّاه المرأة من نصف المهر. (القمر) وعند شمس الأئمة وعامة المحققين منهم أبو اليسر. (القمر)
Chapter on Rulings. Explanation of the Condition of the Ruling. The explicit wording of the condition combines both aspects, i.e., the specific and the non-specific, so that if he says, 'If I marry a woman, she is divorced,' or 'If I marry this woman, she is divorced,' divorce occurs with marriage in both cases. The fourth: the sign, which is that by which existence is known without any obligation or existence being attached to it, i.e., the existence of the ruling. His statement: 'by which existence is known' excludes the cause, because it is a means of bringing about, not a mere indicator; and his statement: 'without any obligation being attached to it' excludes the effective cause, and 'without any existence being attached to it' excludes the condition, like iḥṣān in the chapter of adultery, for it is a sign for stoning, and it is the description of the adulterer being free, Muslim, legally responsible, having had intercourse in a valid marriage once. So legal responsibility is a condition in all rulings, and freedom is to complete the punishment, but the main point here is Islam and intercourse in a valid marriage. We have made it a sign, not a condition, because when adultery occurs, its being a cause for stoning does not depend on an iḥṣān that occurs thereafter; for if iḥṣān occurs after adultery, stoning is not established by its occurrence; rather, flogging becomes obligatory. The explicit wording of the condition, i.e., the explicit condition, which by its wording combines both aspects, unlike the indication of the condition, which does not combine both aspects, but is specific to the indefinite noun due to the deficiency of this indication, for it is a condition in meaning not in wording. (al-Qamar) 'The fourth' i.e., of the things related to rulings. (al-Qamar) 'by which existence is known' etc., like the takbīr in prayer as a sign of transition from one pillar to another, the adhān as a sign of prayer, the talbiyah as a sign of the rites of Hajj, and like Ramadan in the statement of a man to his wife 'you are divorced one month before Ramadan,' for it is a pure indicator of the time in which divorce occurs, and sometimes the sign is called a condition, metaphorically, like iḥṣān in the chapter of adultery. (al-Sanbalī) 'excludes the effective cause' because the obligation of the effect depends on the effective cause. (al-Qamar) 'excludes the condition' because the existence of the conditioned depends on it. (al-Qamar) 'to complete the punishment' i.e., to make it complete. (al-Qamar) 'The main point here' etc.: He said in al-Taḥqīq: It is said: iḥṣān in adultery is the combination of seven things: intellect, puberty, freedom, valid marriage, consummation of marriage, each of the spouses being like the other in the description of iḥṣān, and Islam. He said: And Shams al-A'imma said: those conditions of iḥṣān in particular are two things: Islam and consummation in a valid marriage with a woman like him. As for intellect and puberty, they are conditions for legal capacity for punishment, not conditions of iḥṣān in particular; and freedom is a condition for achieving the punishment. (al-Sanbalī) 'here' i.e., in the particular conditions of iḥṣān. (al-Qamar) 'does not depend' etc. i.e., just as dependence occurs upon the occurrence of the condition. (al-Qamar) 'capacity for punishment'
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a definition and distinction of the 'sign' (ʿalāmah) among the things related to a ruling (aḥkām). It begins by reiterating that the explicit wording of a condition (sharṭ) can cover both unspecified and specified matters, as in conditional divorce. The fourth category after cause (sabab), condition (sharṭ), and effective cause (ʿillah) is the sign (ʿalāmah), defined as something that indicates the existence of a ruling without having any bearing on its obligation (wujūb) or existence (wujūd). The commentator explains each qualification: 'indicates existence' excludes the cause because a cause actually produces the ruling; 'without obligation' excludes the effective cause (ʿillah) because the obligation of the effect depends on it; 'without existence' excludes the condition (sharṭ) because the existence of the conditioned depends on it. The example given is iḥṣān in zina, which is a description of the adulterer (being free, Muslim, legally responsible, having had valid intercourse). Some scholars hold iḥṣān to be a sign (ʿalāmah) for the obligation of stoning (rajm), not a condition, because if iḥṣān occurs after zina, stoning does not apply; only flogging does. This shows that iḥṣān is not a condition for the existence of the ruling but only indicates that at the time of zina, the circumstances were such that stoning is due. The passage then notes a dispute among later scholars (mutaʾakhkhirūn): some still consider iḥṣān a sign, but the majority (al-akthar) choose that it is a condition (sharṭ) for the obligation of rajm, because stoning depends on its presence. The practical difference appears in witness liability: if iḥṣān is a sign, witnesses of iḥṣān who retract after stoning are not liable for the blood money (diyah), because the sign is not a cause to which the ruling can be attributed. But if iḥṣān is a condition, then witnesses of the condition become liable according to some mashāyikh (like Fakhr al-Islam), because the condition can substitute for the cause when attribution is difficult. However, Shams al-A'imma and many scholars hold that condition witnesses are not liable. The text clarifies that even though iḥṣān is often called a condition metaphorically, technically it is a sign. The passage uses examples like takbīr in prayer (sign of transition), adhān (sign of prayer time), and the statement 'you are divorced one month before Ramadan' (sign of a specific time).

Key Terms
العلامة (al-ʿalāmah): ما يعرف الوجود من غير أن يتعلق به وجوب ولا وجود: that by which existence is known without any obligation or existence being attached to it.
الشرط (al-sharṭ): ما يتوقف عليه وجود المشروط: that on which the existence of the conditioned depends.
الإحصان (al-iḥṣān): حال في الزاني يصير به الزنا في تلك الحالة موجبًا للرجم: a state in the adulterer by which zina in that state becomes a cause for stoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary difference between a sign (ʿalāmah) and a condition (sharṭ)?
A) A sign is always explicit while a condition is implicit.
B) A sign indicates existence without affecting obligation or existence, while a condition is necessary for existence.
C) A sign only applies to indefinite nouns, while a condition applies to definite ones.
D) A sign is used only in family law, while a condition is used in criminal law.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of ʿalāmah is a precise usul tool: it indicates the existence of a ruling without any causal or conditional relation.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
10 min
Is Iḥṣān a Sign or Condition? A Hanafi Usul Dispute
Dispute over iḥṣān as sign or condition with thamarah al-khilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the two Hanafi positions on iḥṣān and evaluate the practical consequence in witness liability.

Core Idea
Whether iḥṣān is a sign or condition determines who pays diyah after a retraction.

One of the most instructive applications of the sign (ʿalāmah) definition is the dispute over iḥṣān (being muhṣan) in the law of stoning (rajm). Some early Hanafis treated iḥṣān as a mere sign that stoning is due when zina occurs, while later majority scholars argued it is a condition. The difference becomes concrete when the witnesses of iḥṣān retract: if it is a sign, they owe nothing; if a condition, some say they must pay the blood money.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the early view (iḥṣān is a sign) and the later majority view (iḥṣān is a condition).
The early view is attributed to 'some later scholars' (baʿḍ al-mutaʾakhkhirīn), while the mukhtār al-akthar is that it is a condition.
2
Examine the proofs for the sign position
The key proof: if iḥṣān were a condition, then if it occurs after zina, rajm would become obligatory, but it does not; only flogging becomes obligatory.
This shows iḥṣān is not necessary for the existence of rajm at the moment of zina.
3
Examine the proofs for the condition position
The majority argue that rajm depends on iḥṣān, just as amputation depends on nisāb in theft. Without iḥṣān, no rajm.
This treats iḥṣān as a condition for the obligation.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is in witness liability. If sign, no liability; if condition, liability arises according to some (Fakhr al-Islam) but not according to Shams al-A'imma.
This dispute shows how a usul classification affects legal consequences.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text states that the majority choice is that iḥṣān is a condition, but the issue is not fully settled.
Note the nuanced layers of ikhtilaf within the school.

(القمر) وإنما العمدة ههنا إلخ : قال في "التحقيق": قيل: إحصان الزنا عبارة عن اجتماع سبعة أشياء: العقل، والبلوغ والحرية والنكاح الصحيح، والدخول بالنكاح ، وكون كل واحد من الزوجين مثل الآخر في صفة الإحصان والإسلام قال وقال شمس الأئمة بالله شرط الإحصان على الخصوص شيئان: الإسلام والدخول بالنكاح الصحيح بامرأة هي مثله، فأما العقل والبلوغ فهما شرطا الأهلية للعقوبة لا شرطا الإحصان على الخصوص، والحرية شرط تحصيل العقوبة. (السنبلي ههنا أي في خصوص شرط الإحصان. (القمر) لا يتوقف إلخ أي كما يكون التوقف على حدوث الشرط.(القمر) أهلاً للعقوبة
وعدم كونه علة وسببًا ،ظاهر فعلم أنه عبارة عن حال في الزاني يصير به الزنا في تلك الحالة موجبًا للرجم، وهو معنى كونه علامة، وهذا عند بعض المتأخرين، ومختار الأكثر أنه الإحصان شرط لوجوب الرجم؛ لأن الشرط ما يتوقف عليه وجود الحكم والإحصان بهذه المثابة؛ إذ الزنا لا يوجب الرجم بدونه كالسرقة لا توجب القطع بدون النصاب حتى لا يضمن شهوده إذا رجعوا بحال، تفريع على كون الإحصان علامةً لا شرطًا، يعني إذا رجع شهود الإحصان بعد الرجم لا يضمنون دية المرجوم بحال أي سواء رجعوا وحدهم أو مع شهود الزنا أيضًا؛ لأنه علامة لا يتعلق بها وجوب ولا وجود ولا يجوز إضافة الحكم إليه، الإحصان بخلاف ما إذا اجتمع شهود الشرط والعلة بأن شهد اثنان بقوله: "إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق" وشهد اثنان بدخول الدار ، ثم رجع شهود الشرط وحدهم، فإنهم يضمنون عند بعض المشايخ؛ لأن الشرط صالح لخلافة العلة عند تعذر إضافة الحكم إليها لتعلق الوجود به وثبوت التعدّي منهم، وهو مختار فخر الإسلام ، وعند شمس الأئمة: لا ضمان. وعدم كونه أي الإحصان علة وسببًا ظاهر؛ لأنه ليس مؤثر في الرجم ولا هو طريق مفض إليه.(القمر) ظاهر إلخ وهو أنه ليس بطريق مفض إليه، فعرفنا أن الرجم غير مضاف إليه وجوبًا ولا جودًا، ولكنه عبارة عن حال في الزاني يصير الزنا في تلك الحالة موجبًا للرجم، فكان معرفًا أن الزنا حين وجد كان موجبا للرجم، فكان علامة لا شرطا . (السنبلي عن حال إلخ وهو كون الزاني حرا مسلما كما مر . (القمر) أنه شرط إلخ فشهود الإحصان إذا رجعوا يضمنون لإضافة التلف بالرجم إلى هذه الشهود.(القمر) والإحصان بهذه المثابة : فإن وجوب الرجم يتوقف عليه. (القمر) أو مع شهود الزنا إلخ: قبل القضاء أو بعده؛ لأنهم كانوا شهود العلامة والعلامة لا يتعلّق بها وجود ولا وجوب فلا يجوز إضافة الحكم إليها بوجه، فإذا لم يضف الرجم إلى العلامة وهو الإحصان فشهود الإحصان بريئون عنه، فلا ضمان عليهم (السنبلي) وجوب ولا وجود أي وجوب الحكم وهو الرجم ولا وجوده. (القمر) إن دخلت إلخ: أي بأن الزوج علق طلاقها على دخول الدار وهي غير موطوءة. (القمر) فإنهم يضمنون: أي الزوج ما أدّاه المرأة من نصف المهر. (القمر) وعند شمس الأئمة وعامة المحققين منهم أبو اليسر. (القمر)
Chapter on Rulings. Explanation of the Condition of the Ruling. The explicit wording of the condition combines both aspects, i.e., the specific and the non-specific, so that if he says, 'If I marry a woman, she is divorced,' or 'If I marry this woman, she is divorced,' divorce occurs with marriage in both cases. The fourth: the sign, which is that by which existence is known without any obligation or existence being attached to it, i.e., the existence of the ruling. His statement: 'by which existence is known' excludes the cause, because it is a means of bringing about, not a mere indicator; and his statement: 'without any obligation being attached to it' excludes the effective cause, and 'without any existence being attached to it' excludes the condition, like iḥṣān in the chapter of adultery, for it is a sign for stoning, and it is the description of the adulterer being free, Muslim, legally responsible, having had intercourse in a valid marriage once. So legal responsibility is a condition in all rulings, and freedom is to complete the punishment, but the main point here is Islam and intercourse in a valid marriage. We have made it a sign, not a condition, because when adultery occurs, its being a cause for stoning does not depend on an iḥṣān that occurs thereafter; for if iḥṣān occurs after adultery, stoning is not established by its occurrence; rather, flogging becomes obligatory. The explicit wording of the condition, i.e., the explicit condition, which by its wording combines both aspects, unlike the indication of the condition, which does not combine both aspects, but is specific to the indefinite noun due to the deficiency of this indication, for it is a condition in meaning not in wording. (al-Qamar) 'The fourth' i.e., of the things related to rulings. (al-Qamar) 'by which existence is known' etc., like the takbīr in prayer as a sign of transition from one pillar to another, the adhān as a sign of prayer, the talbiyah as a sign of the rites of Hajj, and like Ramadan in the statement of a man to his wife 'you are divorced one month before Ramadan,' for it is a pure indicator of the time in which divorce occurs, and sometimes the sign is called a condition, metaphorically, like iḥṣān in the chapter of adultery. (al-Sanbalī) 'excludes the effective cause' because the obligation of the effect depends on the effective cause. (al-Qamar) 'excludes the condition' because the existence of the conditioned depends on it. (al-Qamar) 'to complete the punishment' i.e., to make it complete. (al-Qamar) 'The main point here' etc.: He said in al-Taḥqīq: It is said: iḥṣān in adultery is the combination of seven things: intellect, puberty, freedom, valid marriage, consummation of marriage, each of the spouses being like the other in the description of iḥṣān, and Islam. He said: And Shams al-A'imma said: those conditions of iḥṣān in particular are two things: Islam and consummation in a valid marriage with a woman like him. As for intellect and puberty, they are conditions for legal capacity for punishment, not conditions of iḥṣān in particular; and freedom is a condition for achieving the punishment. (al-Sanbalī) 'here' i.e., in the particular conditions of iḥṣān. (al-Qamar) 'does not depend' etc. i.e., just as dependence occurs upon the occurrence of the condition. (al-Qamar) 'capacity for punishment'
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a definition and distinction of the 'sign' (ʿalāmah) among the things related to a ruling (aḥkām). It begins by reiterating that the explicit wording of a condition (sharṭ) can cover both unspecified and specified matters, as in conditional divorce. The fourth category after cause (sabab), condition (sharṭ), and effective cause (ʿillah) is the sign (ʿalāmah), defined as something that indicates the existence of a ruling without having any bearing on its obligation (wujūb) or existence (wujūd). The commentator explains each qualification: 'indicates existence' excludes the cause because a cause actually produces the ruling; 'without obligation' excludes the effective cause (ʿillah) because the obligation of the effect depends on it; 'without existence' excludes the condition (sharṭ) because the existence of the conditioned depends on it. The example given is iḥṣān in zina, which is a description of the adulterer (being free, Muslim, legally responsible, having had valid intercourse). Some scholars hold iḥṣān to be a sign (ʿalāmah) for the obligation of stoning (rajm), not a condition, because if iḥṣān occurs after zina, stoning does not apply; only flogging does. This shows that iḥṣān is not a condition for the existence of the ruling but only indicates that at the time of zina, the circumstances were such that stoning is due. The passage then notes a dispute among later scholars (mutaʾakhkhirūn): some still consider iḥṣān a sign, but the majority (al-akthar) choose that it is a condition (sharṭ) for the obligation of rajm, because stoning depends on its presence. The practical difference appears in witness liability: if iḥṣān is a sign, witnesses of iḥṣān who retract after stoning are not liable for the blood money (diyah), because the sign is not a cause to which the ruling can be attributed. But if iḥṣān is a condition, then witnesses of the condition become liable according to some mashāyikh (like Fakhr al-Islam), because the condition can substitute for the cause when attribution is difficult. However, Shams al-A'imma and many scholars hold that condition witnesses are not liable. The text clarifies that even though iḥṣān is often called a condition metaphorically, technically it is a sign. The passage uses examples like takbīr in prayer (sign of transition), adhān (sign of prayer time), and the statement 'you are divorced one month before Ramadan' (sign of a specific time).

Key Terms
العلامة (al-ʿalāmah): ما يعرف الوجود من غير أن يتعلق به وجوب ولا وجود: that by which existence is known without any obligation or existence being attached to it.
الشرط (al-sharṭ): ما يتوقف عليه وجود المشروط: that on which the existence of the conditioned depends.
الإحصان (al-iḥṣān): حال في الزاني يصير به الزنا في تلك الحالة موجبًا للرجم: a state in the adulterer by which zina in that state becomes a cause for stoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If iḥṣān is considered a condition (sharṭ) for rajm, what is the consequence for witnesses who retract after stoning, according to some scholars (e.g., Fakhr al-Islam)?
A) They are not liable because iḥṣān is a sign.
B) They are liable to pay diyah.
C) They are only liable if they also retract the zina testimony.
D) They are liable but the amount is reduced.

Key Takeaway
The classification of iḥṣān as a sign or condition directly affects whether witnesses of iḥṣān are liable for diyah if they retract.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Distinguishing Shart, Illa, and 'Alama in Hanafi Usul
Defining shart, illa, and 'alama via ihsan and rajm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define shart, illa, and 'alama, distinguish them using the Hanafi criteria, and apply the distinction to determine legal consequences in cases like ihsan and rajm.

Core Idea
A sign ('alama) indicates a ruling without affecting its existence or obligation, unlike a condition (shart) or cause (illa).

In Hanafi usul, understanding the difference between a condition, a cause, and a sign is crucial for correctly attributing legal effects. This passage uses the case of ihsan (being married, free, and Muslim) in the penalty of rajm to illustrate these concepts. The key question: is ihsan a condition for rajm, or just a sign that rajm is applicable? The answer determines whether witnesses of ihsan are liable if they retract. Let's explore the definitions and the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three concepts
Start by locating the definitions of shart, illa, and 'alama in the passage. Note that shart is something upon which the existence of the ruling depends, illa is the effective cause that brings about the ruling, and 'alama is a sign that indicates the ruling but does not affect its existence or obligation.
The passage focuses on 'alama and shart, using ihsan as the test case.
2
Analyze the dispute: is ihsan shart or 'alama?
The majority Hanafis (preferred view) hold that ihsan is a 'alama (sign) because rajm is attributed to zina itself, not to ihsan. Zufar holds it is a shart (condition) because rajm depends on ihsan. Identify the evidence for each side as presented.
Note that the Hanafi response emphasizes that a 'alama is not suitable for substitution (khilafah), while a shart can substitute for the cause when attribution to the cause is impossible.
3
Derive the practical consequence
The distinction affects the liability of witnesses. If ihsan is a 'alama, witnesses of ihsan are not liable if they retract because their testimony did not affect the existence or obligation of the ruling. If it were a shart, they would be liable. Confirm the ruling using the text.
The passage also compares with a divorce condition scenario to illustrate the difference.
4
Examine the qiyas (analogy) used
The text employs analogy: it compares the case of witnesses of a condition (like a suspended divorce) to witnesses of ihsan. Understand how the analogy works and why the majority distinguished the two cases.
The analogy shows that when a condition can substitute for the cause, its witnesses may be liable; but a 'alama cannot substitute.
5
Summarize the usul principle
Formulate the principle: 'Alama has no legal effect on existence or obligation; it only indicates a state. Therefore, legal attribution (idafah) cannot be made to it. This principle governs cases where a sign and a condition appear together.
This principle is part of the Hanafi theory of hukm and ascription.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الأحكام
بيان شرط الحكم وعدم كونه علة وسببًا ،ظاهر فعلم أنه عبارة عن حال في الزاني يصير به الزنا في تلك الحالة موجبًا للرجم، وهو معنى كونه علامة، وهذا عند بعض المتأخرين، ومختار الأكثر أنه الإحصان شرط لوجوب الرجم؛ لأن الشرط ما يتوقف عليه وجود الحكم والإحصان بهذه المثابة؛ إذ الزنا لا يوجب الرجم بدونه كالسرقة لا توجب القطع بدون النصاب حتى لا يضمن الإحصان شهوده إذا رجعوا بحال، تفريع على كون الإحصان علامةً لا شرطًا، يعني إذا رجع شهود الإحصان بعد الرجم لا يضمنون دية المرجوم بحال أي سواء رجعوا وحدهم أو مع شهود الزنا أيضًا؛ لأنه علامة لا يتعلق بها وجوب ولا وجود ولا يجوز إضافة الحكم إليه، الإحصان بخلاف ما إذا اجتمع شهود الشرط والعلة بأن شهد اثنان بقوله: "إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق" وشهد اثنان بدخول الدار ، ثم رجع شهود الشرط وحدهم، فإنهم يضمنون عند بعض المشايخ؛ لأن الشرط صالح لخلافة العلة عند تعذر إضافة الحكم إليها لتعلق الوجود العلة به وثبوت التعدّي منهم، وهو مختار فخر الإسلام ، وعند شمس الأئمة: لا ضمان أي بالشرط شهود الشرط وعدم كونه أي الإحصان علة وسببًا ظاهر؛ لأنه ليس مؤثر في الرجم ولا هو طريق مفض إليه.(القمر) ظاهر إلخ وهو أنه ليس بطريق مفض إليه، فعرفنا أن الرجم غير مضاف إليه وجوبًا ولا جودًا، ولكنه عبارة عن حال في الزاني يصير الزنا في تلك الحالة موجبًا للرجم، فكان معرفًا أن الزنا حين وجد كان موجبا للرجم، فكان علامة لا شرطا . (السنبلي عن حال إلخ وهو كون الزاني حرا مسلما كما مر . (القمر) أنه شرط إلخ فشهود الإحصان إذا رجعوا يضمنون لإضافة التلف بالرجم إلى هذه الشهود.(القمر) والإحصان بهذه المثابة : فإن وجوب الرجم يتوقف عليه. (القمر) أو مع شهود الزنا إلخ: قبل القضاء أو بعده؛ لأنهم كانوا شهود العلامة والعلامة لا يتعلّق بها وجود ولا وجوب فلا يجوز إضافة الحكم إليها بوجه، فإذا لم يضف الرجم إلى العلامة وهو الإحصان فشهود الإحصان بريئون عنه، فلا ضمان عليهم (السنبلي) وجوب ولا وجود أي وجوب الحكم وهو الرجم ولا وجوده. (القمر) إن دخلت إلخ: أي بأن الزوج علق طلاقها على دخول الدار وهي غير موطوءة. (القمر) فإنهم يضمنون: أي الزوج ما أدّاه المرأة من نصف المهر. (القمر) وعند شمس الأئمة وعامة المحققين منهم أبو اليسر. شهود الشرط عليهم قياسًا على شهود الإحصان، وإن رجع شهود اليمين وشهود الشرط جميعًا، فالضمان على شهود اليمين خاصة؛ لأنهم صاحب علّة، فلا يضاف التلف إلى شهود الشرط مع وجودهم، وعند زفر به شهود الإحصان إذا رجعوا وحدهم ضمنوا دية المرجوم ذهابًا إلى أنه شرط والجواب: أن الإحصان علامة لا تصلح للخلافة، ولئن سلّمنا أنه شرط فلا يجوز إضافة الحكم إليه؛ لأن شهود العلة وهي الزنا صالحة للإضافة؛ فلم يبق للشرط اعتبار ؛ إذ لا اعتبار للخلف عند إمكان العمل بالأصل.
كما ذهب إليه المتقدمون
Section on Legal Rulings. Explanation of the condition of the ruling and that it is not a cause or reason. It becomes clear that it (ihsan) is a description in the fornicator through which fornication in that state becomes liable for stoning. This is the meaning of it being a sign. This is according to some later scholars. The choice of the majority is that ihsan is a condition for the obligation of stoning, because the condition is that upon which the existence of the ruling depends, and ihsan is of this status. Since fornication does not necessitate stoning without it, like theft does not necessitate amputation without the nisab. Consequently, the witnesses of ihsan are not liable if they retract at all. This is a branch of considering ihsan a sign, not a condition. That is, if the witnesses of ihsan retract after the stoning, they do not guarantee the blood money of the stoned person at all, whether they retract alone or together with the witnesses of fornication. Because it is a sign, with which neither obligation nor existence is connected, and it is not permissible to attribute the ruling to it. This is unlike when the witnesses of a condition and a cause come together, such as two witnesses testify to the husband's statement: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' and two witnesses testify to the entry into the house. Then the witnesses of the condition alone retract. They are liable according to some scholars, because the condition is suitable to substitute for the cause when it is impossible to attribute the ruling to it due to the connection of existence to the cause and the proven transgression from them. This is the choice of Fakhr al-Islam. According to Shams al-A'imma: no liability. The fact that ihsan is not a cause or reason is apparent, because it is not effective in stoning nor is it a path leading to it. (al-Qamar: 'apparent' etc. meaning it is not a path leading to it. So we know that stoning is not attributed to it in terms of obligation or existence. Rather it is a description in the fornicator by which fornication in that state becomes liable for stoning, so it is a sign that fornication when found was liable for stoning. Thus it is a sign, not a condition.) (al-Sunbuli: 'description' etc. meaning the fornicator is free, Muslim, as previously mentioned.) (al-Qamar: 'it is a condition' etc. then the witnesses of ihsan if they retract are liable, because the loss by stoning is attributed to these witnesses.) (al-Qamar: 'and ihsan is of this status': the obligation of stoning depends on it.) (al-Sunbuli: 'or with the witnesses of fornication' etc.: before or after judgment, because they were witnesses of the sign, and the sign is not connected to existence or obligation, so it is not permissible to attribute the ruling to it in any way. Since stoning is not attributed to the sign, which is ihsan, the witnesses of ihsan are innocent of it, so no liability on them.) (al-Qamar: 'obligation nor existence': meaning the obligation of the ruling which is stoning, nor its existence.) (al-Qamar: 'if you enter' etc.: meaning the husband suspended her divorce on entering the house and she was not yet touched.) (al-Qamar: 'then they are liable': meaning the husband pays half the dower to the woman.) (al-Qamar: 'and according to Shams al-A'imma and the majority of investigators, including Abu al-Yusr.') The witnesses of the condition are liable by analogy to the witnesses of ihsan. If the witnesses of the oath (yamin) and the witnesses of the condition all retract, then the liability is specifically on the witnesses of the oath, because they are the ones of the cause. So the loss is not attributed to the witnesses of the condition in their presence. According to Zufar, the witnesses of ihsan if they retract alone are liable for the blood money of the stoned person, on the view that it is a condition. The answer: ihsan is a sign not suitable for substitution. Even if we concede that it is a condition, it is not permissible to attribute the ruling to it, because the witnesses of the cause, which is fornication, are suitable for attribution. Thus the condition has no consideration. For there is no consideration for the substitute when it is possible to act on the original. As the earlier scholars held.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul work explains the technical distinction between a condition (shart), a cause (illa), and a sign ('alama) in the context of hadd punishments, specifically stoning (rajm) for adultery. The author clarifies that ihsan (being married, free, and Muslim) is not a condition for the obligation of stoning but rather a sign (علامة) that indicates when fornication becomes liable for stoning. The primary ruling is that a sign does not affect the existence or obligation of the ruling; it merely identifies a state. This distinction has practical consequences for the liability of witnesses who retract. If witnesses of ihsan retract after stoning, they are not liable for blood money because their testimony only pertained to a sign, not a condition or cause. In contrast, if witnesses of a condition (e.g., a suspended divorce) retract, they may be liable because the condition can substitute for the cause when attribution to the cause is impossible. The text presents disagreements among Hanafi scholars: Fakhr al-Islam holds that witnesses of a condition are liable, while Shams al-A'imma disagrees. Zufar treats ihsan as a condition and thus imposes liability on its witnesses, but the author refutes this by emphasizing that a sign cannot substitute for a cause. The argument uses qiyas (analogy) to compare witness scenarios, and the preferred position is that of the earlier scholars (متقدمون) that ihsan is a sign, not a condition.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition upon which the existence of the ruling depends; e.g., ihsan is considered a condition for rajm by some.
علامة ('alama): A sign that indicates the presence of a ruling without being a cause or condition; e.g., ihsan as a sign that zina is liable for rajm.
علة (illa): A cause that brings about the ruling; e.g., zina itself is the cause for rajm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, what is the status of ihsan in relation to the obligation of rajm?
A) It is a cause (illa)
B) It is a condition (shart)
C) It is a sign ('alama)
D) It is a preventer (mani')

Key Takeaway
Ihsan is a sign ('alama) for rajm, meaning it indicates when zina is liable for stoning but does not itself affect the obligation or existence of the ruling; therefore, witnesses of ihsan are not liable upon retraction.

Definition of Intellect and Its Role in Legal Capacity
Defines intellect, discusses its role in legal capacity, and refutes Ash'ari and Mu'tazili views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define intellect according to the Hanafi school, explain its variation, and distinguish the Hanafi position on its role in legal capacity from Ash'ari and Mu'tazili views.

Core Idea
Intellect is a tool for understanding revelation, but the Lawgiver uses puberty as the criterion for full capacity.

This lesson defines the term 'aql (intellect) and examines its function in legal capacity (ahliyyah). The Hanafi school sees intellect as a tool for receiving revelation, not an independent source of moral knowledge. While intellect varies among individuals, the Lawgiver has pragmatically set puberty as the measure for sound intellect, thereby resolving the debate between over-reliance on reason (Mu'tazila) and rejection of any role for intellect (Ash'aris).

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of intellect
Find the definition of 'aql as a power (quwwa) by which the soul perceives universals. Note the difference in opinion about its seat: brain (philosophers) vs. heart (usul scholars).
Hanafis describe intellect as a 'light' guiding beyond sensory perception.
2
Understand the Hanafi description of intellect
Recognize the Hanafi characterization of intellect as a 'light' (nur) that leads from the limits of sensory perception. This emphasizes its role as an instrument for understanding higher truths, including revelation.
3
Observe the variation in intellect
Note that intellect is created in varying degrees among individuals: prophets, saints, scholars, common people, villagers, women. Even a child may surpass an adult in intellect.
This variation is the reason the Lawgiver could not rely on intellect alone as a criterion.
4
Recognize the legal criterion set by the Lawgiver
See that despite variation, the Lawgiver has established puberty (bulugh) as the practical marker for sound intellect in legal capacity. This is a substitution for directly evaluating intellect.
Puberty is a tangible, observable sign that replaces the variable internal quality.
5
Analyze the disagreements and the Hanafi middle position
Compare the Ash'ari position (no role for intellect without revelation) and the Mu'tazili position (intellect as independent cause of obligation). The Hanafi view holds intellect as a necessary condition but uses revelation's criterion (puberty) for obligation.
The Hanafi approach balances the necessity of intellect with the practicality of a fixed legal marker.

(الإسراء: ١٥) وقالت المعتزلة: إنه علة موجبة لما استحسنه ومحرمة لما استقبحه على القطع والثبات وأنه: أي العقل خلق متفاوتا في الناس قوةً وضعفًا.(القمر) متفاوتًا: هذا ردّ لما قال المعتزلة: إن العقل غير متفاوتة؛ لأن مدار التكليف والدائر غير متفاوتة، فالمدار أيضا كذلك فالمصنف ردّ قول المعتزلة وإن لم يكن غرضه هذا فلا وجه لذكر هذه العبارة في هذا المقام، لأن مناسبة العبارة بالعقل معتبر لإثبات الأهلية، فقالت الأشعرية: لا عبرة للعقل أصلاً. متفاوتًا يعني أن العقل متفاوت في أفراد الإنسان حدوثاً وبقاء، أما حدويًّا؛ فلأن النفوس متفاوتة بحسب الفطرة في الكمال والنقصان باعتبار زيادة اعتدال البدن ،ونقصانه، وأما بقاء؛ فلأن النفس كلما زادت في كثرة العلوم ازدادت تناسبا بالعقل الفعّال الكامل من كل وجه فازدادت إفاضة نوره عليها لازدياد الاستفاضة بازدياد المناسبة، ولما تفاوتت العقول في الأشخاص تعذر العلم بأن عقل كل شخص هل بلغ المرتبة التي هي مناط التكليف؟ فقدر الشارع تلك المرتبة بوقت البلوغ إقامة للسبب الظاهر مقام حكمه، هذا ملخص ما في 'التلويح'. (السنبلي) لا عبرة: أي في معرفة الأحكام الشرعية العقل دون السمع أي من الشارع (القمر) السمع: أي المسموع وهو الدليل الشرعي. (القمر) حسن شيء: أي كون الشيء قابلا لأن يثاب على فعله. (القمر) وقبحه: أي كون الشيء قابلاً لأن يعاقب عليه. (القمر) لعدم ورود إلخ فإن الصبي العاقل لا يكلفه الشارع. (المحشي)
When he finished explaining the attachments of rulings, he began explaining the legal capacity of the one upon whom the ruling is made, i.e., the responsible person. Since it is known that his capacity is not without intellect, he therefore began by mentioning intellect, saying: 'Chapter on explaining legal capacity' meaning capacity for address. Intellect is considered for establishing capacity because address is not understood without it, and addressing someone who does not understand is objectionable. Its interpretation has already passed in the year. Intellect, according to most, is a power by which the soul perceives universals; its seat is the brain according to philosophers, and the heart according to usul scholars, and it is the flesh. The power is what is meant by 'light' in the Hanafi statement: 'Intellect is a light that guides from the ultimate limit of sensory perception.' And it is created in varying degrees: the most intellect are the prophets, peace be upon them, and saints, then scholars and sages, then common people and rulers, then villagers and women. In each type there are different degrees; a single one may equal a thousand. Many a small child extracts with his intellect what the adult is incapable of, but the Lawgiver has set puberty as the measure for sound intellect. They differed regarding its consideration. The Ash'aris said: No consideration for intellect without revelation; when revelation comes, it is considered, not intellect. So nothing is understood as good or bad, obligatory or prohibited by it, nor is the faith of an intelligent child valid due to lack of revelation regarding it. This is the view of al-Shafi'i. They cited Allah's saying: 'And We were not to punish until We sent a messenger' (17:15). The Mu'tazila said: It is a cause that necessitates what it deems good and prohibits what it deems evil decisively. And that intellect is created varying in people in strength and weakness. (Marginal: This is a refutation of what the Mu'tazila said that intellect is not varying; because the basis of obligation [which is intellect] is not varying, so the basis would also be like that. So the author refuted the Mu'tazila's statement, even if his purpose was not this, there is no reason for mentioning this expression in this context, because the appropriateness of the expression with intellect is considered for establishing capacity. So the Ash'aris said: no consideration for intellect at all. 'Mutanawwitan' (varying) means that intellect varies in individuals in its origination and continuation. As for origination, because souls vary according to natural disposition in perfection and defect, considering the increase or decrease of bodily balance. As for continuation, because whenever the soul increases in abundance of knowledge, it increases in suitability with the active intellect which is complete in every aspect, so the outpouring of its light upon it increases due to the increase of reception because of increased suitability. And since intellects vary among persons, it becomes impossible to know whether the intellect of each person has reached the level that is the basis for obligation. So the Lawgiver determined that level by the time of puberty, establishing the apparent cause in place of its ruling. This is the summary of what is in 'al-Talwih'. (al-Sunbuli) 'No consideration' means: in knowing the legal rulings, the intellect is not considered without the hearing, i.e., the hearing from the Lawgiver. (al-Qamar) 'Hearing' means the heard, i.e., the legal proof. (al-Qamar) 'Goodness of something' means: that the thing is worthy of being rewarded for doing it. (al-Qamar) 'Its badness' means: that the thing is worthy of being punished for. (al-Qamar) 'Due to lack of revelation etc.' means that the Lawgiver does not charge the intelligent child. (al-Qamar) 'They argued with His saying' means: this saying indicates the negation of punishment before the mission of messengers, and this negation is a ruling of unbelief concerning them. (al-Qamar) 'It' means: intellect is a cause that necessitates what reason deems good, like gratitude to the Benefactor, and a prohibitive cause for what reason deems bad, like ingratitude for Allah's blessings. (al-Qamar) 'What it deems good' like knowing the Creator's divinity and thanking the Benefactor (al-Muhashi). 'What it deems bad' like ignorance of the Creator and ingratitude for blessings. (al-Muhashi)
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage defines intellect ('aql) and examines its role in legal capacity (ahliyyah). The author begins by noting that after discussing the attachments of rulings (causes, conditions, signs), he turns to the subject of legal capacity. He states that intellect is essential for capacity, as divine address is only meaningful to one who understands. The definition of intellect is given as a power of the soul to perceive universals; its seat is debated (brain vs. heart). Hanafis describe intellect as a light that guides beyond the senses. Intellect varies among people—prophets have the most, then scholars, etc. Despite this variation, the Lawgiver has established puberty (bulugh) as the practical criterion for sound intellect. The passage then presents two opposing views: the Ash'aris deny any independent role for intellect in legal rulings, relying solely on revelation, citing Q. 17:15. The Mu'tazila claim intellect is a decisive cause for determining good and evil. The Hanafi position is implied by the statement that intellect is considered for capacity, but the actual criterion is puberty, which mediates between the two extremes. The marginal notes further clarify the debate. Overall, the passage establishes the Hanafi usul principle that intellect is a necessary condition for legal capacity, but its evaluation is replaced by a clear legal marker: puberty.

Key Terms
العقل (al-'Aql): A power (quwwa) in the soul by which it perceives universals, created variable, and considered a condition for legal capacity but practically measured by puberty.
الأهلية (al-Ahliyyah): Legal capacity: the suitability of a person to be the subject of obligations (ahliyyat al-wujub) and to perform actions (ahliyyat al-ada'). Full capacity requires intellect and puberty.
السمع (al-Sam'): Revelation (the heard from the Lawgiver); the primary source of legal rulings, without which intellect cannot determine good/bad.
البلوغ (al-Bulugh): Puberty; the legal marker set by the Lawgiver for when a person is considered to have sound intellect and becomes fully obligated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, what is the practical criterion for when a person attains full legal capacity (ahliyyah)?
A) The age of majority as determined by the state
B) The ability to reason abstractly
C) Puberty (bulugh)
D) A specific age like 18

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school affirms intellect as a condition for capacity but delegates the practical determination to puberty, avoiding both the Mu'tazili rationalism and Ash'ari rejection of intellect.

Definition and Types of Legal Capacity (Ahliyya)
Defines ahliyya and its types with Quranic evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ahliyya (legal capacity), distinguish between ahliyyat al-wujub and ahliyyat al-ada', and explain the basis of ahliyyat al-wujub in the primordial covenant (yawm al-mithaq).

Core Idea
Legal capacity is rooted in the primordial covenant: every human is born with a dhimma suitable for rights and duties.

In this passage, the author defines legal capacity (ahliyya) and its two types. The first type, capacity for obligation (ahliyyat al-wujub), is derived from the concept of dhimma (legal personality), which itself originates from the covenantal affirmation of Allah's lordship (Quran 7:172). Understanding this key distinction is essential for grasping how Hanafi usul al-fiqh conceptualizes the subject of law (mahkum alayh) from birth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its types
The passage states: 'الأهلية نوعان' (ahliyya is of two types). Identify the two types: ahliyyat al-wujub and ahliyyat al-ada' (the second type is not elaborated here but is implied).
2
Define ahliyyat al-wujub
It is capacity for obligation, based on the existence of dhimma. Define dhimma as the covenant from yawm al-mithaq.
Dhimma is legally the person (nafs) that bears rights and duties.
3
Locate the dalil
Quran 7:172 is cited as evidence for the covenant.
The verse is a clear text (nass) affirming that all souls acknowledged Allah's lordship.
4
Trace the istinbat
From the verse, the author deduces that every human is born with a dhimma suitable for obligation. This deduction uses the pre-eternal covenant as the cause (sabab).
5
Understand the subtlety: wujub vs ada'
The passage explains that obligation (wujub) is not the end; performance (ada') is. For a minor, obligation is for benefit or harm, not for performance.
This distinction is critical for understanding partial capacity.

والأهلية نوعان: النوع الأول: أهلية وجوب وهي بناء على قيام الذمة، أي أهلية نفس أي مبنية الوجوب لا تثبت إلا بعد وجود ذمة صالحة للوجوب له وعليه، وهي عبارة عن العهد الذي عاهدنا ربنا يوم الميثاق بقوله: ﴿أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ قَالُوا بَلَى شَهِدْنَا﴾ فلما أقررنا بربوبيته يوم الميثاق فقد أقررنا بجميع شرائعه الصالحة لنا وعلينا. والآدمي يولد وله ذمة صالحة للوجوب له وعليه بناء على ذلك العهد الماضي، وما دام لم يولد كان جزء من الأم يُعتق بعتقها، ويدخل في البيع تبعا لها، ولم تكن ذمته صالحةً؛ لأن الأمة يجب عليه الحق من نفقة الأقارب وثمن المبيع الذي اشتراه الولي له وإن كانت صالحة لما يجب له من العتق والإرث والوصية والنسب. وإذا ولد كانت صالحة لما يجب له وعليه، ضرره أي لنفعه أي لأجل الصبي غير أن الوجوب غير مقصود بنفسه، وإنما المقصود أداؤه، فلما لم يتصور ذلك في حق الصبي أي الأداء للوجوب له وعليه أي لوجوب الأحكام المشروعة للنفع أو للضرر، فاللام للنفع، وكلمة "علي" للضرر.
