Insanity: Definition and Legal Capacity
Definition of insanity with legal capacity analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of insanity (al-junūn) and identify its effect on legal capacity (ahlīyah) for acts of worship and financial obligations.

Core Idea
Insanity nullifies legal capacity for acts of worship but not for harmful acts or financial liabilities.

This passage defines insanity in technical Hanafi terms, setting it as an affliction of the brain that disrupts rational action without physical weakness. It then clarifies the scope of its legal impact: certain worships are suspended, but obligations like damages, maintenance, and blood money remain firmly in place.

Guided Path
1
Identify the technical definition
Locate the phrase describing insanity as an affliction (āfah) settling in the brain (dimāgh), causing actions contrary to reason without physical weakness.
Also note the source: quoting Shaykh Abu al-Muʿīn al-Nasafī.
2
Analyze the effect on legal capacity
Note that insanity causes the suspension of acts of worship that can be dropped (e.g., prayer, fasting) because the person loses the ability to understand the address.
Contrast with obligations like damages, maintenance, and blood money which are not dropped.
3
Understand the inheritance digression
Trace the argument: a child who kills his father does not lose inheritance, unlike a disbeliever or slave. The difference is that disbelief and slavery negate capacity for inheritance entirely, not as punishment.
The proof uses Quran 4:141 and 19:5-6 to link inheritance with authority (wilāyah).
4
Distinguish dropped vs retained obligations
Summarize: worship susceptible to being dropped (e.g., prayer, fasting) are suspended; duties that cause harm to others (damages, nadhafa, etc.) are not.
This mirrors the rule for a child (minor).

مثل الصغر
له
لأنه عقوبة إلخ أي لأن حرمان الميراث بالقتل عقوبة إلخ، ولأن موجب القتل يحتمل السقوط بالعفو وبأعذار كثيرة، فيسقط بعذر الصّبا، فكأن مورثه مات حتف أنفه؟ كذا قيل (القمر) كذلك أي إذا كان لا يحرم الصبي الميراث بقتل مورث (القمر) أن يحرم أي الصبي عن الميراث بالكفر والرق فيرث الصبي الكافر عن المسلم والصبي الرقيق عن الحرّ كما يرث الصبي القاتل عن المقتول.(القمر) بل لعدم الأهلية: فإن الوراثة خلافة الملك وولايته والرق ينافي الملك فينافي الإرث والكفر ينافي أهلية الولاية على المسلم (القمر) ينافي أهلية الميراث إلخ لأن الإرث يقتضي أن يكون الوارث مالكا لما يرثه، والرقيق لا يصح الملك؛ لأن كل ما يملكه الرقيق هو ملك لمولاه، ومثل الرق الكفر في أنه ينافي الإرث؛ لأنه ينافي أهلية الولاية، أي لا ولاية للكافر على المسلم لقوله عزّوجلّ: وَلَنْ يَجْعَلَ اللَّهُ لِلْكَافِرِينَ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِينَ سَبِيلاً) (النساء: ١٤١) والإرث مبني على الولاية على ما يشير إليه قوله تعالى : حكاية عن زكريا عليه : وَهَبْ لِي مِنْ لَدُنْكَ وَلِيَا يَرِثُنِي (مريم: ٦،٥) الآية، وعدم الإرث لعدم سببه، أي الولاية فإنه معدوم وجودها في الكافر وعدم أهلية المستحق، فإن الرقيق ليس أهلاً له لا يعد جزاء أي عقوبة (السنبلي) بحيث يبعث : فيختلّ القوة المميزة بين الأمور الحسنة والقبيحة.(القمر) خلاف مقتضى العقل إلخ : قال الشيخ أبو المعين: لا يمكن الوقوف على حقيقة الجنون إلا بعد الوقوف على حقيقة العقل ومحله دافعا له، فالعقل معنى يمكن به الاستدلال من الشاهد على الغائب، والاطلاع على عواقب الأمور والتميز بين الخير والشر، ومحله الدماغ، فالمعنى الموجب لانعدام آثاره وتعطيل أفعاله الباعث للإنسان على
أفعال مضادّة لتلك الأفعال من غير ضعف وفتور في الأعضاء يُسمى جنونًا، كذا في "الغاية". (السنبلي) وتسقط به العبادات إلخ كالصلاة لفوات الأهلية بزوال العقل بالجنون فلا يفهم الخطاب. (القمر)

بيان الأهلية
١٥٩
بيان الجنون
لا ضمان المتلفات ونفقة الأقارب والدية كما في الصبي بعينه، وكذا الطلاق والعتاق أي وجوب الدية
ونحوهما من المضار غير مشروع في حقه.
كالهبة والصدقة
لكنه إذا لم يمتدّ ألحق بالنوم عند علمائنا الثلاثة، فيجب عليه قضاء العبادات كما على
لعدم تضاعف العبادات
النائم؛ إذ لا حرج في قضاء القليل، وهذا في الجنون العارضي بأن بلغ عاقلاً ثم جُنّ، وأمّا في الجنون الأصلي بأن بلغ مجنونا، فعند أبي يوسف الله هو بمنزلة الصبا حتى لو أفاق قبل مضي الشهر في الصوم أو قبل تمام يوم وليلة في الصلاة لا يجب عليه القضاء، وعند أي من وقت البلوغ محمد محله هو بمنزلة العارضي، فيجب عليه القضاء، وقيل: الاختلاف على العكس. ثم أراد أن يبين حدّ الامتداد وعدمه ليبتني عليه وجوب القضاء وعدمه، ولما كان ذلك أي حد الامتداد أمرًا غير مضبوط بين ضابطة يستخرج في كل العبادات، فقال: وحد الامتداد في الصلاة أن يزيد على يوم وليلة ولكن باعتبار الصلاة عند محمد حلبه، يعني ما لم تصر الصلاة ستّا
لاضمان المتلفات : فإن هذه الأمور لا تسقط بالجنون كما لا تسقط بالصغر. (القمر) في الصبي: أي الذي لا يعقل وأما المعتوه فكالصبي الذي يعقل كما سيأتي لكن من وجه لا مثله بعينه. (السنبلي) ألحق بالنوم بجامع أن كل واحد منهما عذر عارض زال قبل الامتداد. (القمر) العبادات: أي المتروكة في الجنون الغير الممتد . (القمر) الجنون العارضي فإن هذا الجنون قد حصل بعد كمال الأعضاء، فصار معترضا على المحل بلحوق ،آفة فإذا لم يمتدّ ألحق بالنوم وجعل عدما كذا قيل. (القمر)
هو بمنزلة الصبا فيسقط عنه الوجوب وإن قل؛ لأن هذا الجنون الحاصل قبل البلوغ حصل في وقت نقصان الدماغ لآفة أبقته على ما خلق عليه من الضعف الأصلي، فكان هذا الجنون أمرًا أصليا، فلا يمكن أن يلحق بالعدم، كذا قيل. (القمر) القضاء: أي قضاء ما مضى من صوم الشهر وما فاته من الصلاة. (القمر) :هو : أي الأصلي بمنزلة العارضي، فغير الممتد من الجنون أصليا كان أو عارضيًا جعل كالعدم؛ لأن الجنون الحاصل قبل البلوغ من قبيل العارض؛ لأنه لما زال فقد دلّ ذلك على حصوله عن أمر عارض على أصل الخلقة لنقصان جبل عليه دماغه، فكان مثل العارض بعد البلوغ، كذا قيل. (القمر) على العكس: أي عند محمد حله، الجنون الأصلي بمنزلة الصبا، وعند أبي يوسف الله هو بمنزلة العارضي، فينعكس الحكم حينئذ. (القمر)
أن يزيد إلخ : فإذا زاد على اليوم والليلة فيتكرّر الصلوات وفي قضائها حرج. (القمر)
Explanation of capacity. 158. Explanation of insanity. Pure benefit and this has already passed in the explanation of capacity. Then his statement: 'So he is not deprived of inheritance by killing according to us' is a branching, i.e., killing the testator, based on his statement: 'that the responsibility be removed from him' meaning if a child kills his testator intentionally or by mistake, he is not deprived of his inheritance; because it is a punishment and responsibility that the child does not deserve. It was objected: if that is the case, then he should not be deprived of inheritance by disbelief and slavery? So he answered with his statement: 'Unlike disbelief and slavery; because deprivation of inheritance by these two is not from the category of recompense, but rather due to lack of capacity; since disbelief and slavery oppose the capacity for inheritance from a free Muslim.' Explanation of insanity: And insanity, conjunct to his statement 'minority', is an affliction that settles in the brain such that it incites actions contrary to the requirement of reason without weakness in its limbs, and by it the acts of worship that can be dropped are dropped. Like minority. Because it is a punishment etc.: i.e., because deprivation of inheritance by killing is a punishment etc., and because the cause of killing can be dropped by pardon and many excuses, so it is dropped by the excuse of childhood, as if his testator died a natural death. Thus it was said. (al-Qamar) Similarly, i.e., if the child is not deprived of inheritance by killing his testator, (al-Qamar) then it is proper that he be deprived, i.e., the child from inheritance by disbelief and slavery, so the disbelieving child inherits from the Muslim and the slave child inherits from the free, just as the killer child inherits from the killed. (al-Qamar) Rather, due to lack of capacity: For inheritance is succession of ownership and authority, and slavery opposes ownership thus opposes inheritance, and disbelief opposes the capacity for authority over a Muslim. (al-Qamar) Opposes capacity for inheritance etc. because inheritance requires that the heir own what he inherits, and the slave's ownership is not valid; because everything the slave owns is the property of his master, and like slavery is disbelief in that it opposes inheritance; because it opposes the capacity for authority, i.e., a disbeliever has no authority over a Muslim due to His Almighty's statement: 'And never will Allah give the disbelievers over the believers a way' (al-Nisa: 141), and inheritance is based on authority as indicated by His Almighty's statement narrated from Zakariya, peace be upon him: 'Grant me from Yourself an heir who will inherit me' (Maryam: 5-6) the verse, and the lack of inheritance is due to lack of its cause, i.e., authority, for its existence is absent in the disbeliever and the lack of capacity of the entitled, for the slave is not entitled to it, it is not considered a recompense, i.e., punishment. (al-Sanabli) 'Such that it incites': the distinguishing power between good and bad things becomes impaired. (al-Qamar) 'Contrary to the requirement of reason etc.': Shaykh Abu al-Mu'in said: The reality of insanity cannot be known except after knowing the reality of reason and its locus that repels it. So reason is a meaning by which inference from the witnessed to the unseen is possible, and insight into the consequences of matters and distinction between good and evil, and its locus is the brain. So the meaning necessitating the disappearance of its effects and the suspension of its actions that incites a person to actions contrary to those actions without weakness and languor in the limbs is called insanity. Thus in al-Ghayah. (al-Sanabli) 'And by it the acts of worship are dropped' etc. like prayer due to the forfeiture of capacity by the removal of reason through insanity, so he does not understand the address. (al-Qamar) [Page 160] Explanation of capacity. 159. Explanation of insanity. He is not liable for damages, maintenance of relatives, and blood money just like the child itself, and likewise divorce and manumission and similar harmful acts are not legislated for him. Like gift and charity. But if it is not prolonged, it is attached to sleep according to our three scholars, so he must make up the acts of worship just as the sleeper must, because there is no hardship in making up a small amount, and this is in temporary insanity, i.e., he reached puberty sane then became insane. As for original insanity, i.e., he reached puberty insane, then according to Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, it is like childhood, so if he recovers before a month passes in fasting or before the completion of a day and night in prayer, he does not have to make up. According to Muhammad, his place is like temporary, so he must make up. And it was said: the difference is reversed. Then he wanted to explain the boundary of extension and its lack so that the obligation of making up and its lack are built upon it. And since that, i.e., the boundary of extension, is something not defined, he set a rule that is derived in all acts of worship, so he said: 'And the boundary of extension in prayer is that it exceeds a day and a night' but with consideration of prayer according to Muhammad, meaning the prayer does not become six. 'He is not liable for damages': for these matters are not dropped by insanity just as they are not dropped by childhood. (al-Qamar) 'In the child': i.e., the one who does not reason, and the feeble-minded is like the child who reasons as will come, but in some respects not exactly like him. (al-Sanabli) 'It is attached to sleep' because each of them is a temporary excuse that ceased before extension. (al-Qamar) 'Acts of worship': i.e., those omitted during non-prolonged insanity. (al-Qamar) 'Temporary insanity': for this insanity occurred after the completion of limbs, so it became an affliction on the locus, and if it is not prolonged, it is attached to sleep and considered non-existent. Thus it is said. (al-Qamar) 'It is like childhood' so the obligation falls even if small; because this insanity before puberty occurred at a time of brain deficiency due to an affliction that kept it upon what it was created of original weakness, so this insanity was an original matter, so it cannot be attached to non-existence. Thus it is said. (al-Qamar) 'Making up': i.e., making up what has passed of the month's fast and what he missed of prayer. (al-Qamar) 'He': i.e., the original [insanity] is like temporary, so non-prolonged insanity, whether original or temporary, is considered like non-existent; because the insanity that occurred before puberty is of the type of temporary; because when it goes away, that indicates that it occurred from a temporary matter on the original constitution due to a deficiency his brain was created upon, so it became like temporary after puberty. Thus it is said. (al-Qamar) 'On the contrary': i.e., according to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, original insanity is like childhood, and according to Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, it is like temporary, so the ruling is reversed then. (al-Qamar) 'That it exceeds etc.': So if it exceeds a day and night, the prayers multiply and there is hardship in making them up. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary (sharh) explains the concept of insanity (al-junūn) and its legal effects. The passage begins by recapping a previous ruling that a child who kills his father does not lose inheritance because he lacks legal responsibility (ʿahdah). It then addresses an objection: why does the child lose inheritance due to disbelief (kufr) or slavery (riqq) if these are also not punishments? The response is that disbelief and slavery negate the capacity (ahlīyah) for inheritance itself—inheritance requires ownership and authority over the deceased, which a slave cannot have (since his property belongs to his master) and a disbeliever cannot have over a Muslim (based on Qur'an 4:141 and 19:5-6). Thus, the deprivation is not a punishment but a result of incapacity.

Next, it formally defines insanity: it is an affliction (āfah) that settles in the brain, causing actions contrary to reason without physical weakness. This definition draws on Shaykh Abu al-Muʿīn's concept of ʿaql (reason) as the faculty of inference, foresight, and moral discrimination, located in the brain. Insanity nullifies these effects, leading to the suspension of acts of worship that can be dropped (like prayer), but not obligations like liability for damages, maintenance, or blood money.

The passage then addresses the consequences for missed worship if the insanity is not prolonged (lam yamtadd). According to the three scholars (Abu Hanīfah, Abū Yūsuf, Muḥammad), non-prolonged insanity is treated like sleep: the person must make up missed prayers and fasts because there is no hardship. However, this applies to temporary insanity (ʿāriḍī), where a sane adult becomes insane. For original insanity (aṣlī), where one reaches puberty already insane, there is a dispute: Abū Yūsuf considers it like childhood—no obligation to make up missed worship if recovery occurs before the period (month for fasting, day and night for prayer). Muḥammad treats it like temporary insanity—make-up is required. Some narrations reverse their positions.

Finally, the boundary of extension (ḥadd al-imtidād) is defined: in prayer, if insanity exceeds a day and a night, it is prolonged, so make-up is obligatory (due to hardship of many prayers). This rule is generalized to other acts of worship.

Key Terms
الجنون (al-junūn): An affliction settling in the brain that incites actions contrary to reason without physical weakness, suspending legal capacity for acts of worship.
الأهلية (al-ahlīyah): Legal capacity; the fitness to acquire rights and obligations.
العارضي (al-ʿāriḍī): Temporary insanity occurring after puberty in a sane person.
الأصلي (al-aṣlī): Original insanity present from before puberty (i.e., reaching puberty insane).
الامتداد (al-imtidād): Prolongation of insanity beyond a defined limit (e.g., more than a day and night for prayer).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition, where does insanity reside?
A) In the heart
B) In the brain
C) In the soul
D) In the limbs

Key Takeaway
Insanity is a brain-based affliction that suspends legal capacity for acts of worship but not for financial or harmful obligations.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Temporary vs Original Insanity: Make-up Obligations
Dispute on make-up obligations for original insanity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between temporary and original insanity in Hanafi law and apply the rules for make-up (qaḍāʾ) of missed acts of worship based on the type and duration.

Core Idea
Non-prolonged insanity is like sleep; original insanity sparks a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on qada'.

This passage details the consequences of insanity for missed worship. It distinguishes between temporary insanity (occurring after puberty) and original insanity (present at puberty). For non-prolonged episodes, the rule is clear: make-up is required like sleep. However, for original insanity, the jurists differ: Abu Yusuf treats it like childhood, exempting from make-up if recovery is swift; Muhammad treats it like temporary insanity, requiring make-up.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish temporary from original insanity
Identify the definitions: 'āriḍī arises after puberty in a sane person; aṣlī is present from before puberty.
The passage uses 'balagha ʿāqilan thumma junna' vs 'balagha majnūnan'.
2
Apply the rule for non-prolonged insanity
Note that if insanity does not exceed a certain limit (imtidād), it is attached to sleep. Then make-up of missed worship is obligatory.
The limit for prayer: exceeding a day and night.
3
Analyze the dispute on original insanity
Abu Yusuf: original insanity is like childhood – no make-up if recovery before limit (month for fasting, day/night for prayer). Muhammad: like temporary – make-up required.
Some narrations reverse the positions.
4
Understand the concept of extension (imtidād)
The boundary for prayer is exceeding one day and night; for fasting, a month. Exceeding these makes make-up obligatory due to hardship.
The text generalizes this to all acts of worship via a principle.

لكنه إذا لم يمتدّ ألحق بالنوم عند علمائنا الثلاثة، فيجب عليه قضاء العبادات كما على
لعدم تضاعف العبادات
النائم؛ إذ لا حرج في قضاء القليل، وهذا في الجنون العارضي بأن بلغ عاقلاً ثم جُنّ، وأمّا في الجنون الأصلي بأن بلغ مجنونا، فعند أبي يوسف الله هو بمنزلة الصبا حتى لو أفاق قبل مضي الشهر في الصوم أو قبل تمام يوم وليلة في الصلاة لا يجب عليه القضاء، وعند أي من وقت البلوغ محمد محله هو بمنزلة العارضي، فيجب عليه القضاء، وقيل: الاختلاف على العكس. ثم أراد أن يبين حدّ الامتداد وعدمه ليبتني عليه وجوب القضاء وعدمه، ولما كان ذلك أي حد الامتداد أمرًا غير مضبوط بين ضابطة يستخرج في كل العبادات، فقال: وحد الامتداد في الصلاة أن يزيد على يوم وليلة ولكن باعتبار الصلاة عند محمد حلبه، يعني ما لم تصر الصلاة ستّا
لاضمان المتلفات : فإن هذه الأمور لا تسقط بالجنون كما لا تسقط بالصغر. (القمر) في الصبي: أي الذي لا يعقل وأما المعتوه فكالصبي الذي يعقل كما سيأتي لكن من وجه لا مثله بعينه. Explanation of capacity. 158. Explanation of insanity. Pure benefit and this has already passed in the explanation of capacity. Then his statement: 'So he is not deprived of inheritance by killing according to us' is a branching, i.e., killing the testator, based on his statement: 'that the responsibility be removed from him' meaning if a child kills his testator intentionally or by mistake, he is not deprived of his inheritance; because it is a punishment and responsibility that the child does not deserve. It was objected: if that is the case, then he should not be deprived of inheritance by disbelief and slavery? So he answered with his statement: 'Unlike disbelief and slavery; because deprivation of inheritance by these two is not from the category of recompense, but rather due to lack of capacity; since disbelief and slavery oppose the capacity for inheritance from a free Muslim.' Explanation of insanity: And insanity, conjunct to his statement 'minority', is an affliction that settles in the brain such that it incites actions contrary to the requirement of reason without weakness in its limbs, and by it the acts of worship that can be dropped are dropped. Like minority. Because it is a punishment etc.: i.e., because deprivation of inheritance by killing is a punishment etc., and because the cause of killing can be dropped by pardon and many excuses, so it is dropped by the excuse of childhood, as if his testator died a natural death. Thus it was said. (al-Qamar) Similarly, i.e., if the child is not deprived of inheritance by killing his testator, (al-Qamar) then it is proper that he be deprived, i.e., the child from inheritance by disbelief and slavery, so the disbelieving child inherits from the Muslim and the slave child inherits from the free, just as the killer child inherits from the killed. (al-Qamar) Rather, due to lack of capacity: For inheritance is succession of ownership and authority, and slavery opposes ownership thus opposes inheritance, and disbelief opposes the capacity for authority over a Muslim. (al-Qamar) Opposes capacity for inheritance etc. because inheritance requires that the heir own what he inherits, and the slave's ownership is not valid; because everything the slave owns is the property of his master, and like slavery is disbelief in that it opposes inheritance; because it opposes the capacity for authority, i.e., a disbeliever has no authority over a Muslim due to His Almighty's statement: 'And never will Allah give the disbelievers over the believers a way' (al-Nisa: 141), and inheritance is based on authority as indicated by His Almighty's statement narrated from Zakariya, peace be upon him: 'Grant me from Yourself an heir who will inherit me' (Maryam: 5-6) the verse, and the lack of inheritance is due to lack of its cause, i.e., authority, for its existence is absent in the disbeliever and the lack of capacity of the entitled, for the slave is not entitled to it, it is not considered a recompense, i.e., punishment. (al-Sanabli) 'Such that it incites': the distinguishing power between good and bad things becomes impaired. (al-Qamar) 'Contrary to the requirement of reason etc.': Shaykh Abu al-Mu'in said: The reality of insanity cannot be known except after knowing the reality of reason and its locus that repels it. So reason is a meaning by which inference from the witnessed to the unseen is possible, and insight into the consequences of matters and distinction between good and evil, and its locus is the brain. So the meaning necessitating the disappearance of its effects and the suspension of its actions that incites a person to actions contrary to those actions without weakness and languor in the limbs is called insanity. Thus in al-Ghayah. (al-Sanabli) 'And by it the acts of worship are dropped' etc. like prayer due to the forfeiture of capacity by the removal of reason through insanity, so he does not understand the address. He is not liable for damages, maintenance of relatives, and blood money just like the child itself, and likewise divorce and manumission and similar harmful acts are not legislated for him. Like gift and charity. But if it is not prolonged, it is attached to sleep according to our three scholars, so he must make up the acts of worship just as the sleeper must, because there is no hardship in making up a small amount, and this is in temporary insanity, i.e., he reached puberty sane then became insane. As for original insanity, i.e., he reached puberty insane, then according to Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, it is like childhood, so if he recovers before a month passes in fasting or before the completion of a day and night in prayer, he does not have to make up. According to Muhammad, his place is like temporary, so he must make up. And it was said: the difference is reversed. Then he wanted to explain the boundary of extension and its lack so that the obligation of making up and its lack are built upon it. And since that, i.e., the boundary of extension, is something not defined, he set a rule that is derived in all acts of worship, so he said: 'And the boundary of extension in prayer is that it exceeds a day and a night' but with consideration of prayer according to Muhammad, meaning the prayer does not become six. 'He is not liable for damages': for these matters are not dropped by insanity just as they are not dropped by childhood. (al-Qamar) 'In the child': i.e., the one who does not reason, and the feeble-minded is like the child who reasons as will come, but in some respects not exactly like him. (al-Sanabli) 'It is attached to sleep' because each of them is a temporary excuse that ceased before extension. (al-Qamar) 'Acts of worship': i.e., those omitted during non-prolonged insanity. (al-Qamar) 'Temporary insanity': for this insanity occurred after the completion of limbs, so it became an affliction on the locus, and if it is not prolonged, it is attached to sleep and considered non-existent. Thus it is said. (al-Qamar) 'It is like childhood' so the obligation falls even if small; because this insanity before puberty occurred at a time of brain deficiency due to an affliction that kept it upon what it was created of original weakness, so this insanity was an original matter, so it cannot be attached to non-existence. Thus it is said. (al-Qamar) 'Making up': i.e., making up what has passed of the month's fast and what he missed of prayer. (al-Qamar) 'He': i.e., the original [insanity] is like temporary, so non-prolonged insanity, whether original or temporary, is considered like non-existent; because the insanity that occurred before puberty is of the type of temporary; because when it goes away, that indicates that it occurred from a temporary matter on the original constitution due to a deficiency his brain was created upon, so it became like temporary after puberty. Thus it is said. (al-Qamar) 'On the contrary': i.e., according to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, original insanity is like childhood, and according to Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, it is like temporary, so the ruling is reversed then. (al-Qamar) 'That it exceeds etc.': So if it exceeds a day and night, the prayers multiply and there is hardship in making them up. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary (sharh) explains the concept of insanity (al-junūn) and its legal effects. The passage begins by recapping a previous ruling that a child who kills his father does not lose inheritance because he lacks legal responsibility (ʿahdah). It then addresses an objection: why does the child lose inheritance due to disbelief (kufr) or slavery (riqq) if these are also not punishments? The response is that disbelief and slavery negate the capacity (ahlīyah) for inheritance itself—inheritance requires ownership and authority over the deceased, which a slave cannot have (since his property belongs to his master) and a disbeliever cannot have over a Muslim (based on Qur'an 4:141 and 19:5-6). Thus, the deprivation is not a punishment but a result of incapacity.

Next, it formally defines insanity: it is an affliction (āfah) that settles in the brain, causing actions contrary to reason without physical weakness. This definition draws on Shaykh Abu al-Muʿīn's concept of ʿaql (reason) as the faculty of inference, foresight, and moral discrimination, located in the brain. Insanity nullifies these effects, leading to the suspension of acts of worship that can be dropped (like prayer), but not obligations like liability for damages, maintenance, or blood money.

The passage then addresses the consequences for missed worship if the insanity is not prolonged (lam yamtadd). According to the three scholars (Abu Hanīfah, Abū Yūsuf, Muḥammad), non-prolonged insanity is treated like sleep: the person must make up missed prayers and fasts because there is no hardship. However, this applies to temporary insanity (ʿāriḍī), where a sane adult becomes insane. For original insanity (aṣlī), where one reaches puberty already insane, there is a dispute: Abū Yūsuf considers it like childhood—no obligation to make up missed worship if recovery occurs before the period (month for fasting, day and night for prayer). Muḥammad treats it like temporary insanity—make-up is required. Some narrations reverse their positions.

Finally, the boundary of extension (ḥadd al-imtidād) is defined: in prayer, if insanity exceeds a day and a night, it is prolonged, so make-up is obligatory (due to hardship of many prayers). This rule is generalized to other acts of worship.

Key Terms
العارضي (al-ʿāriḍī): Temporary insanity occurring after puberty in a sane person.
الأصلي (al-aṣlī): Original insanity present from before puberty (i.e., reaching puberty insane).
الامتداد (al-imtidād): Prolongation of insanity beyond a defined limit (e.g., more than a day and night for prayer).
القضاء (al-qaḍāʾ): Making up missed acts of worship after the excuse is removed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a person who experiences temporary insanity (ʿāriḍī) that lasts for 10 hours?
A) No make-up required because insanity removes capacity.
B) Make-up required because it did not exceed a day and night.
C) Make-up is required only if it exceeds a day and night.
D) No make-up because temporary insanity is like sleep.

Key Takeaway
Non-prolonged temporary insanity requires make-up of missed worship; original insanity involves a valid intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Legal Capacity of the Idiot (Ma'tuh) in Hanafi Usul
Defines 'atih and its legal effects on capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-‘atah and apply its legal effects on capacity, distinguishing between valid and invalid acts for the 'atih.

Core Idea
The 'atih has partial capacity: valid in benefit but lacks ‘uhdah for harmful transactions.

In Hanafi usul, legal capacity is tied to intellect. The 'atih (idiot) represents a middle state between the sane adult and the minor or madman. This passage defines his status, clarifies which acts are valid without guardian and which require supervision, and addresses an important dispute on whether acts of worship are obligatory upon him.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defining characteristics of al-‘atah
Find how the passage defines ‘atah: mixed rational and irrational speech/actions, presence of basic intellect with a defect.
This sets the foundation for all subsequent rulings.
2
Distinguish acts based on ‘uhdah requirement
Note that the ‘atih lacks ‘uhdah (liability capacity). Acts that are purely beneficial (e.g., worship, accepting gifts) are valid. Acts that involve potential harm (e.g., sale, purchase, divorce) require guardian permission or are invalid.
‘Uhdah is key: it imposes commitment and penalty.
3
Analyze the objection about consumption liability
Understand why the ‘atih is still liable for consuming property (daman) – it is compensatory, not contractual. The passage distinguishes between ‘uhdah and jabr (compensation).
This clarifies that ‘atih is not completely exempt from all liability.
4
Evaluate the dispute on obligation of worship
Compare the two views: later Hanafis say worship not obligatory (address removed like minor), while Qadi Imam Abu Zaid says it is obligatory (because ‘atih is adult, ‘atah is like illness). Identify the mufta bihi.
The practical consequence: is qada required if missed?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان العته بعد البلوغ
مختلط الكلام يشبه بعض كلامه بكلام العقلاء وبعضه بكلام المجانين، فهو أيضا كالصبا وكذا مختلط الأفعال في وجود أصل العقل وتمكن الخلل على ما قال، وهو كالصبا مع العقل في كل الأحكام حتى لا يمنع صحة القول والفعل فيصح عباداته، وإسلامه، وأو ببيع مال غيره، وإعتاق عبده، ويصح منه قبول الهبة كما يصح من الصبي، لكنه يمنع العهدة، فلا يصح طلاق أي عبد غيره امرأته، ولا إعتاق عبده أصلاً ولا بيعه ولا شراؤه بدون إذن الولي، ولا يُطالب في أي المبيع الوكالة بتسليم المبيع، ولا يردّ عليه بالعيب، ولا يؤمر بالخصومة. ثم أورد عليه أنه إذا كان أن لا يؤاخذ المعتوه بضمان ما استهلكه من الأموال؟ فأجاب عنه بقوله: أي بالبيع كذلك فينبغي وأما ضمان ما استهلكه من الأموال فليس بعهدة، وكونه صبيا، أو عبداً، أو معتوها لا ينافي أي بالغا معتوها عصمة المحل، يعني المعصوم، وعصمته لم تزل من أجل كون المستهلك صبيًا أو معتوها بخلاف حقوق الله، أن ضمان المال ليس بطريق العهدة، بل بطريق جبر ما فوته من المال أي المعتوه أي جزاء الأفعال كالزنا فإن ضمانها إنما يجب جزاءً للأفعال دون المحال، وهو موقوف على كمال العقل. ويوضع عنه الخطاب كالصبي حتى لا تجب عليه العبادات، ولا تثبت في حقه العقوبات، المعتوه أي وجوب أداء في كل الأحكام أي في عدم التكليف في جميع الأحكام وصحة الأداء. (القمر) يمنع العهدة: أي ما يوجب إلزام شيء ومضرته، فإن ذمته ليست صالحة للجزاء والتكليف (القمر) أصلاً أي لا بإذن الولي ولا بدونه. (القمر) ولا بيعه ولا شراؤه إلخ وما في مسير[؟] الدائر: ولا يصح إعتاق عبد نفسه بإذن الولي وبدونه شراؤه بإذنه؛ لأن كل ذلك من المضار والعته يمنعها، انتهى، فعجيب فإن بيعه وشراءه يصح بإذن الولي كما يصح بإذن الولي في الصبي. Statement of idiocy after puberty: mixed speech, some of his words resemble the speech of sane people and some resemble the speech of madmen, so he is also like a minor. Similarly for mixed actions. In the presence of basic intellect but with a defect, as stated, he is like a minor with intellect in all rulings such that it does not prevent the validity of speech and action. So his acts of worship, his acceptance of Islam, or selling another's property, and manumitting his slave are valid, and acceptance of a gift is valid from him as it is valid from a minor. But it prevents liability (ʿuhdah), so divorce of another's wife, manumission of his slave at all, and sale or purchase without guardian's permission are not valid. He is not pursued for delivery of the sold item, nor is he liable for defect, nor ordered for litigation. Then it was objected: if so, should not the idiot be held liable for damages of what he consumed? He answered: likewise, it should be. But the liability for what he consumed of wealth is not (based on) ʿuhdah, and his being a minor, slave, or idiot does not negate the inviolability of the property, i.e., the protected property, and its inviolability has not ceased because the consumer is a minor or idiot, unlike rights of Allah. That liability for wealth is not by way of ʿuhdah, but by way of compensation for what he lost of wealth, i.e., the idiot, i.e., as penalty for actions like adultery, for its liability is only obligatory as penalty for actions regardless of the property, and it depends on complete intellect. And address is removed from him like a minor so that acts of worship are not obligatory upon him, nor penalties established against him. The idiot means obligation of performance in all rulings, i.e., in absence of taklif in all rulings and validity of performance. (Al-Qamar): 'prevents ʿuhdah' means what necessitates imposition of something and its harm, for his dhimma is not suitable for penalty and obligation. (Al-Qamar): 'at all' means not with guardian's permission nor without. (Al-Qamar): 'nor his sale nor his purchase etc.' and what is in Maseer[?] ad-Da'ir: 'and the manumission of his own slave with guardian's permission and his purchase without it are not valid, because all that is harmful and idiocy prevents it.' End. This is strange, for his sale and purchase are valid with guardian's permission as it is valid with guardian's permission in the case of a minor. (Al-Qamar): 'if so' i.e., idiocy prevents ʿuhdah, so the idiot should not be held liable etc., because this liability is from ʿuhdah. (Al-Qamar): 'the property' i.e., the wealth he consumed, because its inviolability is established due to the need of the slave, for the maintenance of his interests depends on it. (Al-Qamar): 'not by way of ʿuhdah' because it is not a penalty for the act. (Al-Qamar): 'of the wealth etc.' explanation of what in 'what he lost'. (Al-Qamar): 'not obligatory' and in Tahrir at-Taqrir quoting at-Taqwim: 'Acts of worship are obligatory upon him as a precaution' [the annotator] and 'not established etc.' I said: this is what the later scholars held. Al-Qadi Imam Abu Zaid said: 'Acts of worship are not dropped from him because the address to him is valid due to his being adult, and idiocy is like illness, unlike a minor because address is removed from him.' Sharh Husami. (Al-Sunbuli). And a guardian is appointed over him as a guardian is appointed over a minor, out of consideration and compassion for him. For he is deficient in intellect and he does not have guardianship over others, in marriage, discipline, and preserving the wealth of orphans, just as a minor is like that. 'And a guardian is appointed over him' means guardianship over the idiot is established for another. (Al-Qamar): 'and he does not have guardianship over others' because he has no guardianship over himself, so how over others?
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage defines the legal status of the 'atih (idiot or feeble-minded person) after puberty within Hanafi fiqh. The 'atih is one whose speech and actions are sometimes rational and sometimes irrational, akin to a madman but lacking full madness. The author explains that the 'atih is treated like a minor (sabi) in many rulings: his acts of worship (prayer, fasting, etc.) are valid if performed, and he can accept gifts. However, he lacks full liability capacity (ʿuhdah)—meaning his dhimma is not fully capable of bearing obligations that involve harm or penalty. Therefore, he cannot validly perform acts that harm himself or others, such as divorcing another's wife, manumitting a slave, or selling/purchasing property without guardian permission. The author then addresses an objection: if the 'atih lacks ʿuhdah, why is he liable for damages when he consumes or destroys someone's property? The answer distinguishes between contractual liability (ʿuhdah) and compensatory liability (daman). The latter is not based on ʿuhdah but on the principle of making good loss (jabr), which applies even to minors and idiots because it is a form of penalty for the act (jaza' al-af'al). However, this penalty depends on complete intellect, so it is not applied to the 'atih for crimes like theft or fornication? Actually the text says that for acts like zina, the penalty is only imposed on those with full intellect. So the 'atih is exempt from criminal penalties and even from obligations of worship according to the author's position (later Hanafis). There is a dispute: some scholars say that 'atih is obligated to worship because he is an adult, and his condition is like illness. The author sides with later scholars that the 'atih is not obligated. Finally, a guardian is appointed over the 'atih to protect his interests, and he cannot be a guardian over others.

Key Terms
العته (al-‘atah): A state after puberty where the person has mixed rational and irrational speech/actions, indicating a defect in intellect but not complete loss.
العهدة (al-‘uhdah): Liability or responsibility that imposes commitment and penalty, specifically related to the capacity of the dhimma to bear obligations and penalties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason that the 'atih is not held liable for consumption of someone's property under the category of 'uhdah?
A) Because the 'atih has no intellect at all
B) Because liability for consumption is based on jabr (compensation), not 'uhdah, and 'atih is still responsible for such acts
C) Because the 'atih is like a madman and completely exempt from all liability
D) Because the guardian must compensate for the 'atih's consumption

Key Takeaway
The 'atih has partial legal capacity: valid in beneficial acts but requires guardian for harmful transactions due to lack of 'uhdah.

The Definition of Forgetfulness (al-Nisyān) in Hanafi Legal Theory
Definition of forgetfulness and its distinction from similar states

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define forgetfulness (al-nisyān) as a legal concept and distinguish it from madness, sleep, and unconsciousness.

Core Idea
Forgetfulness is essential ignorance of what was known, not due to an affliction, and does not remove obligation.

Before we can understand when the law excuses forgetfulness, we must first define it precisely. The Hanafi jurists distinguish forgetfulness from other states that prevent knowledge, such as madness and sleep. This lesson unpacks the definition found in Noor al-Anwaar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Read the first sentence: 'النسيان عطف على ما قبله وهو جهل ضروري بما كان يعلمه، لا بآفة مع علمه بأمور كثيرة' – forgetfulness is a necessary ignorance of what one knew, not due to an affliction, while one knows many other things.
2
Exclude madness
The phrase 'لا بآفة' excludes madness, where ignorance is due to a mental affliction. Madness removes legal responsibility entirely, unlike forgetfulness.
Madness (junun) is a separate category.
3
Exclude sleep and unconsciousness
The condition 'مع علمه بأمور كثيرة' excludes sleep and fainting, where one is not aware of anything. This reinforces that forgetfulness presupposes some awareness of other matters.
Sleeping person is not mukallaf.
4
Determine the legal effect
The text asserts 'وهو لا ينافي الوجوب في حق الله تعالى' – forgetfulness does not negate obligation in rights of Allah. Therefore, if one forgets a prayer or fast, the obligation to perform it remains and qada is required.
This is the default rule; exception comes later.

Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage defines nishyan (forgetfulness) as a type of ignorance that arises after knowledge, not due to a pathological affliction like madness, and distinguishes it from sleep and unconsciousness (where one is not aware). The key principle: forgetfulness generally does not remove the obligation to perform or make up acts of worship (like prayer and fasting) because the duty was established when one knew. However, when forgetfulness is prevalent (ghalib)—i.e., it commonly occurs in a particular act due to human nature or circumstantial pressures—then the law provides leniency. Three examples are given: (1) Eating/drinking forgetfully during fasting: the fast is not invalidated because the soul naturally craves; (2) Omitting tasmiyah (saying 'Bismillah') when slaughtering an animal: the meat remains halal because the fear and awe of slaughter cause forgetting; (3) A forgetful person saying the taslim (greeting of peace) after only two rak'ahs: the prayer is not nullified; one adds two rak'ahs and performs sajda sahw. The qualification 'prevalent' excludes cases where forgetfulness is rare or not typical, such as speaking or greeting in non-sitting positions during prayer—these are not excused. The commentator (Al-Qamar) adds that forgetfulness in the state of ihram (for a pilgrim) while hunting is not excused because ihram is a constant reminder.

Key Terms
النسيان (al-nisyān): Essential ignorance of something one previously knew, occurring at the time of need, without a pathological cause.
غالب (ghālib): Prevalent or common occurrence of forgetfulness in a particular act, due to natural disposition or circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT excluded from the definition of forgetfulness?
A) madness
B) sleep
C) unconsciousness
D) obsession (waswas)

Key Takeaway
Forgetfulness is a necessary ignorance after knowledge, not arising from an affliction, and it does not remove the duty to perform or make up obligatory acts.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Prevalent Forgetfulness (Ghalib) and Its Legal Exceptions
Explanation of when forgetfulness is excused due to prevalence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that forgetfulness is excused only when it is prevalent (ghalib) and identify the three exemplar cases.

Core Idea
Prevalent forgetfulness excuses the act; rare forgetfulness does not.

While forgetfulness generally requires qada, Islamic law recognizes that some acts are prone to forgetfulness due to human nature. The Hanafi school applies a principle: if forgetfulness is prevalent (ghalib) in a particular act, the law provides leniency. This lesson examines three classic examples and the qualification that limits the excuse.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of ghalib
The text says: 'لكنه إذا كان غالبًا يكون عفواً' – if it is prevalent, it becomes excused. This is the exception to the default rule that forgetfulness does not drop obligation.
Ghalib here means the act is such that forgetfulness is common due to natural or circumstantial factors.
2
Examine the first example: fasting
In fasting, the soul naturally desires food and drink, so forgetfulness is prevalent. If one eats or drinks forgetfully, the fast is not invalidated. The text says 'فَيُعْفَى ولا يفسد صومه به'.
This is a clear concession; no qada required.
3
Examine the second example: slaughtering
When slaughtering an animal, the fear and awe cause the heart to be occupied, leading to forgetfulness in saying tasmiyah. The Hanafi school excuses this, so the meat remains halal.
Other schools may require tasmiyah intentionally; Hanafi says tasmiyah is sunnah, but if forgotten due to ghalabah, it is excused.
4
Examine the third example: greeting in prayer
In the first sitting (al-qa'dah al-ula), it is easy to confuse it with the final sitting because there is no distinguishing sign. So forgetting and saying taslim after two rak'ahs is excused; one adds two rak'ahs and does sajda sahw.
The excuse applies only if one does not speak; if one speaks, it invalidates.
5
Note the qualification
The text adds: 'وإنما قيد بقوله: "إذا كان غالبًا ليخرج السلام والكلام في الصلاة ناسيا' – the condition of ghalib excludes cases where forgetfulness is not prevalent, such as greeting in non-sitting positions or speaking during prayer. Those are not excused because forgetfulness does not prevail there.
So the exception is narrow; it does not cover all forgetfulness.

D) eating forgetfully while fasting

Key Takeaway
Forgetfulness is excused only when it is prevalent (ghalib) due to natural causes; otherwise, the default rule of responsibility applies.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Legal Definition of Slavery (Raqq)
Defines slavery as legal incapacity and explains its origin and indivisibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the legal definition of slavery in Hanafi usul and explain its origin, indivisibility, and legal effects.

Core Idea
Slavery is a legal incapacity, a right of Allah, indivisible, and originally a penalty for disbelief.

This passage from Noor al-Anwaar provides a classic Hanafi definition of slavery (al-raqq) as a legal status. Understanding this definition is crucial because it forms the basis for many rulings regarding slaves' capacity to own property, testify, and perform legal acts. We will break down the definition's components and explore why slavery is considered indivisible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition's core statement
Locate the phrase that defines slavery. It begins with 'وهو عاجز لا يقدر على التصرفات' (he is incapable, unable to perform legal acts). This is the essential legal description.
Note that the definition focuses on legal incapacity, not physical strength.
2
Analyze the origin (sabab) of slavery
The text states that slavery is originally a penalty (جزاء) for disbelief (الكفر). Understand that this is the initial cause; after establishment, it persists even if the slave converts to Islam.
Analogous to kharaj tax on land: initially imposed on non-Muslims but remains if purchased by a Muslim.
3
Examine the indivisibility (عدم التجزؤ) of slavery
Slavery is described as indivisible because it is a right of Allah. This means a person cannot be partially enslaved. Contrast with ownership (الملك), which can be divided (e.g., selling a slave to two persons).
Example from text: selling half a slave is invalid, but selling a whole slave to two buyers is valid by consensus.
4
List the legal effects (athar) of slavery
From the passage, derive the consequences: the slave cannot perform legal acts, own property, give testimony, and is himself owned like other property.
These effects flow from the legal incapacity.
5
Apply the definition to a hypothetical case
Using the indivisibility principle, consider: if an imam conquers a town and sees maslaha in enslaving half the inhabitants, it is not allowed because slavery cannot be partial.
This shows the practical implication of the definition in governance.

And he is incapable, unable to perform legal acts, even if physically stronger and more robust than a free person. It means legally enslaved as a penalty for disbelief, because the disbelievers disdained the worship of Allah, so Allah made them slaves of His slaves. This is in origin, meaning its initial establishment; for slavery is not imposed initially except on disbelievers, then after that even if he embraces Islam, it remains on him and his children, and he is not freed from it unless emancipated, like kharaj which is initially established only on the disbeliever, then after that if a Muslim purchases kharaj land, the kharaj remains as it is and does not change. And to this he alluded with his saying: but in its continuation it became a legal matter, i.e., in its continuation it became a ruling from the rulings of sharia without regard to the meaning of penalty; by it a person becomes subject to being owned, i.e., penalty for disbelief and degradation, i.e., due to this slavery the slave becomes a locus, because he is owned and degraded. And 'arada originally is the butcher's cloth with which he wipes the grease from his hand. And it is a description that is not divisible in establishment and removal, because it is a right of Allah; thus it is not valid to describe the slave as being enslaved in some parts and not others, unlike the ownership attached to him, for it is the slave's right and can be described as divisible. For a man may sell his slave to two persons by consensus, but if he sells half of the slave, he is unable, does not own property, his testimony is not accepted; rather he is owned by others like other property. (al-Sanbali) So Allah made them etc.: And they were likened to beasts in being owned, degraded, and disdainful. (al-Qamar) And this means that slavery is a penalty for disbelief. (al-Qamar) If a Muslim purchases: i.e., from a dhimmi kharaj land, the kharaj remains, i.e., on the Muslim. (al-Qamar) It is not divisible etc. Its analogy is washing the limbs of wudu, for it is divisible; even if one washes his hands and face, the event of impurity is removed from them and purity is established, but the permissibility of prayer, which is indivisible, is not established without washing all limbs. (al-Sanbali) In establishment: if the imam conquers a town and sees maslaha in enslaving half of the people of the town as common, it is not executable from him, for slavery is the effect of disbelief and it is indivisible, so slavery is also indivisible. (al-Qamar) So it is not valid because it is impossible that some part is accepted for testimony and some part not. (al-Qamar) It is permissible by consensus: and ownership is established for each of them in half. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage defines slavery (al-raqq) as a legal incapacity (ajz hukmi) that prevents the slave from performing legal acts, owning property, giving testimony, etc. The root cause of slavery is disbelief (kufr); it was originally imposed as a penalty on disbelievers who rejected the worship of Allah. Even if a slave later accepts Islam, the status of slavery remains on him and his offspring unless emancipated. The author uses an analogy: just as kharaj (land tax) is initially imposed on non-Muslims but remains even if the land is bought by a Muslim, so slavery persists even after conversion. In its continuation, slavery becomes a pure legal ruling without reference to its penal origin. A key characteristic of slavery is its indivisibility (la yatajazza). It is a right of Allah, so a slave cannot be partially enslaved; he is either fully enslaved or free. In contrast, ownership (like selling a slave in halves) is divisible because it is a human right. The text gives examples: selling a slave to two persons is valid for half each, but selling half a slave is invalid because slavery itself is indivisible. Thus, a slave cannot be partially capable of testimony or ownership.

Key Terms
الرق (al-raqq): Slavery; a legal incapacity that is a penalty for disbelief, indivisible in nature.
الجزاء (al-jazā): Penalty; slavery is a punishment for disbelief in the original establishment.
التجزؤ (al-tajazzu): Divisibility; slavery is indivisible (la yatajazza), unlike ownership which can be divided.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition in this passage, why is slavery indivisible?
A) Because it is based on physical strength.
B) Because it is a right of Allah.
C) Because it is a temporary status.
D) Because it is a type of ownership.

Key Takeaway
Slavery is a legal incapacity, a right of Allah that is indivisible and originally a penalty for disbelief, with lasting effects even after conversion until emancipation.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
The Indivisibility of Slavery and Manumission: A Usul al-Fiqh Analysis
Explaining the indivisible nature of slavery and manumission with logical proofs and internal Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why slavery and freedom are indivisible legal qualities in Hanafi usul and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two companions on the divisibility of the act of manumission.

Core Idea
Slavery and freedom are indivisible legal states (rights of Allah), whereas ownership is divisible.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar dissects the legal nature of slavery and manumission, revealing a foundational usul principle: certain legal qualities cannot be partially established or removed. The text contrasts slavery (a right of Allah) with ownership (a right of the slave), and then presents a key internal dispute over whether the act of manumission is divisible. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying rulings related to slaves and freed persons in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal nature of slavery
The text states slavery is a description (وصف) that does not admit division in establishment or removal because it is a right of Allah. Understand that this means a slave cannot be partially enslaved.
This indivisibility is a key usul principle: certain legal qualities are unified by their divine origin.
2
Contrast slavery with ownership
Ownership is a right of the slave and is divisible, as demonstrated by the permissibility of selling a slave to two buyers. Note that ownership is more general than slavery.
Ownership can be partial because it is a personal right, unlike slavery which is a divine right.
3
Analyze the definition of manumission
Manumission (عتق) is defined as a legal strength (قوة حكمية) that qualifies a person for ownership and authority. According to the two companions, it is also indivisible because it establishes freedom, which is indivisible.
Freedom is the opposite of slavery and shares its indivisible nature.
4
Follow the logical proof for indivisibility of manumission
The two companions argue using a logical syllogism: if manumission were divisible, three absurdities would follow (effect without cause, cause without effect, or division of freedom). Therefore, manumission must be indivisible.
This is a pure rational proof (dalil aqli) based on necessary connections.
5
Compare Abu Hanifa's alternative view and tarjih
Abu Hanifa argues that manumission is removal of ownership, which is divisible. Hence, freeing part of a slave does not free the whole but corrupts ownership in the remaining part. Recognize that the later school leans towards the two companions' view.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) differs: complete freedom vs. mukatab status.

(القمر)
Explanation of Legal Capacity. 177. Explanation of Sleep. And he is incapable, unable to perform transactions, even if according to sense he is stronger and more robust than a free person. That is, the enslaved legally is a punishment for disbelief; because the disbelievers were arrogant against worshipping Allah Almighty, so Allah Almighty made them slaves of His slaves. And this is in origin, meaning the origin of its placement and beginning; because slavery is not applied initially except to disbelievers, then after that even if he becomes Muslim, it remains upon him and his children, and does not separate from him until he is freed, like the kharaj is not established initially except upon the disbeliever, then after that if a Muslim buys kharaj land, the kharaj remains as it is and does not change. And to this he pointed with his saying: 'But in continuance it became from the legal matters', meaning it became in continuance a ruling from the rulings of the Sharia without considering in it the meaning of punishment. By it a person becomes subject to ownership, meaning punishment for disbelief and debasement. That is, because of this slavery the slave becomes a locus for being owned and debased. And 'al-‘urḍa' in origin is the butcher's cloth with which he wipes the grease of his hand. And it is a description that is not divisible in establishment and removal; because it is a right of Allah Almighty, so it is not valid that the slave be described as being 'enslaved in some parts and not others', contrary to the ownership attached to him, for it is a right of the slave and is described as divisible. [Interpretation for 'for slavery'] in removal and establishment; because if a man sells his slave to two persons, it is permissible by consensus, and if he sells half of the slave, he is incapable, does not own property, his testimony is not accepted, rather he is owned by others like other property. (al-Qamar) 'Worship of Allah' etc.: Rather they took them besides Him, and did not reflect on the signs of tawhid, and joined themselves to beasts and inanimate objects in that, so Allah Almighty recompensed them in this world by making them slaves of His slaves, owned and debased; and for this reason slavery is not established upon a Muslim initially. (al-Sanabli) 'So Allah made them' etc.: And they were joined to beasts in being owned and debased and arrogance. (al-Qamar) And this, meaning that slavery is a punishment for disbelief. (al-Qamar) 'If a Muslim buys': meaning from a dhimmi kharaj land, the kharaj remains, meaning upon the Muslim. (al-Qamar) 'It is not divisible' etc. And its analogy is washing the limbs of wudu, for it is divisible to the extent that if one washes his hands and face, the hadath is removed from them and purification is established, but the permissibility of prayer, which is not divisible, is not established without washing all limbs. (al-Sanabli) 'In establishment': For if the Imam conquers a town and sees the maslaha in enslaving half of the people of the town as a share, that does not become effective from him, because slavery is the effect of disbelief and it is not divisible, so slavery is also not divisible. (al-Qamar) 'So it is not valid' because it is impossible that some be accepted in testimony and some not accepted. (al-Qamar) 'Permissible by consensus': And ownership is established for each of them in the half. (al-Qamar) Explanation of Legal Capacity. 167. Explanation of Sleep. Ownership remains for him in the other half by consensus, and it is more general than slavery; since it can be described for other than humans like commodities without slavery, like manumission which is its opposite, for it also does not admit division, and it is [interpretation: i.e., being owned] [interpretation: i.e., slavery] a legal strength by which a person becomes qualified for ownership and authority of testimony and judgeship and the like. It becomes. And likewise the act of manumission according to them, i.e., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, in its carrying is also not divisible; because the act of manumission is the establishment of freedom; so freedom is its effect. For if the act of manumission were divisible and he frees some, then either freedom is established in all, necessitating the effect without the cause, or freedom is not established in anything, necessitating the cause without the effect, or freedom is established in some, necessitating division of freedom. And this is the meaning of his statement: 'Lest there occur the effect without the cause, or the cause without the effect, or division of freedom.' And in some manuscripts his statement 'or division of freedom' is not found, and its editing is not free from artifice. And Abu Hanifa said in his comment: It is removal of ownership, and it is divisible. [i.e., artifice] It does not admit division etc. because it is a strength, etc., and the establishment of such strength cannot be conceived in some common part without another. Just as they agreed on the non-division of freedom and slavery, they agreed on the division of ownership. (al-Sanabli) 'And it is a legal strength': i.e., by the ruling of the Legislator, and slavery is a legal weakness, so freedom and slavery become opposites due to the opposition between strength and weakness. And this strength is not divisible, for its establishment cannot be conceived in some common part without another. (al-Qamar) 'Also', i.e., like freedom it is not divisible. Since the act of manumission is not divisible, by manumitting some, the whole becomes free according to them. (al-Qamar) 'It is not divisible' meaning that manumitting some is manumitting the whole. 'For if it were' etc. Its summary: that if the act of manumission were divisible, such that he freed some, e.g., half of his slave, and freedom were not divisible, rather freedom is established in the whole, then the existence of the effect, i.e., freedom, would occur without the cause, i.e., the act of manumission, due to the lack of manumission of the whole on the assumption of manumission of some. And if the act of manumission were divisible and freedom were not established in anything, then the existence of the cause, i.e., the act of manumission, would occur without the effect. And if the act of manumission were divisible and freedom were also divisible, then division of freedom would occur, which is invalid by agreement. And what is in 'Maseer al-Da'ir' that the effect occurs without the cause if freedom is divided without the act of manumission, and the cause occurs without the effect if the act of manumission is divided without freedom — this I do not understand. (al-Qamar) 'Lest the effect occur', and the necessary consequence is invalid because disjunction between cause and effect is not permissible given the necessary connection between them. (al-Qamar) 'And in some manuscripts' etc., and Bahr al-Ulum chose this manuscript. (al-Qamar) 'And its editing', i.e., the formulation of the speech according to some manuscripts is not complete, for the proof is not complete without his statement 'or division of freedom', but Bahr al-Ulum established it. (al-Sanabli) 'And it is' i.e., ownership is divisible, so its removal is also divisible. Thus if he frees some, the whole does not become free; rather ownership in the remainder becomes corrupt and he becomes like a mukatab. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Noor al-Anwar addresses the legal nature of slavery (رق) and manumission (عتق) within the Hanafi school. The author first establishes that slavery is a divinely ordained punishment for disbelief, initially applied only to non-Muslims. Once established, it persists even after conversion to Islam, similar to kharaj tax on land. The key ruling is that slavery is an indivisible quality (وصف لا يتجزأ) — a slave cannot be partially enslaved; the entire person is either enslaved or free. This is argued as a right of Allah (حق الله تعالى). In contrast, ownership (ملك) is a right of the slave (حق العبد) and can be divided, as seen in the permissibility of selling a slave to two buyers by consensus. The indivisibility of slavery is supported by analogies: just as ablution (wudu) has divisible effects (removal of hadath from individual limbs) but the permissibility of prayer is indivisible and requires complete washing, so too slavery's legal effects (e.g., incapacity, inadmissibility of testimony) cannot be partial. The commentator al-Sanabli notes that if an Imam conquers a town, he cannot enslave half the inhabitants as a common share, because slavery is an indivisible effect of disbelief. The passage then moves to manumission (عتق), defining it as a legal strength (قوة حكمية) that qualifies a person for ownership and authority. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions), the act of manumission (إعتاق) is also indivisible because it establishes freedom (عتق), which is indivisible. Their argument is logical if manumission were divisible, three impossible consequences would follow: (1) freeing part would free the whole, causing the effect (freedom) without the cause (manumission of the whole); (2) freeing part would free nothing, causing the cause without effect; or (3) freedom itself would be divisible, which is invalid. Therefore, by manumitting part of a slave, the entire slave becomes free. Abu Hanifa (Imam) holds a different view: manumission is simply the removal of ownership (إزالة الملك), which is divisible because ownership itself is divisible. Thus, if one frees part of a slave, the whole does not become free; instead, ownership in the remaining part becomes corrupted (فسد الملك) and the slave becomes like a mukatab (a slave contracted for emancipation). The two companions' view is presented as the stronger argument, though the text acknowledges that some manuscripts omit the phrase 'or division of freedom' in the proof, and Bahr al-Ulum preferred that version. The main takeaway is that both slavery and freedom are indivisible legal states, while ownership is divisible — a distinction with practical implications in sale, manumission, and legal capacity.

Key Terms
الرق (al-riqq): A legal quality (وصف) that is indivisible, imposed as punishment for disbelief, making the person owned and debased, and removing full legal capacity.
العتق (al-‘itq): A legal strength (قوة حكمية) opposite to slavery, qualifying a person for ownership and authority; it is indivisible because it is a right of Allah.
الملك (al-milk): Ownership, a right of the slave (in the context of being owned) that is divisible; it is more general than slavery as it can apply to non-humans.
الأهلية (al-ahliyya): Legal capacity, the quality by which a person becomes qualified for rights and obligations; slavery diminishes it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the logical consequence if the act of manumission (إعتاق) were divisible?
A) The slave would become completely free, which is desirable.
B) It would lead to one of three impossibilities: effect without cause, cause without effect, or division of freedom.
C) The slave would be considered a mukatab automatically.
D) Ownership would be removed in parts without affecting freedom.

Key Takeaway
Slavery and freedom are indivisible legal states because they are rights of Allah, whereas ownership is divisible; this distinction has direct practical implications for rulings on manumission and legal capacity.

Slavery and Ownership: The Contradiction of Power and Incapacity
Rational justification of the ruling that a slave cannot own property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi legal definition of riqq, identify why it contradicts milkiyyah using the concepts of power and incapacity, and evaluate the role of consensus in establishing this ruling.

Core Idea
Slavery (riqq) and ownership (milkiyyah) are opposites: one implies power, the other incapacity; they cannot coexist in the same person.

This passage delves into a fundamental Hanafi usul principle: the inherent contradiction between being owned (mamlukiyyah) and owning property (milkiyyah). The author argues that a slave cannot own property because ownership requires legal power, whereas slavery imposes legal weakness. We will explore the rational argument, examine objections, and see how later scholars ultimately relied on consensus (ijma') to settle the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Key Terms
Locate the terms riqq (slavery), milk/milkiyyah (ownership), and mamlukiyyah (state of being owned) in the Arabic text. Understand their legal definitions.
Riqq is defined as a legal weakness (za'f hukmi).
2
Understand the Contradiction
The author asserts that riqq contradicts milkiyyah because ownership is a mark of power (qudrah) while being owned is a mark of incapacity ('ajz). These are opposites and cannot coexist in the same person from the same perspective.
The contradiction is ontological, not merely practical.
3
Examine the Objection
Some scholars raised the objection that the two could coexist from different respects: the slave is owned as property but could own as a human. Identify this objection in the text.
The objection is found in the phrase 'فيه بحث'.
4
Evaluate the Responses
The passage presents several responses: the argument that it would lead to property owning property (absurd), and the alternative of relying on consensus (ijma'). Trace the reasoning and note the preference for ijma'.
The author of al-Tahqiq states that the rational proof is incomplete.
5
Recognize the Application: Tasarri
The passage applies the principle: slaves and mukatabs cannot practice tasarri (taking a concubine) because that requires full ownership rights.
Tasarri is a right that only a full owner can exercise.

And some, i.e., our master Khadim Ahmad, gave an answer to him that if one were to say his ownership is due to his humanity, it would follow that property is an owner of property, which is not permissible because an owner is one who disposes of property, and property is disposed of, and it is not permissible for the disposed of to be a disposer in a single state, unlike ownership of what is not property, because necessity calls for its establishment, as in the commentaries of al-Husami. So reflect. (al-Sanbali) From the aspect of humanity, etc. Its analogue: the mukatab is free and owned from two aspects: he is owned in terms of the neck and free in terms of the hand. (al-Qamar) Even so, the slave does not own: the slave and the mukatab, because their necks remain (owned), but in the former both hand and neck, in the latter only neck. Tasarri means taking a female slave for intercourse and coitus, for that is among the rights of ownership, and these two are not fit for ownership. (al-Qamar)

Commentary
This passage explains a fundamental Hanafi legal principle: a slave cannot own property because ownership (milkiyyah) and being owned (mamlukiyyah) are contradictory. The author defines riqq (slavery) as a legal weakness (za‘f hukmi) that prevents the slave from having full legal capacity (ahliyyah) to own property. The argument is that ownership implies power (qudrah) to dispose, while being owned implies subjection to another's power ('ajz). These two cannot coexist in the same person from the same perspective. An objection is raised that they could coexist from different angles (as property vs. as human). The response clarifies that if a slave were considered owner due to humanity, it would imply that property (the slave himself) is an owner of property, which is incoherent because property is the object of ownership, not the subject. The commentator favors relying on consensus (ijma‘) for this ruling, as the rational proof has difficulties. The passage also discusses the application: a slave or mukatab cannot practice tasarri (taking a concubine) because that requires full ownership rights.

Key Terms
رق (riqq): Slavery; a legal condition of subjugation to a master, defined as a legal weakness (za‘f hukmi).
ملك (milk): Ownership; a legal power to dispose of property.
مملوكية (mamlukiyyah): The state of being owned; a symbol of incapacity.
تسرّي (tasarrī): Taking a female slave as a concubine (sirriya) for sexual relations.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
